Revocation of a Will by Word and Deed; Denial is Not Revocation
Rulings on how a testator may revoke a will, and that mere denial is not revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the methods by which a testator may revoke a will according to the Hanafi school, and explain why mere denial does not constitute revocation.

Core Idea
A will can be revoked by word or deed before acceptance; denial of the will is not revocation.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rules on revoking a will (رجوع). The testator may revoke his will before the legatee's acceptance, either by explicit words or by actions inconsistent with the will. Additionally, we explore an important distinction: simply denying that one made a will does not count as revocation. This nuanced ruling reflects the Hanafi school's precision in legal causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of revocation
The testator has the right to revoke a will before acceptance by the legatee (which occurs after death). This is like other contracts where revocation is allowed before acceptance.
2
Distinguish between revocation by word and by deed
Revocation can be explicit (saying 'I revoke my will') or implicit through actions inconsistent with the will, such as selling, gifting, or destroying the bequeathed item.
Actions that remove the item from ownership indicate the testator no longer intends to honor the will.
3
Understand the special case of generic bequest
If the will is for a share like one-third of property, revocation can only be by explicit words, not by deed, because there is no specific item to dispose of.
4
Analyze the tadbir distinction
For conditional tadbir (e.g., 'if I die of this illness, you are free'), the testator cannot revoke by words but can revoke by selling the slave. For absolute tadbir, no revocation is possible at all, by word or deed.
This shows the nuance in Hanafi law regarding different types of deathbed declarations.
5
Examine the denial controversy
Denial (juhud) of having made a will is not considered revocation because it negates the existence of the will, whereas revocation presupposes its existence. Imam Muhammad held this view; Abu Yusuf differed.
The chosen (mufta bihi) position is Imam Muhammad's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله الرجوع عن الوصية قولا وفعلا بأن باع أو وهب أو قطع الثوب، أو ذبح الشاة، والجحود لا يكون رجوعا. وله الرجوع إلخ : أي للموصي الرجوع عن الوصية؛ لأن القبول بعد الموت فجاز الرجوع قبل القبول كسائر العقود، ثم الرجوع إما يكون قولا بأن قال: رجعت عن وصيتي به له، أو فعلا بأن باع الموصي أو وهب أو قطع الثوب أو ذبح الشاة. واعلم أن تصور الرجوع من حيث القول والفعل محله ما إذا كان الموصى به عينا، فقال: رجعت عن وصيتي، أو أخرج العين عن ملكه، فإن أوصى بثلث ماله لم يتصور الرجوع إلا بالقول، وقد يكون الرجوع بالفعل دون القول كما لو قال لعبده: إن مت من مرضي هذا فأنت حر فهو مدبر مقيد حتى لو قال: رجعت عن ذلك لا يصح، ولو باع العبد جاز بيعه وتبطل الوصية، بخلاف التدبير المطلق، حيث لا يتصور الرجوع عنه مطلقا لا قولا ولا فعلا. (ملا مسكين، فتح) والجحود إلخ : أي الإنكار بأن قال له :رجل هل أوصيت؟ فأنكر لا يكون رجوعا؛ لأن الجحود نفي الأصل، فلا يجامعه الرجوع؛ إذ الرجوع يستلزم الإثبات وبه كان يفتي محمد بحه، فلذلك اختاره الشيخ، وعند أبي يوسف: -
And he has the right to revoke the will by word and deed, such as selling, gifting, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. And denial (al-juhud) is not revocation. And he has the right to revoke: meaning the testator may revoke the will because acceptance occurs after death, so revocation is permitted before acceptance like other contracts. Then revocation is either by word, such as saying 'I revoke my will for him', or by deed, such as the testator selling, gifting, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. Know that the conceptualization of revocation by word or deed applies when the bequest is a specific item; he says 'I revoke my will' or removes the item from his ownership. If he bequeaths one-third of his property, revocation is only conceptualized by word. And there is a case where revocation is by deed without word, such as if he says to his slave: 'If I die from this illness of mine, you are free' – he is a suspended mudabbar (muqayyad). Even if he says 'I revoke that', it is not valid, but if he sells the slave, the sale is valid and the will is voided, unlike absolute tadbir where revocation is not conceptualized at all, neither by word nor by deed. (Mulla Miskin, Fath) And denial: meaning denial, such as if a man asks him 'Did you make a will?' and he denies it, that is not revocation because denial negates the original, so it cannot coexist with revocation, since revocation requires affirming the existence of the will. That was the fatwa of Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani), and therefore al-Shaykh (al-Hakim?) chose it. According to Abu Yusuf: … [the text breaks].
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage explains the modes of revoking a will (رجوع). A testator may revoke his will before the legatee's acceptance (which occurs after death). Revocation can be explicit (by saying 'I revoke my will') or implicit through actions inconsistent with the will, such as selling the bequeathed item, gifting it, or even destroying it (cutting the cloth, slaughtering the animal). These actions show that the testator no longer intends to honor the will. However, if the bequest is of a generic share like 'one-third of my property', revocation can only be by explicit words because such a share is not a specific item that can be physically disposed of. The passage also distinguishes between a conditional tadbir (e.g., 'if I die of this illness, you are free') and an absolute tadbir. For a conditional tadbir, the owner cannot revoke by words (saying 'I revoke') but can revoke by selling the slave, which voids the tadbir. For absolute tadbir, no revocation is possible at all. Finally, denial (جحود) of having made a will is not considered revocation. If asked 'Did you make a will?' and the testator says 'No', this does not count as revocation because denial negates the existence of the will, whereas revocation presupposes its existence. Imam Muhammad took this view and it is the chosen position; Abu Yusuf reportedly disagreed (that denial is revocation), but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation of a will by the testator before the legatee's acceptance; can be by word or deed.
جحود (juhud): Denial of having made a will; not considered revocation because it negates the existence of the will.
تدبير (tadbir): Declaration by a master that his slave will be free upon his death; absolute tadbir is irrevocable; conditional tadbir (mudabbar muqayyad) can be revoked by selling the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths a specific shirt to Zayd. Later, the testator sells the shirt to another person. What is the effect on the will?
A) The will remains valid because revocation must be by words.
B) The will is revoked because the sale is an act inconsistent with the will.
C) The will is valid only if the buyer knew of the will.
D) The will becomes a debt on the testator's estate.

Key Takeaway
A will can be revoked by words or inconsistent deeds before acceptance, but mere denial of its existence does not count as revocation.

Bequest to a Fetus: Conditions and Legal Reasoning
Ruling on bequest to/for a fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid bequest to a fetus and explain the Hanafi legal reasoning that distinguishes it from a gift.

Core Idea
Bequest to a fetus is valid because it resembles inheritance; a gift is not because acceptance is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on bequests involving a fetus—both when the fetus is the legatee (bequest to a fetus) and when the fetus itself is the subject (bequest of a fetus). The passage establishes validity under specific conditions and uses a dual analogy to gift and inheritance to justify the ruling. By the end, you will understand the conditions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the text discusses two distinct cases: (1) bequest where the legatee is a fetus (الوصية للحمل), and (2) bequest where the subject is a fetus (الوصية بالحمل). Both are valid under certain conditions.
The term 'for a fetus' and 'by a fetus' are technical.
2
Extract the conditions
The condition for validity is that the fetus is born alive within the shortest term of pregnancy, i.e., six months from the time of the will (or from death if the subject is the fetus).
Six months is the minimum duration of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand why a gift is invalid
The text explicitly states that a gift (hibah) to a fetus is not valid because acceptance is a condition, and a fetus cannot accept. Also, no guardian can take delivery on its behalf.
This highlights the importance of acceptance in gift contracts.
4
Trace the legal reasoning (qiyas)
The author argues that a bequest resembles both a gift (requiring acceptance) and inheritance (where acceptance is not required). Since a fetus cannot accept, the resemblance to inheritance prevails, making the bequest valid.
This is a classic example of ta'arud al-ashbah (conflict of similarities).
5
Apply the reasoning to the exception case
If someone bequeaths a slave-girl except her pregnancy, the exception is valid because the pregnancy is not included in the name 'slave-girl' literally, and it can be singled out in a bequest.
This shows consistency: what can be bequeathed independently can be excepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
أحكام الوصية
وتصح الوصية للحمل وبه إن ولدت لأقل مدته من وقت الوصية، ولا تصح الهبة بالحمل. وإن أوصى بأمة إلا حملها صحت الوصية والاستثناء وله الرجوع عن الوصية قولا وفعلا بأن باع أو وهب أو قطع الثوب، أو ذبح الشاة، والجحود لا يكون رجوعا. والثالث: مختلف فيه، وهو ما إذا قال: أوصيت بثلث مالي لفلان، ثم عتق، فالوصية باطلة عند أبي حنيفة خلافا لهما. وتصح الوصية للحمل لأنها استخلاف، والجنين يصلح خليفة في الإرث، فكذا في الوصية، لا يقال: شرطها القبول، أهله؛ لأنا نقول: الوصية تشبه الهبة وتشبه الميراث كما مر فلشبهها بالهبة يشترط القبول إذا أمكن، والجنين ليس من أهله، ولشبهها بالميراث يسقط إذا لم يمكن عملا بالشبهين، ولهذا يسقط بموت الموصى له قبل القبول. وبه تصح الوصية بالحمل بأن قال: أوصيت بحمل جاريتي هذه لفلان؛ لأنه يجري فيه الإرث، فكذا الوصية أيضا؛ لأنها أخته. إن ولدت شرط لكلا الصورتين أي إنما تصح الوصية للحمل، وبالحمل إن ولدت المرأة ذلك الحمل لأقل مدته وهي ستة أشهر من وقت الوصية، وإن أوصى به يعتبر من وقت الموت. ولا تصح الهبة له أي للحمل؛ لأن الهبة من شرطها القبول، ولا يتصور ذلك من الجنين، ولا يلي عليه أحد حتى يقبض عنه، فصار كالبيع. صحت الوصية لأن الحمل لا يتناوله اسم الجارية لفظا، وإنما يستحق بالإطلاق تبعا، فإذا أفرد الأم بالوصية صح إفراده؛ لأن الحمل يجوز إفراده بالوصية، فكذا استثناؤه؛ لأن كل ما جاز إيراد العقد عليه جاز إخراجه من العقد. وله الرجوع أي للموصي الرجوع عن الوصية؛ لأن القبول بعد الموت فجاز الرجوع قبل القبول كسائر العقود، ثم الرجوع إما يكون قولا بأن قال: رجعت عن وصيتي به له، أو فعلا بأن باع الموصي أو وهب أو قطع الثوب أو ذبح الشاة. والجحود أي الإنكار بأن قال له رجل هل أوصيت؟ فأنكر لا يكون رجوعا؛ لأن الجحود نفي الأصل، فلا يجامعه الرجوع؛ إذ الرجوع يستلزم الإثبات وبه كان يفتي محمد، فلذلك اختاره الشيخ، وعند أبي يوسف: هو رجوع؛ لأن الجحود نفي في الماضي والحال فالأولى أن يكون رجوعا وبه قالت الثلاثة، وفي "العيون": الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف
Book of Wills. Rulings of the will. A bequest is valid for a fetus and by a fetus if she gives birth to it for the shortest term from the time of the will. A gift is not valid for a fetus. If he bequeaths a slave-girl except her pregnancy, the bequest and the exception are valid. He may revoke the bequest verbally or by action, such as by selling, giving as a gift, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. Denial is not a revocation. The third is disputed: if he said 'I bequeath a third of my wealth to so-and-so,' then he becomes free, the bequest is void according to Abu Hanifa contrary to the two. The bequest for a fetus is valid because it is deputyship, and the fetus is suitable as a deputy in inheritance, so also in bequest. It is not said that its condition is acceptance by its people, for we say: the bequest resembles a gift and resembles inheritance. Due to its resemblance to a gift, acceptance is required when possible, but the fetus is not among its people. Due to its resemblance to inheritance, it drops when not possible, acting on both resemblances. For this reason it drops upon the death of the legatee before acceptance. And by it the bequest by a fetus is valid, such as if he said 'I bequeath the pregnancy of this my slave-girl to so-and-so' because inheritance applies to it, so also bequest because it is its sister. If she gives birth is a condition for both forms: the bequest for a fetus and by a fetus is only valid if the woman gives birth to that pregnancy at its shortest term, which is six months from the time of the will, and if he bequeaths by it it is considered from the time of death. A gift is not valid for it (the fetus) because acceptance is a condition of the gift, and that is not conceivable from the fetus, nor does anyone act as his guardian to accept delivery for him, so it becomes like a sale. The bequest is valid because the name 'slave-girl' does not include the pregnancy literally, but it is entitled by absolute mention as a dependent. If he singles out the mother with the bequest, its singling out is valid because the pregnancy is permitted to be singled out in a bequest, so also its exception because whatever is permitted to be included in a contract is permitted to be excluded from it. He may revoke: the testator may revoke the bequest because acceptance is after death, so revocation is permitted before acceptance like other contracts. Then revocation is either verbal, such as saying 'I have revoked my bequest to him for it,' or by action, such as the testator selling, giving as a gift, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. Denial: denial such as a man saying to him 'Did you bequeath?' and he denies, is not a revocation because denial negates the origin, so it does not coexist with revocation since revocation entails affirmation. Muhammad used to give fatwa accordingly, so the teacher chose it. According to Abu Yusuf: it is a revocation because denial negates in the past and present, so it is more appropriate to be a revocation, and the three said that. In al-'Uyun: the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with three main issues: bequests involving a fetus, revocation of wills, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether denial (juhud) constitutes revocation. The author first states that a bequest is valid for a fetus (i.e., when the legatee is a fetus) and by a fetus (i.e., bequeathing the fetus itself as the subject), provided the fetus is born alive within six months of the will (or from the time of death if the subject is bequeathed). This is based on the principle that a bequest resembles both a gift and inheritance: like a gift, acceptance is normally required, but since a fetus cannot accept, the resemblance to inheritance takes precedence, allowing validity. The bequest is valid even if the mother is bequeathed except the pregnancy—the exception is valid because the pregnancy is not included in the name 'slave-girl' literally. Revocation can be verbal or by an act that disposes of the property, like selling or giving away. A key dispute arises on denial: Abu Hanifa holds that denying having made a bequest is not revocation because it negates the very existence of the bequest, whereas Abu Yusuf (and also Muhammad and the other two, i.e., possibly the Sahibayn) argue that since denial negates in the past and present, it effectively cancels the bequest and thus is a revocation. The text notes that fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's view. The legal reasoning is analogical (qiyas) based on the nature of revocation and denial.

Key Terms
الوصية للحمل (al-wasiyyah li al-haml): A bequest where the legatee is a fetus in the womb, valid if born within six months of the will.
الوصية بالحمل (al-wasiyyah bi al-haml): A bequest where the subject is a fetus (pregnancy), valid under the same condition.
الهبة (al-hibah): Gift – a contract requiring offer, acceptance, and delivery; invalid for a fetus due to impossibility of acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a valid bequest to a fetus in the Hanafi school?
A) The fetus must be born within nine months.
B) The fetus must be born alive within six months of the will.
C) The fetus must be named at the time of the will.
D) The fetus must be born before the testator's death.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a fetus is valid on condition that the fetus is born alive within six months of the will, based on its resemblance to inheritance.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Revocation of Wills: Verbal and by Action
Ruling on revocation of wills and dispute on denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid methods of revoking a will in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether denial constitutes revocation.

Core Idea
A will can be revoked verbally or by any act that disposes of the property; denial is considered revocation according to the fatwa.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rules on revoking a will. The text states that revocation is permissible before acceptance by the legatee, and it can be done verbally or through actions that indicate a change of intent, such as selling or giving away the bequeathed property. It then introduces a dispute on denial (juhud): whether denying having made a will counts as revocation. This intra-Hanafi difference has practical consequences for whether the legatee still has rights.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Revocation is permitted before the legatee accepts the bequest, because acceptance occurs after the testator's death. Until then, the testator may change his mind.
Unlike a gift, a will is revocable before acceptance.
2
Identify verbal revocation
Verbal revocation is explicit: the testator says 'I revoke my bequest.'
Clear statement suffices.
3
Identify acts of revocation
Any action that disposes of the property – such as selling, giving as a gift, cutting cloth (if bequeathed), etc. – constitutes revocation because it shows the testator no longer intends the bequest.
The act must be inconsistent with the bequest.
4
Introduce the denial dispute
When asked 'Did you make a bequest?', if the testator denies (juhud), there is ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says it is not revocation, but Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad) say it is. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to al-'Uyun, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, making denial a form of revocation.
This is the relied-upon position for practice.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا
أحكام الوصية
وتصح الوصية للحمل وبه إن ولدت لأقل مدته من وقت الوصية، ولا تصح الهبة بالحمل. وإن أوصى بأمة إلا حملها صحت الوصية والاستثناء وله الرجوع عن الوصية قولا وفعلا بأن باع أو وهب أو قطع الثوب، أو ذبح الشاة، والجحود لا يكون رجوعا. والثالث: مختلف فيه، وهو ما إذا قال: أوصيت بثلث مالي لفلان، ثم عتق، فالوصية باطلة عند أبي حنيفة خلافا لهما. وتصح الوصية للحمل لأنها استخلاف، والجنين يصلح خليفة في الإرث، فكذا في الوصية، لا يقال: شرطها القبول، أهله؛ لأنا نقول: الوصية تشبه الهبة وتشبه الميراث كما مر فلشبهها بالهبة يشترط القبول إذا أمكن، والجنين ليس من أهله، ولشبهها بالميراث يسقط إذا لم يمكن عملا بالشبهين، ولهذا يسقط بموت الموصى له قبل القبول. وبه تصح الوصية بالحمل بأن قال: أوصيت بحمل جاريتي هذه لفلان؛ لأنه يجري فيه الإرث، فكذا الوصية أيضا؛ لأنها أخته. إن ولدت شرط لكلا الصورتين أي إنما تصح الوصية للحمل، وبالحمل إن ولدت المرأة ذلك الحمل لأقل مدته وهي ستة أشهر من وقت الوصية، وإن أوصى به يعتبر من وقت الموت. ولا تصح الهبة له أي للحمل؛ لأن الهبة من شرطها القبول، ولا يتصور ذلك من الجنين، ولا يلي عليه أحد حتى يقبض عنه، فصار كالبيع. صحت الوصية لأن الحمل لا يتناوله اسم الجارية لفظا، وإنما يستحق بالإطلاق تبعا، فإذا أفرد الأم بالوصية صح إفراده؛ لأن الحمل يجوز إفراده بالوصية، فكذا استثناؤه؛ لأن كل ما جاز إيراد العقد عليه جاز إخراجه من العقد. وله الرجوع أي للموصي الرجوع عن الوصية؛ لأن القبول بعد الموت فجاز الرجوع قبل القبول كسائر العقود، ثم الرجوع إما يكون قولا بأن قال: رجعت عن وصيتي به له، أو فعلا بأن باع الموصي أو وهب أو قطع الثوب أو ذبح الشاة. والجحود أي الإنكار بأن قال له رجل هل أوصيت؟ فأنكر لا يكون رجوعا؛ لأن الجحود نفي الأصل، فلا يجامعه الرجوع؛ إذ الرجوع يستلزم الإثبات وبه كان يفتي محمد، فلذلك اختاره الشيخ، وعند أبي يوسف: هو رجوع؛ لأن الجحود نفي في الماضي والحال فالأولى أن يكون رجوعا وبه قالت الثلاثة، وفي "العيون": الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف
Book of Wills. Rulings of the will. A bequest is valid for a fetus and by a fetus if she gives birth to it for the shortest term from the time of the will. A gift is not valid for a fetus. If he bequeaths a slave-girl except her pregnancy, the bequest and the exception are valid. He may revoke the bequest verbally or by action, such as by selling, giving as a gift, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. Denial is not a revocation. The third is disputed: if he said 'I bequeath a third of my wealth to so-and-so,' then he becomes free, the bequest is void according to Abu Hanifa contrary to the two. The bequest for a fetus is valid because it is deputyship, and the fetus is suitable as a deputy in inheritance, so also in bequest. It is not said that its condition is acceptance by its people, for we say: the bequest resembles a gift and resembles inheritance. Due to its resemblance to a gift, acceptance is required when possible, but the fetus is not among its people. Due to its resemblance to inheritance, it drops when not possible, acting on both resemblances. For this reason it drops upon the death of the legatee before acceptance. And by it the bequest by a fetus is valid, such as if he said 'I bequeath the pregnancy of this my slave-girl to so-and-so' because inheritance applies to it, so also bequest because it is its sister. If she gives birth is a condition for both forms: the bequest for a fetus and by a fetus is only valid if the woman gives birth to that pregnancy at its shortest term, which is six months from the time of the will, and if he bequeaths by it it is considered from the time of death. A gift is not valid for it (the fetus) because acceptance is a condition of the gift, and that is not conceivable from the fetus, nor does anyone act as his guardian to accept delivery for him, so it becomes like a sale. The bequest is valid because the name 'slave-girl' does not include the pregnancy literally, but it is entitled by absolute mention as a dependent. If he singles out the mother with the bequest, its singling out is valid because the pregnancy is permitted to be singled out in a bequest, so also its exception because whatever is permitted to be included in a contract is permitted to be excluded from it. He may revoke: the testator may revoke the bequest because acceptance is after death, so revocation is permitted before acceptance like other contracts. Then revocation is either verbal, such as saying 'I have revoked my bequest to him for it,' or by action, such as the testator selling, giving as a gift, cutting the cloth, or slaughtering the sheep. Denial: denial such as a man saying to him 'Did you bequeath?' and he denies, is not a revocation because denial negates the origin, so it does not coexist with revocation since revocation entails affirmation. Muhammad used to give fatwa accordingly, so the teacher chose it. According to Abu Yusuf: it is a revocation because denial negates in the past and present, so it is more appropriate to be a revocation, and the three said that. In al-'Uyun: the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with three main issues: bequests involving a fetus, revocation of wills, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether denial (juhud) constitutes revocation. The author first states that a bequest is valid for a fetus (i.e., when the legatee is a fetus) and by a fetus (i.e., bequeathing the fetus itself as the subject), provided the fetus is born alive within six months of the will (or from the time of death if the subject is bequeathed). This is based on the principle that a bequest resembles both a gift and inheritance: like a gift, acceptance is normally required, but since a fetus cannot accept, the resemblance to inheritance takes precedence, allowing validity. The bequest is valid even if the mother is bequeathed except the pregnancy—the exception is valid because the pregnancy is not included in the name 'slave-girl' literally. Revocation can be verbal or by an act that disposes of the property, like selling or giving away. A key dispute arises on denial: Abu Hanifa holds that denying having made a bequest is not revocation because it negates the very existence of the bequest, whereas Abu Yusuf (and also Muhammad and the other two, i.e., possibly the Sahibayn) argue that since denial negates in the past and present, it effectively cancels the bequest and thus is a revocation. The text notes that fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's view. The legal reasoning is analogical (qiyas) based on the nature of revocation and denial.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الوصية (al-ruju' 'an al-wasiyyah): Revocation of the will by the testator, valid before acceptance, by word or action that changes ownership.
الجحود (al-juhud): Denial of having made a bequest when asked; disputed whether it constitutes revocation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a testator denying that he made a bequest?
A) It is not considered a revocation.
B) It is considered a revocation.
C) It is only a revocation if said in a legal setting.
D) It has no effect on the bequest.

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a will is valid before acceptance verbally or by action; denial of the will constitutes revocation according to the Hanafi fatwa.

Distributing the One-Third Among Multiple Legatees: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Preference
Rulings on distributing one-third with multiple legatees and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for distributing the one-third among multiple legatees when total bequests exceed the limit without heir consent, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of preference.

Core Idea
Excess bequests over one-third are void; within the one-third, Hanafis dispute whether preference can operate.

This lesson deals with the distribution of the one-third of an estate when multiple bequests exceed that limit and the heirs do not consent. The Hanafi school has clear rules for proportionate splitting, but a notable intra-madhhab dispute arises when one legatee is given 'all wealth' and another 'one-third'. Abu Hanifa treats both as one-third each, while the Sahibayn allow the testator's preference to proportion the shares. This lesson walks through the rulings and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Without heir consent, only one-third of the estate can be used for bequests.
This is the fundamental limit.
2
Apply to simple cases
When two legatees each get one-third, they split the actual one-third equally. When one gets one-third and another one-sixth, they split in a 2:1 ratio.
Proportional distribution is the norm.
3
Analyze the complex case
One legatee is given 'all wealth' and another 'one-third'. Total exceeds one-third, so the excess is void.
The question is how to distribute the valid one-third pool.
4
Compare the two positions
Abu Hanifa: equal split (half each) because the 'all' bequest is reduced to one-third. Sahibayn: three-quarters to the 'all' legatee, one-quarter to the other, because preference can be given within the one-third.
This is the core intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Understand the reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues preference is part of the void excess and cannot stand alone. The Sahibayn argue the testator's intent for preference is independent and can operate within the limit.
Both views are rational; the dispute is on the nature of the voiding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ولآخر بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة، فثلثه لهما، وإن أوصى لآخر بثلث ماله ثم لآخر بسدس ماله فالثلث بينهما أثلاثا، وإن أوصى لأحدهما بجميع ماله والآخر بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة، فثلثه بينهما نصفان ولا يضرب للموصى له بالكل شيء زائد على الثلث. هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الثلث بينهما على أربعة أسهم: ثلاثة أرباع للموصى له بالكل، وسهم للموصى له بالثلث؛ لأن الموصي قصد شيئين: الاستحقاق والتفضيل وامتناع الاستحقاق لحق الورثة ولا مانع من التفضيل. وله: أن الوصية بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة باطلة فيجعل كأنه أوصى لكل بالثلث فتنصف والتفضيل ثبت في ضمن الاستحقاق، فبطل ببطلانه. ولا يضرب بيان للأصل الذي يتفرع عليه المسألة الخلافية المذكورة آنفا يعني إذا أوصى لرجل بأكثر من الثلث، ولم تجز الورثة لا يجعل له سهم فيما زاد على الثلث عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما: يضرب له بما زاد على الثلث.
Chapter of bequest of one-third of wealth and similar. If he bequeaths to a man one-third of his wealth and to another one-third of his wealth and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third is for both of them. If he bequeaths to another one-third of his wealth then to another one-sixth of his wealth, then the one-third is between them in three portions. If he bequeaths to one of them all his wealth and to the other one-third of his wealth and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third is between them half and half, and nothing extra over the one-third is given to the one bequeathed all. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the one-third is between them in four shares: three-quarters for the one bequeathed all, and one share for the one bequeathed one-third, because the testator intended two things: entitlement and preference. Entitlement is prevented by the heirs' right, but there is no obstacle to preference. For him (Abu Hanifa): the bequest of more than one-third, if the heirs do not consent, is void, so it is considered as if he bequeathed one-third to each, so it is divided half. Preference is established within entitlement, so it is void by its voidness. And 'he is not given' is an explanation of the principle from which the aforementioned disputed issue branches, meaning if he bequeaths to a man more than one-third and the heirs do not consent, no share is given to him for the excess over one-third according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two, he is given for the excess over one-third.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This chapter from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses how to distribute the one-third of the estate among multiple legatees when the total bequests exceed one-third and the heirs do not consent. The fundamental rule is that without heir consent, only one-third can be used for bequests. When two people are each bequeathed one-third (total two-thirds), they split the actual one-third equally (half each). If one is bequeathed one-third and another one-sixth (total half), they split the one-third in proportion: the one with one-third gets two parts, the one with one-sixth gets one part (since one-third is double one-sixth). A more complex case arises when one is bequeathed all the wealth and another is bequeathed one-third. Since the total exceeds one-third, what happens? Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest of 'all' is void as to the excess over one-third, so effectively each is considered to have one-third, and they split the one-third equally (half each). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that since the testator's intent included preference for the one with 'all', and there is no bar to preferring within the one-third limit, the distribution should be proportional: the one with 'all' gets three-fourths (since 'all' is three times 'one-third'), and the one with one-third gets one-fourth. The Hanafi response points out that preference is tied to entitlement; if the full entitlement is void, the preference falls with it. The key principle stated: 'He is not given anything over one-third' means no share for the excess. This chapter illustrates the Hanafi method of handling conflicting bequests with limited resources.

Key Terms
الوصية بثلث المال (al-wasiyyah bi-thuluth al-mal): Bequest of one-third of the estate, the maximum allowed without heir consent.
التفضيل (al-tafdil): Preference given to one legatee over another within the one-third limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a testator bequeaths all his wealth to one person and one-third to another without heir consent, how does Abu Hanifa rule the one-third should be divided?
A) Entirely to the one bequeathed all.
B) Half to each.
C) Three-quarters to the one bequeathed all, one-quarter to the other.
D) Proportional to the original amounts.

Key Takeaway
Within the one-third limit, bequests are distributed proportionally; the Sahibayn's allowance of preference marks a significant intra-Hanafi difference.

Dividing the One-Third Among Multiple Legatees: Equal and Proportional Shares
Basic division of the third with multiple legatees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the division of the available one-third of an estate when multiple bequests are made, applying the Hanafi rule that equal claims yield equal shares and proportional claims yield proportional shares.

Core Idea
When multiple bequests exhaust the one-third, the division follows the strength of each claim—equal or proportional.

This lesson unpacks the first two scenarios from the source: when two people each receive a bequest of one-third, and when one receives one-third and another one-sixth. Understanding these simple cases is essential before tackling the more complex disputes. The guiding principle is that the available one-third is divided according to the measure of each legatee's right, with no extra share for anyone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequests and heirs' consent
Note what each legatee was bequeathed and whether the heirs consent. In our scenarios, they do not consent, so only one-third is available.
Heirs' consent would allow full execution, but here it is denied.
2
Determine if the third is sufficient for both
If both bequests together exceed one-third, the third must be shared. If they were within the third, no reduction needed.
3
Check equality of cause
If both bequests are of the same amount (e.g., one-third each), their rights are equal, so they share the third equally.
Equality of cause leads to equality in entitlement.
4
Apply proportional division for unequal bequests
If one bequest is larger (e.g., one-third) and the other smaller (e.g., one-sixth), divide the third in proportion to their values: 2:1 ratio.
Analogous to creditors dividing a bankrupt estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
باب الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
أوصى لذا بثلث ماله ولآخر بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة، فثلثه لهما، وإن أوصى لآخر الوصيتين أي ثلث ماله ماله، فالثلث بينهما أثلاثا ، وإن أوصى لأحدهما بجميع ماله والآخر بثلث ماله و لم تجز الورثة، فثلثه بينهما نصفان ولا يضرب للموصى له . هو رجوع؛ لأن الجحود نفي في الماضي والحال فالأولى أن يكون رجوعا وبه قالت الثلاثة، وفي "العيون": الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٦/٢]
باب الوصية إلخ لما كان أقصى ما يدور عليه مسائل الوصايا عند عدم إجازة الورثة ثلث المال، ذكر تلك المسائل التي تتعلق بها في هذا الباب بعد ذكر مقدمات هذا الكتاب كذا في "النهاية" و"الغاية". [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٨٠/٩] فثلثه لهما : أي إذا لم تجز الورثة الوصيتين كان الثلث بينهما؛ لأن ثلث المال يضيق عن حقهما؛ إذ لا يزاد عليه عند عدم الإجازة، وقد تساويا في سبب الاستحقاق، فيستويان في الاستحقاق والمحل يقبل الشركة، فيكون الثلث بينهما نصفين؛ لاستواء حقهما، و لم يوجد ما يدل على الرجوع عن الأول تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٨٠/٩] وإن أوصى لآخر إلخ يعني أوصى لرجل بسدس ماله بعد أن أوصى لزيد مثلا بثلث ماله، فالثلث بينهما من حيث الأثلاث؛ لأن كل واحد منهما يستحق بسبب صحيح شرعي، وضاق الثلث عن حقهما، فيقسمانه على قدر حقهما كما في أصحاب الديون، فيجعل الأقل سهما، والأكثر سهمين، فصار ثلاثة أسهم: سهم لصاحب الأقل، وسهمان لصاحب الأكثر. (عيني، هداية)
بينهما نصفان: هذا عند أبي حنيفة حاله، وعندهما الثلث بينهما على أربعة أسهم: ثلاثة أرباع للموصى له بالكل، وسهم للموصى له بالثلث؛ لأن الثلث واحد والكل ثلاثة فصارت أربعة لهما: أن الموصي قصد شيئين: الاستحقاق والتفضيل وامتناع الاستحقاق لحق الورثة ولا مانع من التفضيل وله: أن الوصية بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة باطلة فيجعل كأنه أوصى لكل بالثلث فتنصف والتفضيل ثبت في ضمن الاستحقاق، فبطل ببطلانه. (فتح بتصرف) ولا يضرب إلخ بيان للأصل الذي يتفرع عليه المسألة الخلافية المذكورة آنفا يعني إذا أوصى لرجل بأكثر من الثلث، ولم تجز الورثة لا يجعل له سهم فيما زاد على الثلث عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما: يضرب له بما زاد على قالت الثلاثة، فمفعول قوله "لا" "يضرب محذوف أي لا يضرب له شيئا زائدا على من أوصى له بالثلث، وفي "المغرب": ضرب في الجزور بسهم إذا شرك فيها وأخذ منها نصيبا وقال الفقهاء: فلان يضرب فيه بالثلث أي يأخذ منه شيئا بحكم ماله من الثلث لهما أن الوصية أخت الميراث، والوارث يضرب في التركة، = فكذا هذا وله : أن الموصى له يضرب بما يستحقه، وهو لا يستحق ما وراء الثلث إلا بإجازة الورثة، ولم يوجد، إلا أن الإمام استثنى من هذا الحكم الصور الثلث المذكورة بقوله: "إلا في المحاباة" إلخ، ووجه الفرق له بين هذه الصور الثلاث وبين غيرها أن الوصية إذا كانت مقدرة بما زاد على الثلث صريحا كالنصف والثلثين، والشرع أبطل الوصية في الزائد يكون ذكره لغوا، فلا يعتبر في حق الضرب، بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن مقدرة حيث لا يكون في العبارة ما يكون مبطلا للوصية كما إذا أوصى بخمسين، واتفق أن ماله مائة فإن الوصية غير باطلة بالكلية لإمكان أن يظهر له فوق المائة، وإذا لم تبطل بالكلية تكون معتبرة في حق الضرب. (فتح)
ذلك من إلا في المحاباة: أي لا يضرب للموصى له بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة إلا في هذه الصور الثلاث، وصورة المحاباة: أن يكون له عبدان قيمة أحدهما ألف ومائة، وقيمة الآخر ست مائة وأوصى بأن يباع واحد منهما بمائة لفلان، والآخر بمائة لفلان آخر، فقد حصلت المحاباة لأحدهما بألف درهم، ولآخر بخمس مائة، فإن خرج ثلث ماله، أو أجازت الورثة جاز ذلك، وإن لم يكن له مال غيرهما، ولم تجز الورثة جاز محاباتهما بقدر الثلث، فيكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بحسب وصيته، وهي الألف، والموصى له الآخر بحسب وصيته وهي خمس مائة، فلو كان هذا كسائر الوصايا وجب أن لا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بأكثر من خمس مائة وستة وستين وثلثي درهم عند الإمام؛ لأن عنده الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث لا يضرب إلا بالثلث، وهذا ثلث ماله. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢]
والسعاية صورة السعاية أن يوصى بعتق هذين العبدين قيمة أحدهما ألف وقيمة الآخر ألفان، ولا مال له غيرهما، فإن أجازت الورثة يعتقان معا، وإن لم تجز الورثة يعتقان من الثلث وثلث ماله ألف، فيكون الثلث منه للذي قيمته ألف فيعتق منه هذا القدر بجانا، وهو ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو الثلثان ستمائة وستة وستون درهما وثلثا درهم والثلثان منه للذي قيمته ألفان، فيعتق منه هذا القدر بلا سعاية، وهو ست مائة وستة وستون وثلثا درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو ألف وثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم، فلو كان كسائر الوصايا وجب أن يسعى الذي قيمته ألف في خمس مائة نصف قيمته، والذي قيمته ألفان في ألف وخمس مائة ثلاثة أرباع قيمته؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يضرب الذي قيمته ألفان إلا بالألف، فوجب أن يكون بينهما نصفان رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢] والدراهم المرسلة إلخ [أي المطلقة عن كونها ثلثا أو نصفا أو نحوهما. (طائي)] صورة الدراهم المرسلة: أن لأحدهما بألف ولآخر بألفين وثلث ماله ألف، ولم تجز الورثة، يكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا، يضرب كل واحد منهما بقدر حقه، فللموصى له بالألف، ثلثه ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم وللموصى له بألفين، ضعفه ست مائة وستة وستون وثلثا درهم، وكان قياس أصل أبي حنيفة أن يكون الألف بينهما نصفين رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢]
The Book of Wills. Bequest of One-Third of Wealth and the Like. Chapter on bequest of one-third of wealth and the like. If he bequeaths to someone one-third of his wealth and to another one-third of his wealth, and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third belongs to them both. If he bequeaths to another the two bequests, meaning one-third of his wealth, then the one-third is between them in thirds. If he bequeaths to one of them all his wealth and to the other one-third of his wealth, and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third is between them half-half, and the legatee does not receive a share [of the excess]. It is revocation; because denial is negation in the past and present, so it is more appropriate to be revocation, and with that the three said. In 'al-Uyun': the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/476] The chapter on bequest etc. Since the maximum domain of the issues of wills when the heirs do not consent is one-third of the wealth, he mentioned those issues related to it in this chapter after mentioning the introductions of this book. This is from 'al-Nihaya' and 'al-Ghaya'. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/280] So his one-third belongs to both: meaning if the heirs do not consent to both bequests, the one-third is between them; because the one-third of wealth is insufficient for both their rights, as it is not increased upon at the time of non-consent. They are equal in the cause of entitlement, so they are equal in entitlement, and the locus accepts partnership, so the one-third is half between them due to equality of their rights, and nothing indicates revocation of the first. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/280] 'And if he bequeaths to another' etc. means he bequeaths to a man one-sixth of his wealth after he had bequeathed to Zayd, for example, one-third of his wealth. Then the one-third is between them in terms of thirds, because each of them is entitled by a valid legal cause, and the one-third is insufficient for both their rights, so they divide it according to the measure of their rights as in the case of creditors. Thus the smaller is made one share, and the larger two shares, so it becomes three shares: one share for the owner of the smaller, two shares for the owner of the larger. (Ayni, Hidaya) 'Half between them': This is according to Abu Hanifa in his view, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the one-third is between them in four shares: three quarters for the legatee of all, and one share for the legatee of one-third; because the one-third is one and the all is three, so they become four. Their argument: The testator intended two things: entitlement and preference; entitlement is prevented due to the right of the heirs, but there is no obstacle to preference. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: The bequest of more than one-third, if the heirs do not consent, is void, so it is as if he bequeathed to each one-third, so it becomes half, and preference is established within entitlement, so it is nullified by its nullity. (Fath with adaptation) 'And the legatee does not receive a share' etc. is an explanation of the principle from which the aforementioned disputed issue branches. It means if he bequeaths to a man more than one-third, and the heirs do not consent, he is not given a share in what exceeds the one-third according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them, he is given a share for the excess. The three said, so the object of 'does not' is omitted, i.e. he is not given anything in excess over the one for whom he bequeathed one-third. In 'al-Maghrib': 'daraba fi al-jazur' means he participates in the camel and takes a portion. The jurists said: So-and-so participates with one-third, i.e. he takes something by virtue of his right to one-third. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) argument: The bequest is a sibling of inheritance, and the heir participates in the estate, so likewise this. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: The legatee participates according to what he is entitled to, and he is not entitled to beyond one-third except by the consent of the heirs, and it does not exist. However, the Imam (Abu Hanifa) excepted from this ruling the three mentioned scenarios by his saying: 'except in the case of muhabah' etc. The difference for him between these three scenarios and others is that if the bequest is explicitly quantified as exceeding one-third, like half or two-thirds, and the Law invalidates the bequest in the excess, then mentioning it is futile and not considered for participation. Contrary to when it is not quantified, where there is nothing in the expression that invalidates the bequest, as if he bequeaths fifty dirhams and it happens that his wealth is one hundred, then the bequest is not totally invalid because it is possible that his wealth exceeds one hundred, and if it is not totally invalid, it is considered for participation. (Fath) 'That of except in muhabah': i.e. the legatee does not participate with more than one-third if the heirs do not consent except in these three scenarios. The scenario of muhabah: He has two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and one hundred, and the value of the other is six hundred, and he instructed that one of them be sold for one hundred to someone and the other for one hundred to another. Then there is a beneficial sale for one of them of one thousand dirhams, and for the other five hundred. If one-third of his wealth covers it, or the heirs consent, it is permissible. If he has no other wealth besides these two, and the heirs do not consent, their beneficial sale is permissible to the extent of one-third, so the one-third is between them in thirds. The legatee of one thousand participates according to his bequest, which is one thousand, and the other legatee according to his bequest, which is five hundred. If this were like other bequests, it would be necessary that the legatee of one thousand should not participate with more than five hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams according to the Imam, because in his view the legatee of more than one-third does not participate except with one-third, and this is one-third of his wealth. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477] 'And al-sa'yah': The scenario of sa'yah: He bequeaths the emancipation of these two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and the value of the other is two thousand, and he has no other wealth besides them. If the heirs consent, both are freed together. If the heirs do not consent, both are freed from the one-third, and one-third of his wealth is one thousand. Then the one-third from the slave worth one thousand is freed without payment from that amount, which is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and he works for the remainder, which is two-thirds: six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And the two-thirds from the slave worth two thousand is freed without payment from that amount, which is six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, and he works for the remainder, which is one thousand three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams. If this were like other bequests, it would be necessary that the slave worth one thousand should work for five hundred (half his value), and the slave worth two thousand should work for one thousand five hundred (three-quarters of his value), because then the slave worth two thousand does not participate except with one thousand, so it would be necessary that it be half between them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477] 'And al-darahim al-mursalah' etc. [i.e. unspecified as to being one-third, half, or the like. (Ta'i)] The scenario of unspecified dirhams: He bequeaths to one one thousand and to another two thousand, and one-third of his wealth is one thousand, and the heirs do not consent. Then the one-third is between them in thirds; each participates according to his right. So for the legatee of one thousand, his one-third is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and for the legatee of two thousand, his double is six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And the original analogy of Abu Hanifa would require that the one thousand be half between them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477]
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentaries presents rulings on bequests (wasiyya) involving one-third of the estate when the heirs do not consent to the bequest. The key principle is that without the heirs' consent, only one-third of the testator's wealth can be executed for bequests. The chapter covers multiple beneficiaries with different shares. The first scenario: if two people each receive a bequest of one-third, and the heirs do not consent, the available third is divided equally between them. This is straightforward because their claims are equal. The second scenario: one beneficiary is bequeathed one-third and another one-sixth, the third is divided in a 2:1 ratio, proportional to their claims. The third scenario is more debated: one beneficiary is bequeathed the entire estate and another one-third. When the heirs do not consent, only one-third is available. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the third is divided equally between them. His reasoning: the bequest of the entire estate is void beyond the first third, so it is as if each was bequeathed one-third, resulting in equal shares. The two companions, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, rule that the third is divided in a 3:1 ratio—three-quarters for the one who was to receive all, one-quarter for the one who was to receive one-third. Their reasoning: the testator intended both entitlement and preference; since entitlement to all is prevented by the heirs' right, the preference remains in the available third. Abu Hanifa counters that preference is contingent on entitlement, and since entitlement to the excess is void, so is the preference. The passage then explains a general principle: a legatee does not receive a share in excess of one-third from the available third (Abu Hanifa's view). The two companions disagree, analogizing to inheritance where the heir participates in the whole estate. However, Abu Hanifa makes exceptions for three cases: (1) muhabah (a beneficial sale where the testator sold items below value), (2) sa'yah (bequest of emancipation of slaves, where the freed slaves work to pay off the remaining value), and (3) unspecified dirhams (where the bequest is in absolute terms not tied to a fraction). In these cases, the legatee participates according to the full amount of his bequest, not just one-third, because the bequest is not explicitly exceeding the third or is of a different nature. These exceptions are detailed with specific examples and calculations, showing how the available third is divided proportionally according to each bequest's value. The passage emphasizes the importance of understanding when a bequest is considered void in its excess and when it persists for participation in the third.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A testamentary disposition of property to take effect after death, governed by the rule that no more than one-third of the estate can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.
الثُلْث (al-thulth): One-third of the testator's net estate; the maximum amount that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and one-half to Amr, and heirs do not consent, how is the available one-third divided?
A) Equally between them.
B) Zayd gets 2/5, Amr gets 3/5 of the third.
C) Zayd gets 1/3, Amr gets 2/3 of the third.
D) Only Zayd receives because his bequest is within the third.

Key Takeaway
When multiple bequests compete for the limited one-third, the division is proportional to each legatee's specified share of the whole estate.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
15 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Bequest of All Property Plus Another's One-Third
Disputed division and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding the division of the one-third when one legatee is bequeathed all property and another one-third, and apply the exceptions of muhabah, sa'yah, and unspecified dirhams.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa divides the third equally; the two companions divide 3:1 in favor of the all-property legatee.

This lesson tackles the most debated scenario in the passage: a testator leaves everything to one person and one-third to another. The heirs reject both, so only the third is available. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on how to split it. Their arguments reveal deeper principles about entitlement, preference, and the nature of void bequests. The passage also provides three exceptions where even Abu Hanifa's general rule is set aside.

Guided Path
1
State the exact scenario and the issue
One legatee gets all, another gets one-third. Heirs do not consent. Only the one-third is executable. How should it be divided?
The total bequests exceed the third.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's view and his proof
Abu Hanifa says the third is divided equally (half each). His reasoning: the bequest of all is void beyond the third, so it becomes like a bequest of one-third. Both claims are thus equal.
Preference is subsidiary to entitlement; without entitlement, preference falls.
3
Present the two companions' view and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the third is divided 3:1 (three-fourths to the all-property legatee, one-fourth to the other). Their reasoning: the testator intended both entitlement and preference; entitlement to all is blocked by heirs' right, but preference remains.
They analogize to inheritance where heirs participate proportionally.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-argument
He responds that preference cannot exist independently of entitlement. Since the entitlement to the whole is void, the preference vanishes as well.
5
Learn the three exceptions to the rule
Abu Hanifa makes exceptions for muhabah (beneficial sale), sa'yah (bequest of emancipation), and unspecified dirhams (absolute amount). In these, the legatee participates according to the full bequest, not just the third.
These cases involve bequests that are not explicitly quantified as exceeding one-third or have a different nature.

كتاب الوصايا
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
باب الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
أوصى لذا بثلث ماله ولآخر بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة، فثلثه لهما، وإن أوصى لآخر الوصيتين أي ثلث ماله ماله، فالثلث بينهما أثلاثا ، وإن أوصى لأحدهما بجميع ماله والآخر بثلث ماله و لم تجز الورثة، فثلثه بينهما نصفان ولا يضرب للموصى له . هو رجوع؛ لأن الجحود نفي في الماضي والحال فالأولى أن يكون رجوعا وبه قالت الثلاثة، وفي "العيون": الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٦/٢]
باب الوصية إلخ لما كان أقصى ما يدور عليه مسائل الوصايا عند عدم إجازة الورثة ثلث المال، ذكر تلك المسائل التي تتعلق بها في هذا الباب بعد ذكر مقدمات هذا الكتاب كذا في "النهاية" و"الغاية". [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٨٠/٩] فثلثه لهما : أي إذا لم تجز الورثة الوصيتين كان الثلث بينهما؛ لأن ثلث المال يضيق عن حقهما؛ إذ لا يزاد عليه عند عدم الإجازة، وقد تساويا في سبب الاستحقاق، فيستويان في الاستحقاق والمحل يقبل الشركة، فيكون الثلث بينهما نصفين؛ لاستواء حقهما، و لم يوجد ما يدل على الرجوع عن الأول تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٨٠/٩] وإن أوصى لآخر إلخ يعني أوصى لرجل بسدس ماله بعد أن أوصى لزيد مثلا بثلث ماله، فالثلث بينهما من حيث الأثلاث؛ لأن كل واحد منهما يستحق بسبب صحيح شرعي، وضاق الثلث عن حقهما، فيقسمانه على قدر حقهما كما في أصحاب الديون، فيجعل الأقل سهما، والأكثر سهمين، فصار ثلاثة أسهم: سهم لصاحب الأقل، وسهمان لصاحب الأكثر. (عيني، هداية)
بينهما نصفان: هذا عند أبي حنيفة حاله، وعندهما الثلث بينهما على أربعة أسهم: ثلاثة أرباع للموصى له بالكل، وسهم للموصى له بالثلث؛ لأن الثلث واحد والكل ثلاثة فصارت أربعة لهما: أن الموصي قصد شيئين: الاستحقاق والتفضيل وامتناع الاستحقاق لحق الورثة ولا مانع من التفضيل وله: أن الوصية بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة باطلة فيجعل كأنه أوصى لكل بالثلث فتنصف والتفضيل ثبت في ضمن الاستحقاق، فبطل ببطلانه. (فتح بتصرف) ولا يضرب إلخ بيان للأصل الذي يتفرع عليه المسألة الخلافية المذكورة آنفا يعني إذا أوصى لرجل بأكثر من الثلث، ولم تجز الورثة لا يجعل له سهم فيما زاد على الثلث عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما: يضرب له بما زاد على قالت الثلاثة، فمفعول قوله "لا" "يضرب محذوف أي لا يضرب له شيئا زائدا على من أوصى له بالثلث، وفي "المغرب": ضرب في الجزور بسهم إذا شرك فيها وأخذ منها نصيبا وقال الفقهاء: فلان يضرب فيه بالثلث أي يأخذ منه شيئا بحكم ماله من الثلث لهما أن الوصية أخت الميراث، والوارث يضرب في التركة، = فكذا هذا وله : أن الموصى له يضرب بما يستحقه، وهو لا يستحق ما وراء الثلث إلا بإجازة الورثة، ولم يوجد، إلا أن الإمام استثنى من هذا الحكم الصور الثلث المذكورة بقوله: "إلا في المحاباة" إلخ، ووجه الفرق له بين هذه الصور الثلاث وبين غيرها أن الوصية إذا كانت مقدرة بما زاد على الثلث صريحا كالنصف والثلثين، والشرع أبطل الوصية في الزائد يكون ذكره لغوا، فلا يعتبر في حق الضرب، بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن مقدرة حيث لا يكون في العبارة ما يكون مبطلا للوصية كما إذا أوصى بخمسين، واتفق أن ماله مائة فإن الوصية غير باطلة بالكلية لإمكان أن يظهر له فوق المائة، وإذا لم تبطل بالكلية تكون معتبرة في حق الضرب. (فتح)
ذلك من إلا في المحاباة: أي لا يضرب للموصى له بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة إلا في هذه الصور الثلاث، وصورة المحاباة: أن يكون له عبدان قيمة أحدهما ألف ومائة، وقيمة الآخر ست مائة وأوصى بأن يباع واحد منهما بمائة لفلان، والآخر بمائة لفلان آخر، فقد حصلت المحاباة لأحدهما بألف درهم، ولآخر بخمس مائة، فإن خرج ثلث ماله، أو أجازت الورثة جاز ذلك، وإن لم يكن له مال غيرهما، ولم تجز الورثة جاز محاباتهما بقدر الثلث، فيكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بحسب وصيته، وهي الألف، والموصى له الآخر بحسب وصيته وهي خمس مائة، فلو كان هذا كسائر الوصايا وجب أن لا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بأكثر من خمس مائة وستة وستين وثلثي درهم عند الإمام؛ لأن عنده الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث لا يضرب إلا بالثلث، وهذا ثلث ماله. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢]
والسعاية صورة السعاية أن يوصى بعتق هذين العبدين قيمة أحدهما ألف وقيمة الآخر ألفان، ولا مال له غيرهما، فإن أجازت الورثة يعتقان معا، وإن لم تجز الورثة يعتقان من الثلث وثلث ماله ألف، فيكون الثلث منه للذي قيمته ألف فيعتق منه هذا القدر بجانا، وهو ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو الثلثان ستمائة وستة وستون درهما وثلثا درهم والثلثان منه للذي قيمته ألفان، فيعتق منه هذا القدر بلا سعاية، وهو ست مائة وستة وستون وثلثا درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو ألف وثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم، فلو كان كسائر الوصايا وجب أن يسعى الذي قيمته ألف في خمس مائة نصف قيمته، والذي قيمته ألفان في ألف وخمس مائة ثلاثة أرباع قيمته؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يضرب الذي قيمته ألفان إلا بالألف، فوجب أن يكون بينهما نصفان رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢] والدراهم المرسلة إلخ [أي المطلقة عن كونها ثلثا أو نصفا أو نحوهما. (طائي)] صورة الدراهم المرسلة: أن لأحدهما بألف ولآخر بألفين وثلث ماله ألف، ولم تجز الورثة، يكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا، يضرب كل واحد منهما بقدر حقه، فللموصى له بالألف، ثلثه ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم وللموصى له بألفين، ضعفه ست مائة وستة وستون وثلثا درهم، وكان قياس أصل أبي حنيفة أن يكون الألف بينهما نصفين رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢]
The Book of Wills. Bequest of One-Third of Wealth and the Like. Chapter on bequest of one-third of wealth and the like. If he bequeaths to someone one-third of his wealth and to another one-third of his wealth, and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third belongs to them both. If he bequeaths to another the two bequests, meaning one-third of his wealth, then the one-third is between them in thirds. If he bequeaths to one of them all his wealth and to the other one-third of his wealth, and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third is between them half-half, and the legatee does not receive a share [of the excess]. It is revocation; because denial is negation in the past and present, so it is more appropriate to be revocation, and with that the three said. In 'al-Uyun': the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/476] The chapter on bequest etc. Since the maximum domain of the issues of wills when the heirs do not consent is one-third of the wealth, he mentioned those issues related to it in this chapter after mentioning the introductions of this book. This is from 'al-Nihaya' and 'al-Ghaya'. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/280] So his one-third belongs to both: meaning if the heirs do not consent to both bequests, the one-third is between them; because the one-third of wealth is insufficient for both their rights, as it is not increased upon at the time of non-consent. They are equal in the cause of entitlement, so they are equal in entitlement, and the locus accepts partnership, so the one-third is half between them due to equality of their rights, and nothing indicates revocation of the first. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/280] 'And if he bequeaths to another' etc. means he bequeaths to a man one-sixth of his wealth after he had bequeathed to Zayd, for example, one-third of his wealth. Then the one-third is between them in terms of thirds, because each of them is entitled by a valid legal cause, and the one-third is insufficient for both their rights, so they divide it according to the measure of their rights as in the case of creditors. Thus the smaller is made one share, and the larger two shares, so it becomes three shares: one share for the owner of the smaller, two shares for the owner of the larger. (Ayni, Hidaya) 'Half between them': This is according to Abu Hanifa in his view, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the one-third is between them in four shares: three quarters for the legatee of all, and one share for the legatee of one-third; because the one-third is one and the all is three, so they become four. Their argument: The testator intended two things: entitlement and preference; entitlement is prevented due to the right of the heirs, but there is no obstacle to preference. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: The bequest of more than one-third, if the heirs do not consent, is void, so it is as if he bequeathed to each one-third, so it becomes half, and preference is established within entitlement, so it is nullified by its nullity. (Fath with adaptation) 'And the legatee does not receive a share' etc. is an explanation of the principle from which the aforementioned disputed issue branches. It means if he bequeaths to a man more than one-third, and the heirs do not consent, he is not given a share in what exceeds the one-third according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them, he is given a share for the excess. The three said, so the object of 'does not' is omitted, i.e. he is not given anything in excess over the one for whom he bequeathed one-third. In 'al-Maghrib': 'daraba fi al-jazur' means he participates in the camel and takes a portion. The jurists said: So-and-so participates with one-third, i.e. he takes something by virtue of his right to one-third. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) argument: The bequest is a sibling of inheritance, and the heir participates in the estate, so likewise this. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: The legatee participates according to what he is entitled to, and he is not entitled to beyond one-third except by the consent of the heirs, and it does not exist. However, the Imam (Abu Hanifa) excepted from this ruling the three mentioned scenarios by his saying: 'except in the case of muhabah' etc. The difference for him between these three scenarios and others is that if the bequest is explicitly quantified as exceeding one-third, like half or two-thirds, and the Law invalidates the bequest in the excess, then mentioning it is futile and not considered for participation. Contrary to when it is not quantified, where there is nothing in the expression that invalidates the bequest, as if he bequeaths fifty dirhams and it happens that his wealth is one hundred, then the bequest is not totally invalid because it is possible that his wealth exceeds one hundred, and if it is not totally invalid, it is considered for participation. (Fath) 'That of except in muhabah': i.e. the legatee does not participate with more than one-third if the heirs do not consent except in these three scenarios. The scenario of muhabah: He has two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and one hundred, and the value of the other is six hundred, and he instructed that one of them be sold for one hundred to someone and the other for one hundred to another. Then there is a beneficial sale for one of them of one thousand dirhams, and for the other five hundred. If one-third of his wealth covers it, or the heirs consent, it is permissible. If he has no other wealth besides these two, and the heirs do not consent, their beneficial sale is permissible to the extent of one-third, so the one-third is between them in thirds. The legatee of one thousand participates according to his bequest, which is one thousand, and the other legatee according to his bequest, which is five hundred. If this were like other bequests, it would be necessary that the legatee of one thousand should not participate with more than five hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams according to the Imam, because in his view the legatee of more than one-third does not participate except with one-third, and this is one-third of his wealth. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477] 'And al-sa'yah': The scenario of sa'yah: He bequeaths the emancipation of these two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and the value of the other is two thousand, and he has no other wealth besides them. If the heirs consent, both are freed together. If the heirs do not consent, both are freed from the one-third, and one-third of his wealth is one thousand. Then the one-third from the slave worth one thousand is freed without payment from that amount, which is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and he works for the remainder, which is two-thirds: six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And the two-thirds from the slave worth two thousand is freed without payment from that amount, which is six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, and he works for the remainder, which is one thousand three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams. If this were like other bequests, it would be necessary that the slave worth one thousand should work for five hundred (half his value), and the slave worth two thousand should work for one thousand five hundred (three-quarters of his value), because then the slave worth two thousand does not participate except with one thousand, so it would be necessary that it be half between them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477] 'And al-darahim al-mursalah' etc. [i.e. unspecified as to being one-third, half, or the like. (Ta'i)] The scenario of unspecified dirhams: He bequeaths to one one thousand and to another two thousand, and one-third of his wealth is one thousand, and the heirs do not consent. Then the one-third is between them in thirds; each participates according to his right. So for the legatee of one thousand, his one-third is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and for the legatee of two thousand, his double is six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And the original analogy of Abu Hanifa would require that the one thousand be half between them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/477]
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentaries presents rulings on bequests (wasiyya) involving one-third of the estate when the heirs do not consent to the bequest. The key principle is that without the heirs' consent, only one-third of the testator's wealth can be executed for bequests. The chapter covers multiple beneficiaries with different shares. The first scenario: if two people each receive a bequest of one-third, and the heirs do not consent, the available third is divided equally between them. This is straightforward because their claims are equal. The second scenario: one beneficiary is bequeathed one-third and another one-sixth, the third is divided in a 2:1 ratio, proportional to their claims. The third scenario is more debated: one beneficiary is bequeathed the entire estate and another one-third. When the heirs do not consent, only one-third is available. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the third is divided equally between them. His reasoning: the bequest of the entire estate is void beyond the first third, so it is as if each was bequeathed one-third, resulting in equal shares. The two companions, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, rule that the third is divided in a 3:1 ratio—three-quarters for the one who was to receive all, one-quarter for the one who was to receive one-third. Their reasoning: the testator intended both entitlement and preference; since entitlement to all is prevented by the heirs' right, the preference remains in the available third. Abu Hanifa counters that preference is contingent on entitlement, and since entitlement to the excess is void, so is the preference. The passage then explains a general principle: a legatee does not receive a share in excess of one-third from the available third (Abu Hanifa's view). The two companions disagree, analogizing to inheritance where the heir participates in the whole estate. However, Abu Hanifa makes exceptions for three cases: (1) muhabah (a beneficial sale where the testator sold items below value), (2) sa'yah (bequest of emancipation of slaves, where the freed slaves work to pay off the remaining value), and (3) unspecified dirhams (where the bequest is in absolute terms not tied to a fraction). In these cases, the legatee participates according to the full amount of his bequest, not just one-third, because the bequest is not explicitly exceeding the third or is of a different nature. These exceptions are detailed with specific examples and calculations, showing how the available third is divided proportionally according to each bequest's value. The passage emphasizes the importance of understanding when a bequest is considered void in its excess and when it persists for participation in the third.

Key Terms
المحاباة (al-muhabah): A sale where the testator sells an item at a price significantly below its market value; treated as a constructive bequest of the difference.
السعاية (al-sa'yah): The labor a partially emancipated slave performs to pay off the remaining value after being freed from the bequest.
الدراهم المرسلة (al-darahim al-mursalah): Unspecified dirhams in a bequest, not tied to a fraction of the estate; treated as an absolute amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions, how is the available one-third divided when one legatee is bequeathed all property and another one-third?
A) Equally.
B) 3:1 in favor of the all-property legatee.
C) 1:3 in favor of the third legatee.
D) All to the all-property legatee.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions centers on whether a testator's intention to give preference can survive when the primary entitlement is blocked by law.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest of 'Share of Son' Void; 'Like Share of Son' Valid
Rulings on bequests of son's share vs. like share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest of a son's share versus like a son's share, explain the reasoning, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with Zufar.

Core Idea
Bequeathing a son's share is void; bequeathing 'like' it is valid and gives the legatee a portion equivalent to the son's share.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies a common confusion: a testator cannot bequeath the specific share that his son will inherit, as that would be a bequest of another's property. However, bequeathing an amount 'like' the son's share is valid. The commentator explains the ruling and the logic behind it, including a minority view from Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two phrases
Identify the Arabic phrases 'نصيب ابنه' and 'مثل نصيب ابنه'. Note that 'نصيب' refers to the actual inheritance share while 'مثل' means 'like' or 'equivalent'.
2
Understand the ruling for each
State the ruling: 'نصيب ابنه' is void (باطل) because it is a bequest of what will belong to the son after death. 'مثل نصيب ابنه' is valid (صحيح) because 'like' a thing is different from the thing itself.
3
Apply the ruling to scenarios
If the testator has one son, the bequest of 'like his share' is for half the estate; if two sons, the legatee gets one-third. This respects the testator's intention to make the legatee like one of his sons.
4
Analyze Zufar's opposing view
Zufar argued that bequest of the son's share is valid because at the time of bequest, the property belongs to the testator. The Hanafi response is that the son's share is determined after death, so it is a future right of the son.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that bequest of the son's share is void; bequest of like the son's share is valid and limited to one-third unless heirs approve more.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه و بنصيب ابنه بطل، وبمثل نصيب ابنه صح، فإن كان له ابنان، فله الثلث، وبسهم أو للموصي للموصى له أي لو أوصى بسهم جزء من ماله فالبيان إلى الورثة فإن قال : سدس مالي لفلان، ثم قال: له ثلث مالي مفوض فيعطونه ما شاء أي للموصى الموصى أيضاً مالي، له ثلث ماله وإن قال: سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال له سدس مالي، له السدس. للموصى له وإن أوصى بثلث دراهمه أو غنمه، وهلك ثلثاه، له ما بقي، بطل: هذا إذا كان له ابن وإن لم يكن له ابن فالوصية جائزة، وقال زفر جاز مطلقا؛ لأن الكل ماله في الحال، وذكر نصيب الابن للتقدير، ولنا أن نصيب الابن ما يصيبه بعد الموت، فكان وصية مال الغير، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه؛ لأن مثل الشيء غيره. (عيني، فتح) صح ويكون ذلك وصية بنصف المال إذا كان له ابن واحد، فإن أجازه جاز، وإلا لكان له الثلث. (فتح) فإن كان إلخ : أي فإن كان للموصي ابنان، فللموصى له الثلث، والقياس أن يكون له النصف عند إجازة الورثة؛ لأنه أوصى له بمثل نصيب ابنه، ونصيب كل واحد منهما النصف وجه الأول: أنه قصد أن يجعل له مثل ابنه لا أن يزيد نصيبه على نصيب ابنه، وذلك بأن يجعل الموصى له كأحدهم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢] وفي كلام المصنف تفكيك الضمير، فلو أتى بالظاهر مكان الضمير في قوله: "فله الثلث" بأن قال: فللموصى له الثلث لكان أولى. (فتح) فالبيان إلى الورثة فيقال لهم: أعطوه ما شئتم؛ لأنه مجهول يتناول القليل والكثير والوصية لا تمنع بالجهالة، والورثة قائمون مقام الموصي، فكان إليهم بيانه وسوّى الشيخ ههنا بين السهم والجزء، وهو اختيار بعض المشايخ والمروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن السهم عبارة عن السدس، نقل ذلك عن ابن مسعود له، وفي "المجمع": ولو أوصى : رصى بسهم من ماله فله أخس سهام الورثة عند أبي حنيفة، ولا يزاد على السدس؛ لأن مخرج السدس أعدل المخارج، فلا يتجاوز عنه كما في الإقرار وقالا له أخس سهام الوصايا، إلا أن يزيد على الثلث، فيكون له الثلث؛ لأن محل الوصية الثلث [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢]
The book of bequests. Bequest of a third of wealth and similar. And bequest of the share of his son is void, and bequest of like the share of his son is valid. If he has two sons, then he (the legatee) gets the third. And with 'a share' or 'to the testator for the legatee' meaning if he bequeaths a share, a portion of his wealth, then the explanation is left to the heirs. If he says: one-sixth of my wealth to so-and-so, then says: for him one-third of my wealth, it is delegated, so they give him whatever they wish. Meaning for the legatee, also 'my wealth, for him one-third of his wealth'. And if he says: one-sixth of my wealth to so-and-so, then says for him one-sixth of my wealth, for him is the one-sixth. For the legatee, and if he bequeaths a third of his dirhams or his sheep, and two-thirds perish, he gets what remains. It is void: this is if he has a son. But if he has no son, the bequest is valid. Zufar said: it is valid absolutely, because all of it is his property at present, and mentioning the son's share is for estimation. For us, the son's share is what he gets after death, so it is a bequest of another's property, unlike the case of bequest of like the son's share, because 'like' a thing is other than it. (Ayni, Fath) It is valid, and that bequest is for half the wealth if he has one son. If he permits it, it is permitted; otherwise he gets the third. (Fath) 'If he has' etc.: meaning if the testator has two sons, the legatee gets the third. By analogy, he should get half with the heirs' permission, because he bequeathed to him like the share of his son, and the share of each is half. The first view: he intended to make him like his son, not to increase his share over his son's share, and that is by making the legatee like one of them. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 478/2. In the author's words, there is disconnection of the pronoun. If he had used the explicit instead of the pronoun in his words 'for him is the third' and said 'for the legatee is the third', it would be better. (Fath) So the explanation is left to the heirs: they are told to give him whatever they wish, because it is unknown, including little and much, and a bequest is not prevented by ignorance. The heirs stand in place of the testator, so its explanation is up to them. The Shaykh equated here between 'share' and 'portion', and this is the choice of some mashayikh. The narration from Abu Hanifah: that 'share' means one-sixth, transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud. In al-Majma': 'If he bequeaths a share of his wealth, then he gets the lowest of the heirs' shares according to Abu Hanifah, and it should not exceed the sixth, because the denominator of the sixth is the most balanced denominator, so it is not exceeded just as in iqrar. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he gets the lowest of the bequest shares, unless it exceeds the third, in which case he gets the third, because the place of bequest is the third.' Ramz al-Haqa'iq 478/2.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses multiple rulings on bequests. It begins by distinguishing between two types of bequests: (1) bequeathing the 'share of my son' (نصيب ابنه) which is void because it refers to a specific portion that will belong to the son after death, thus constituting a bequest of another's property. (2) Bequeathing 'like the share of my son' (مثل نصيب ابنه) which is valid because 'like' a thing is something else; it does not refer to the son's actual share but to an equivalent amount. If the testator has one son, the bequest is for half the wealth (since the son's share is half); if the heirs approve, it stands, otherwise the legatee gets one-third (the maximum for a bequest). If the testator has two sons, the legatee gets one-third (since each son's share is half, but the intended meaning is to make the legatee like one of the sons, i.e., an equal sharer, which is one-third of the estate). The text also discusses the ruling on bequeathing 'a share' (سهم) or 'a portion' (جزء). Such a bequest is undefined, and its specification is left to the heirs who may give whatever they wish. The narrator reports that Shaykh al-Islam equated 'share' and 'portion', but the preferred view from Abu Hanifah is that 'share' means one-sixth, based on a transmission from Ibn Mas'ud. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opine that the legatee gets the lowest share among the bequest shares (i.e., the smallest fraction used in bequests, typically one-sixth or less), but not exceeding one-third, as that is the limit for bequests.

Key Terms
نصيب الابن (nasib al-ibn): The actual share of inheritance the son receives.
مثل نصيب الابن (mithl nasib al-ibn): An amount equivalent to the son's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is bequest of 'like the share of my son' valid while bequest of 'the share of my son' is void?
A) Because 'like' indicates a different amount that can be determined.
B) Because 'like' a thing is considered a separate entity from the thing itself.
C) Because the son's share is unknown.
D) Because the testator cannot bequeath property he does not own.

Key Takeaway
Bequeathing the actual share of an heir is void because that share belongs to the heir after death; bequeathing an equivalent is valid.
