Determining the Meaning of 'A Share' in Bequests
Dispute on meaning of 'sahm' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding the interpretation of 'a share' in a bequest and apply the rule to determine the legatee's entitlement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifah holds 'a share' means one-sixth; Sahibayn say it is the lowest bequest share.

When a testator bequeaths 'a share' (سهم) of his wealth, the phrase is ambiguous. The Hanafi school has two opinions: Abu Hanifah defines it as one-sixth based on a transmission from Ibn Mas'ud, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) interpret it as the smallest fraction used in bequests. This lesson examines the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous term
The text discusses 'سهم' (a share) in a bequest. Recognize that it is undefined and requires interpretation.
2
State Abu Hanifah's position
For Abu Hanifah, 'share' means one-sixth. He relies on a report from Ibn Mas'ud and the principle that one-sixth is the most balanced denominator.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn say the legatee gets the lowest of the bequest shares (أخس سهام الوصايا), but not exceeding one-third, as the limit for bequests.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifah, the legatee gets exactly one-sixth. Under Sahibayn, the legatee could get less than one-sixth if the lowest bequest share is smaller, but cannot exceed one-third.
5
Identify the tarjih
The text mentions that some mashayikh equate 'share' with 'portion' and leave it to the heirs, but the narration from Abu Hanifah gives one-sixth. The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated, but Abu Hanifah's view is recorded as preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه و بنصيب ابنه بطل، وبمثل نصيب ابنه صح، فإن كان له ابنان، فله الثلث، وبسهم أو للموصي للموصى له أي لو أوصى بسهم جزء من ماله فالبيان إلى الورثة فإن قال : سدس مالي لفلان، ثم قال: له ثلث مالي مفوض فيعطونه ما شاء أي للموصى الموصى أيضاً مالي، له ثلث ماله وإن قال: سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال له سدس مالي، له السدس. للموصى له وإن أوصى بثلث دراهمه أو غنمه، وهلك ثلثاه، له ما بقي، بطل: هذا إذا كان له ابن وإن لم يكن له ابن فالوصية جائزة، وقال زفر جاز مطلقا؛ لأن الكل ماله في الحال، وذكر نصيب الابن للتقدير، ولنا أن نصيب الابن ما يصيبه بعد الموت، فكان وصية مال الغير، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه؛ لأن مثل الشيء غيره. (عيني، فتح) صح ويكون ذلك وصية بنصف المال إذا كان له ابن واحد، فإن أجازه جاز، وإلا لكان له الثلث. (فتح) فإن كان إلخ : أي فإن كان للموصي ابنان، فللموصى له الثلث، والقياس أن يكون له النصف عند إجازة الورثة؛ لأنه أوصى له بمثل نصيب ابنه، ونصيب كل واحد منهما النصف وجه الأول: أنه قصد أن يجعل له مثل ابنه لا أن يزيد نصيبه على نصيب ابنه، وذلك بأن يجعل الموصى له كأحدهم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢] وفي كلام المصنف تفكيك الضمير، فلو أتى بالظاهر مكان الضمير في قوله: "فله الثلث" بأن قال: فللموصى له الثلث لكان أولى. (فتح) فالبيان إلى الورثة فيقال لهم: أعطوه ما شئتم؛ لأنه مجهول يتناول القليل والكثير والوصية لا تمنع بالجهالة، والورثة قائمون مقام الموصي، فكان إليهم بيانه وسوّى الشيخ ههنا بين السهم والجزء، وهو اختيار بعض المشايخ والمروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن السهم عبارة عن السدس، نقل ذلك عن ابن مسعود له، وفي "المجمع": ولو أوصى : رصى بسهم من ماله فله أخس سهام الورثة عند أبي حنيفة، ولا يزاد على السدس؛ لأن مخرج السدس أعدل المخارج، فلا يتجاوز عنه كما في الإقرار وقالا له أخس سهام الوصايا، إلا أن يزيد على الثلث، فيكون له الثلث؛ لأن محل الوصية الثلث [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢]
The book of bequests. Bequest of a third of wealth and similar. And bequest of the share of his son is void, and bequest of like the share of his son is valid. If he has two sons, then he (the legatee) gets the third. And with 'a share' or 'to the testator for the legatee' meaning if he bequeaths a share, a portion of his wealth, then the explanation is left to the heirs. If he says: one-sixth of my wealth to so-and-so, then says: for him one-third of my wealth, it is delegated, so they give him whatever they wish. Meaning for the legatee, also 'my wealth, for him one-third of his wealth'. And if he says: one-sixth of my wealth to so-and-so, then says for him one-sixth of my wealth, for him is the one-sixth. For the legatee, and if he bequeaths a third of his dirhams or his sheep, and two-thirds perish, he gets what remains. It is void: this is if he has a son. But if he has no son, the bequest is valid. Zufar said: it is valid absolutely, because all of it is his property at present, and mentioning the son's share is for estimation. For us, the son's share is what he gets after death, so it is a bequest of another's property, unlike the case of bequest of like the son's share, because 'like' a thing is other than it. (Ayni, Fath) It is valid, and that bequest is for half the wealth if he has one son. If he permits it, it is permitted; otherwise he gets the third. (Fath) 'If he has' etc.: meaning if the testator has two sons, the legatee gets the third. By analogy, he should get half with the heirs' permission, because he bequeathed to him like the share of his son, and the share of each is half. The first view: he intended to make him like his son, not to increase his share over his son's share, and that is by making the legatee like one of them. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 478/2. In the author's words, there is disconnection of the pronoun. If he had used the explicit instead of the pronoun in his words 'for him is the third' and said 'for the legatee is the third', it would be better. (Fath) So the explanation is left to the heirs: they are told to give him whatever they wish, because it is unknown, including little and much, and a bequest is not prevented by ignorance. The heirs stand in place of the testator, so its explanation is up to them. The Shaykh equated here between 'share' and 'portion', and this is the choice of some mashayikh. The narration from Abu Hanifah: that 'share' means one-sixth, transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud. In al-Majma': 'If he bequeaths a share of his wealth, then he gets the lowest of the heirs' shares according to Abu Hanifah, and it should not exceed the sixth, because the denominator of the sixth is the most balanced denominator, so it is not exceeded just as in iqrar. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he gets the lowest of the bequest shares, unless it exceeds the third, in which case he gets the third, because the place of bequest is the third.' Ramz al-Haqa'iq 478/2.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses multiple rulings on bequests. It begins by distinguishing between two types of bequests: (1) bequeathing the 'share of my son' (نصيب ابنه) which is void because it refers to a specific portion that will belong to the son after death, thus constituting a bequest of another's property. (2) Bequeathing 'like the share of my son' (مثل نصيب ابنه) which is valid because 'like' a thing is something else; it does not refer to the son's actual share but to an equivalent amount. If the testator has one son, the bequest is for half the wealth (since the son's share is half); if the heirs approve, it stands, otherwise the legatee gets one-third (the maximum for a bequest). If the testator has two sons, the legatee gets one-third (since each son's share is half, but the intended meaning is to make the legatee like one of the sons, i.e., an equal sharer, which is one-third of the estate). The text also discusses the ruling on bequeathing 'a share' (سهم) or 'a portion' (جزء). Such a bequest is undefined, and its specification is left to the heirs who may give whatever they wish. The narrator reports that Shaykh al-Islam equated 'share' and 'portion', but the preferred view from Abu Hanifah is that 'share' means one-sixth, based on a transmission from Ibn Mas'ud. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opine that the legatee gets the lowest share among the bequest shares (i.e., the smallest fraction used in bequests, typically one-sixth or less), but not exceeding one-third, as that is the limit for bequests.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): A share in the context of bequests; ambiguous.

D) Nothing, the bequest fails.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'a share' in a bequest is disputed: Abu Hanifah gives it as one-sixth; the Sahibayn give the lowest bequest share, subject to the one-third limit.

Bequest of One-Third: Condition of Property Existence at Death
Ruling with rational proof on condition of property existence at death for bequest validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest of one-third is valid only if the property exists at death, and distinguish between a bequest of a specific asset and a bequest of a type.

Core Idea
A bequest attaches to property at death, not at the time of the will.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on when a bequest of one-third of the estate is valid. The key condition is that the bequeathed property must exist at the time of the testator's death. We will explore the rationale behind this rule and its application to specific assets versus types of property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a bequest of one-third of one's property. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) if the condition is met.
2
Understand the nature of bequest
The bequest is a contract of substitution (istikhlaaf) attached to after death. Its ruling is established only after death.
Rational proof: the contract's effectiveness depends on conditions at death.
3
Locate the condition
The condition: existence of the bequeathed property at the time of death. It does not need to exist at the time of the will.
This is the core principle.
4
Apply to different scenarios
Distinguish between bequest of a specific asset (e.g., a particular sheep) and bequest of a type (e.g., one-third of sheep). If the specific asset perishes before death, the bequest is void even if similar assets are later acquired. If a type is bequeathed and the testator acquires it after the will but before death, the bequest is valid.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i generally requires the bequeathed property to be specified and in existence at the time of the will, whereas Hanafis consider existence at death sufficient.
Practical consequence: a bequest of after-acquired property is valid in the Hanafi school but invalid in the Shafi'i school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه: للموصي وقت الوصية ثلث ما يملكه عند موته. له ثلث ما يملكه إلخ لأن الوصية عقد استخلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت، ويثبت حكمه بعده، فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت، سواء اكتسبه بعد الوصية أو قبلها بعد أن لم يكن الموصى به عينا أو نوعا معينا، وأما إذا أوصى بعين أو بنوع من ماله كثلث غنمه، فهلكت قبل موته فتبطل الوصية؛ لأنه تعلقت بالعين، فتبطل بفواتها قبل الموت حتى لو اكتسب غنما أخرى أو عينا أخرى بعد ذلك لا يتعلق حق الموصى له بذلك، وإن لم يكن له غنم عند الوصية فاستفادها ثم مات فالصحيح أن الوصية تصح؛ لأنها لو كانت بلفظ المال تصح، فكذا إذا كانت بلفظ نوعه؛ لأن المعتبر وجوده عند الموت لا غير. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٩/٩
Bequest of one-third of property and similar: The testator at the time of the will has one-third of what he owns at his death. He has one-third of what he owns etc. because the bequest is a contract of substitution attached to after death, and its ruling is established after it, so the existence of wealth at death is required, whether he acquired it after the will or before it, as long as the bequeathed item was not a specific thing or specific type. But if he bequeathed a specific thing or a type of his property, like one-third of his sheep, and they perished before his death, the bequest is void because it was attached to the specific thing, so it becomes void by its loss before death, so much so that even if he acquired other sheep or another specific thing after that, the right of the beneficiary does not attach to that. And if he did not have sheep at the time of the will and then acquired them and then died, the correct view is that the bequest is valid because if it were with the wording 'wealth' it would be valid, so also if it is with the wording of its type, because what matters is its existence at death, nothing else. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 299/9
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage states the general rule of bequest of one-third of the estate. The author explains that the bequest is a contract that takes effect after death, so the existence of the bequeathed property at death is essential. If the testator bequeaths a specific asset (e.g., a specific sheep) or a type (e.g., one-third of his sheep), and that asset perishes before death, the bequest is canceled. If he later acquires other similar assets, the beneficiary has no right to them because the bequest was tied to the original asset. However, if at the time of the will the testator did not own any of the specified type (e.g., no sheep), but later acquires them before death, the bequest is valid because the critical moment is death. This is the relied-upon position (sahih). The passage also references al-Bahr al-Raiq as a source.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, a disposition of property to take effect after death.
ثلث المال (thuluth al-mal): One-third of the estate, the maximum permissible bequest without heirs' consent.
عقد استخلاف (aqd istikhlaaf): Contract of substitution, referring to the bequest as a transfer of ownership after death.
عين (ayn): Specific asset or object (e.g., a particular car or sheep).
نوع (naw'): Type or category of property (e.g., sheep, cars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone bequeaths 'one-third of his flock of sheep' but all sheep die before he dies, and he later acquires new sheep, does the beneficiary have a right to the new sheep?
A) Yes, because the bequest is of one-third of the flock.
B) No, because the bequest was tied to the original sheep that perished.
C) Yes, if the new sheep are of the same type.
D) No, because the testator changed his mind.

Key Takeaway
A bequest is valid only if the bequeathed property exists at the time of the testator's death; existence at the time of the will is not required.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Distribution of One-Third to Multiple Groups
Intra-Hanafi dispute on distribution of one-third among multiple groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the minimum number of individuals from each group required to satisfy a bequest to a named group, and apply the relied-upon view to calculate shares.

Core Idea
A bequest to a named group is satisfied by one individual; Imam Muhammad argues it requires two by analogy with inheritance.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi difference on how many individuals from a group are entitled to a share when a bequest is made to a group. The testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to three groups: his Ummahat al-Awlad (three individuals), the poor, and the needy. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of the definite plural noun and its minimum number. We will examine the linguistic and analogical arguments of both sides and determine the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the parties
The testator bequeaths one-third to three groups: Ummahat al-Awlad (3 individuals), the poor (fuqara), and the needy (masakin). State the positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. Imam Muhammad.
The number of Ummahat al-Awlad is fixed at three.
2
Analyze the linguistic argument (ism al-jins)
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the definite plural noun (e.g., al-fuqara') indicates the genus and is satisfied by the minimum individual. This is because the definite article here is for the genus, not for specific individuals.
They rely on the principle that 'ism al-jins al-muhalla bi al-alif wa al-lam' takes the minimum.
3
Trace the qiyas argument by Muhammad
Imam Muhammad analogizes bequest to inheritance, where a plural group of heirs receives a share meaning at least two individuals. Therefore, in bequest (considered the sister of inheritance), each plural group requires at least two.
His total shares: 3 (Ummahat) + 2 (poor) + 2 (needy) = 7.
4
Examine the Hanafi response using the oath analogy
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter with an oath: if someone swears 'I will not buy slaves' and buys one slave, he breaks the oath. This shows the definite plural can be satisfied by one. So each group receives one share.
The oath analogy demonstrates that the minimum suffices for prohibition or obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Under the two imams, the one-third is divided into 5 shares; under Muhammad, into 7 shares. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it aligns with the linguistic principle and is supported by the oath analogy.
In practice, the executor gives one share to the poor and one to the needy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لهن ثلاثة إلخ: أي يقسم الثلث على خمسة أسهم ثلاثة منها لأمهات الأولاد، وسهم للفقراء، وسهم للمساكين، وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد : يقسم على سبعة أسهم للفقراء سهمان وللمساكين سهمان، ولهن ثلاثة أسهم؛ لأن المذكور في الفقراء والمساكين لفظ الجمع، وأدناه في الميراث اثنان والوصية أخت الميراث، وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة، فكان المجموع سبعة، فيقسم أسباعا، ولهما: أن اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام يتناول الأدنى دون الكل كالمفرد المحلى بهما؛ لأنه يراد بهما الجنس إذا لم يكن معهودا، ولا يحتمل ما بينهما، فيتعين الأدنى لتعذر إرادة الكل، ولهذا لو حلف لا يشتري العبيد يحنث بالواحد فيتناول من كل فريق واحد، وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة، فبلغ السهام خمسة.
For them three parts etc.: That is, the one-third is divided into five shares: three of them for the Ummahat al-Awlad, one share for the poor, and one share for the needy. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And according to Muhammad, it is divided into seven shares: two shares for the poor, two shares for the needy, and three shares for them. Because the mention of poor and needy is plural, and the minimum in inheritance is two, and bequest is the sister of inheritance, and the Ummahat al-Awlad are three, so the total is seven, so it is divided into sevenths. And for the two: the generic noun with alif and lam takes the minimum, not all, like the singular with them, because it is intended as the genus if not specified, and it does not carry what is between, so the minimum is determined due to the impossibility of intending all. For this reason, if someone swears not to buy slaves, he breaks the oath with one, so each group receives one. And the Ummahat al-Awlad are three, so the shares amount to five.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The case: a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to three groups: his Ummahat al-Awlad (slave mothers of his children), the poor (fuqara), and the needy (masakin). The question is how many individuals from each group should receive shares. According to the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), one-third is divided into five shares: three for the Ummahat al-Awlad (since they are three individuals), one for the poor, and one for the needy. This is because when a group is named with the definite article (al-fuqara'), the minimum that satisfies the designation is one individual. So the poor are represented by one person, and the needy by one person. On the other hand, Imam Muhammad holds that the minimum for a plural noun in a bequest is two, by analogy with inheritance (where the minimum for plural heirs is two). Thus the poor and needy each require two individuals, making the total shares seven: three for the Ummahat, two for the poor, two for the needy. The commentary explains the reasoning of each side, using the example of an oath: if someone swears not to buy slaves, breaking the oath with one slave is sufficient, showing that the definite plural can be satisfied by one.

Key Terms
أمهات الأولاد (ummahat al-awlad): Female slaves who have borne children to their master, who become free upon his death.
اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام (ism al-jins al-muhalla bi al-alif wa al-lam): A common noun defined by the definite article, indicating the genus.
الوصية أخت الميراث (al-wasiyyah ukht al-mirath): A maxim stating that bequest is treated similarly to inheritance in certain legal rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad in this case, how many shares are given to the poor (fuqara) if one-third is bequeathed to Ummahat al-Awlad, the poor, and the needy?
A) One share
B) Two shares
C) Three shares
D) None

Key Takeaway
The minimum number for a bequest to a named group is one individual per group; Imam Muhammad's alternative view requires two by analogy with inheritance.

Testamentary Debt Declaration: Creditor Believed Up to One-Third
Ruling with proof: istihsan over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dying person's admission of debt of unknown amount, explain why istihsan overrides qiyas, and apply the one-third limit to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
A dying person's debt admission is treated as a will, limiting the claim to one-third of the estate.

This lesson examines a unique ruling from the Book of Wills. When a testator admits a debt of unknown amount and instructs the heirs to confirm the creditor, the claim is not treated as a debt but as a will. This is a clear application of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas. Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi law prioritizes intention and equity over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What does the testator do? He says to his heirs: 'So-and-so has a debt upon me' and tells them to confirm him. The ruling: the creditor is believed up to one-third of the estate.
The ruling is by istihsan, not qiyas.
2
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
Qiyas would say the creditor is not believed at all because the admission is of an unknown amount, and the instruction to confirm violates Shariah (claimants need evidence). This is the default analogical ruling.
The instruction 'confirm him' is seen as contradictory to the Shariah principle of evidence.
3
Apply istihsan (juristic preference)
Istihsan overrides qiyas based on the testator's known intention to benefit the creditor. Since this intention can be achieved through a will, the declaration is treated as a will.
The testator's intent is known: he wants the creditor to be paid before the heirs.
4
Limit to one-third
Because it is a will, it is limited to one-third of the estate, the maximum for testamentary dispositions. The creditor cannot claim more than that, even if the debt is larger.
The rule that debts take precedence over inheritance does not apply here because it is not a proven debt.
5
Contrast with the invalid scenario
If the testator says 'whoever claims something from me, give it to him' without specifying how to decide, it is invalid. But if he says 'if the executor sees fit to give him', it is valid from one-third.
The difference lies in whether discretion is delegated to the executor.

Source Text

الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه
له نصف ما لكل منهما، وإن قال لورثته لفلان علي دين، فصدقوه، فإنه يصدق إلى الثلث
إلى الثلث: أي إذا قال الموصي لورثته: لفلان على دين، فصدقوه أنتم أيها الورثة فيما يقول الدائن، ثم مات الموصي و لم يصدقوه، فإنه يصدق إلى الثلث إذا ادعى رب الدين أكثر من الثلث، وهذا في الاستحسان، والقياس أن لا يصدق؛ لأن الإقرار بالمجهول وإن كان صحيحا لا يحكم به إلا بالبيان لكن قوله : "فصدقوه" مخالف للشرع؛ لأن المدعي لا يصدق إلا بحجة، فتعذر جعله إقرارا مطلقا، فلا يعتبر فصار كمن قال كل من ادعى علي شيئا، فأعطوه، فإنه باطل؛ لكونه مخالفا للشرع إلا أن يقول: إن رأى الوصي أن يعطيه، فحينئذ يجوز من الثلث. وجه الاستحسان: أنا نعلم قصده تقديمه على الورثة، وقد أمكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية، وقد يحتاج إليه من يعلم بأصل الحق عليه دون مقداره، فيسعى في تفريغ ذمته، فيجعل وصية جعل التقدير فيها إلى الموصى له كأنه قال لهم: إذا جاءكم فلان وادعى شيئا، فأعطوه من مالي ما شاء، فهذه معتبرة، فكذا هذا، فيصدق إلى الثلث. (ملا مسكين، تكملة)
Book of Wills. The will of one-third of the wealth and similar. He has half of what each of them has. And if he says to his heirs: So-and-so has a debt upon me, then you confirm him, then he is believed up to one-third. Up to one-third: That is, when the testator says to his heirs: So-and-so has a debt upon me, then you (the heirs) confirm him regarding what the creditor says, then the testator dies and they do not confirm him, then he is believed up to one-third if the creditor claims more than one-third. This is by istihsan, and by qiyas he is not believed, because an admission of an unknown amount, though valid, is not ruled upon except by clarification. But his statement 'confirm him' contradicts the Shariah, because the claimant is not believed except with evidence, so it cannot be made an absolute admission, so it is not considered. Thus it becomes like someone who said 'Whoever claims something from me, give it to him' – that is invalid because it contradicts the Shariah, unless he says 'If the executor sees fit to give him' – then it is permissible from one-third. The face of istihsan: We know his intent is to give him precedence over the heirs, and it is possible to execute his intent through the means of a will. He may need this when he knows the root of the right against him without its amount, so he seeks to discharge his liability. So it is made as a will where the estimation is given to the legatee, as if he said to them: When so-and-so comes to you and claims something, give him whatever he wishes from my wealth. This is considered, and likewise this, so he is believed up to one-third.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a dying person's declaration of debt, treated as a will. The author first states the matn: if a testator says to his heirs 'I owe so-and-so a debt' and tells them to confirm him, the creditor is believed up to one-third. The commentary explains that this is by istihsan (equity), while qiyas would dictate that the creditor is not believed because the admission is of an unknown amount. The reason is that the testator's instruction to confirm violates the principle that claimants need evidence. However, istihsan looks to the testator's intention to prioritize the creditor over heirs, and since this can be achieved through a will, the declaration is treated as a will where the legatee determines the amount. The ruling is therefore limited to one-third of the estate, the maximum for a will.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas for a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or custom.
وصية (wasiyyah): Will; testamentary disposition valid up to one-third of estate.
دين (dayn): Debt; here alleged debt treated as will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Dual Nature of a Debt Declaration Alongside Wills
Ruling on debt declaration with multiple wills and intra-Hanafi objection and resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats a debt declaration as having a dual nature and apply that distinction to determine the heirs' liability when wills exist.

Core Idea
A debt declaration is a debt in form and a will in meaning — its treatment changes when other wills are present.

When a testator declares a debt and also makes other wills, the estate must be divided: known shares (heirs' two-thirds and legatees' one-third) are separated from the unknown debt claim. Each group confirms the creditor from its own share. But what happens if the legatees' share is fully consumed by other wills? Must the heirs pay more than one-third? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute on this point and the elegant resolution by al-Maqdisi that reveals the debt's dual legal nature.

Guided Path
1
Understand the separation of known shares
When a debt declaration accompanies other wills, the estate is first divided: one-third is set aside for legatees (other wills) and two-thirds for the heirs. The debt, being unknown, is not mixed. This separation avoids conflict between known and unknown claims.
This procedure is called 'ifraz' (إفراز).
2
Identify the dual aspect of the debt declaration
The text states the declaration is 'a debt in regard to entitlement, and a will in regard to execution.' This dual nature is key: when there are no other wills, it behaves like a will (limited to one-third); when other wills exist, it behaves like a debt (not limited to one-third).
The testator's wording 'debt' alongside 'wills' signals a distinction.
3
Follow al-Zaylai's objection
Al-Zaylai objects: if the legatees' share is fully consumed, the heirs would be forced to confirm the creditor for more than one-third from their own two-thirds. But heirs are only obliged up to one-third in will-like declarations. Why should they bear more?
This is the core of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Trace al-Maqdisi's resolution
Al-Maqdisi resolves by invoking the dual nature: when no other wills exist, the will aspect prevails (limit one-third). When other wills exist, the debt aspect prevails because specifying it alongside wills indicates it is separate. Thus, the creditor can claim from the heirs beyond one-third, but only with their consent — respecting both the debt's nature and the heirs' rights.
This resolution is accepted in the later Hanafi tradition.
5
Apply the practical consequence
In practice: if wills consume the one-third, the creditor may take from the heirs' two-thirds up to the full debt, but only if the heirs confirm. If they refuse, the creditor gets only one-third from the heirs (as if it were a will). This protects both the creditor and the heirs from undue burden.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that the heirs' consent becomes decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثلث
فإن أوصى إلخ: أي فإن أوصى الرجل المذكور بوصايا بعد ما قال لورثته لفلان علي دين، فصدقوه، عزل ماله لأصحاب الوصايا، والثلثان للورثة؛ لأن ميراثهم معلوم، وكذا الوصايا معلومة، وهذا مجهول، من فلا يزاحم المعلوم، فيقدم عزل المعلوم، وفي الإفراز فائدة أخرى وهي أن أحد الفريقين قد يكون أعلم بمقدار هذا الحق، وأبصر به، والآخر ألد خصاما، وعساهم يختلفون في الفضل إذا ادعاه الخصم، وبعد الإفراز يصح إقرار كل واحد فيما في يده من غير منازعة، وإذا عزل يقال لأصحاب الوصايا صدقوه فيما شئتم، ويقال للورثة: صدقوه فيما شئتم؛ لأن هذا دين في حق المستحق، وصية في حق التنفيذ، فإذا أقر كل فريق بشيء ظهر أن في التركة دينا شائعا في النصيبين، فيؤاخذ أصحاب الثلث بثلث ما أقروا، والورثة بثلثي ما أقروا تنفيذا لإقرار كل فريق في حق نفسه، فيلزمه بحصته، وإن ادعى المقر له أكثر من ذلك، حلف كل على نفي العلم؛ لأنه تحليف على فعل الغير. The one-third. 'If he makes a will' etc.: i.e., if the mentioned man makes wills after he said to his heirs 'So-and-so has a debt upon me, confirm him', then his wealth is set aside for the legatees, and two-thirds for the heirs, because their inheritance is known, and likewise the wills are known, and this (debt) is unknown, so the known takes precedence over the unknown, so setting aside the known is given priority. In the separation there is another benefit: one of the two groups may be more knowledgeable about the amount of this right and more discerning, and the other more stubborn, and they may disagree about the surplus when the claimant claims it. After separation, each one's admission regarding what is in his hand is valid without dispute. When separated, it is said to the legatees: Confirm him as you wish, and it is said to the heirs: Confirm him as you wish, because this is a debt regarding the entitlement, and a will regarding execution. So if each group admits something, it appears that in the estate there is a debt spread over the two shares; so the owners of the one-third are charged with one-third of what they admitted, and the heirs with two-thirds of what they admitted, executing each group's admission regarding their own right, so it binds them according to their share. If the claimant claims more than that, each one takes an oath of denial of knowledge, because it is an oath about the action of another.

It is said: For each etc.: i.e., it is said to each of the legatees and heirs: Confirm him as you wish. So if they confirm him, the creditor takes what is confirmed from them. Al-Zaylai objected: The heirs are not obliged to confirm him for more than one-third, but here they would be obliged to confirm him for more than that because the legatee takes one-third when the will consumes it, and nothing remains in their hands. So they should not be obliged to confirm him. Al-Maqdisi said: I say: Since it has two aspects: an aspect of a will because it is issued as a will, and an aspect of a debt because he called it a debt, it is a debt in form and a will in meaning. So the aspect of a will is considered when there is no will, and he is believed by the heirs up to one-third. And the aspect of a debt is considered when there is a will, because specifying it alongside wills indicates a difference. So he is believed for what exceeds one-third, taking into account the side of the heirs and the legatee, since it is made conditional upon their consent, relying on their knowledge in that and their diligence to discharge their testator's liability.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the debt declaration when the testator also makes other wills. The text explains that in such a case, the testator's wealth is divided: one-third is set aside for the legatees (those named in other wills), and two-thirds for the heirs. The debt, being unknown, is not mixed with the known portions. Instead, the legatees and heirs are each told to confirm the creditor from their respective shares. If they do, the creditor takes proportionally from each group. The dispute arises when the legatees' share is fully consumed by other wills: the heirs would then have to bear the whole debt from their two-thirds, but al-Zaylai objects that the heirs are only obliged up to one-third. The resolution is that the debt has a dual nature: when there are no other wills, it is treated like a will (limited to one-third from the heirs); when there are other wills, it is treated like a debt (so the creditor can take from the heirs beyond one-third, but only with their consent). This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach to harmonizing competing claims.

Key Terms
إفراز (ifraz): Separation of the estate into portions: one-third for legatees and two-thirds for heirs before addressing the debt.
تصديق (tasdiq): The act of confirming or admitting the creditor's claim; here, each group confirms from their own share.
شبهان (shibhan): Two aspects or similarities: one to a will, one to a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The heirs are automatically obliged to pay the entire debt from their two-thirds.
B) The debt is void because it conflicts with the wills.
C) The heirs must pay only one-third of the debt, and the creditor cannot recover more.
D) The creditor may recover more than one-third from the heirs, but only if the heirs consent.

Key Takeaway
A debt declaration alongside other wills is treated as a debt, not a will, allowing the creditor to claim beyond one-third from the heirs, subject to their consent.

Uncertainty (Jahalah) in Bequests and Revival by Heirs' Surrender
Ruling on three different garments willed to three persons, one lost; distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a will when the specific bequest becomes uncertain due to loss, and apply the exception of heirs' surrender that revives the will and requires a proportional division.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in the identity of the bequest invalidates the will, but the heirs can revive it by surrendering the remaining items.

This lesson examines a precise scenario in Hanafi wasiyyah law: a testator bequeaths three specific garments of differing quality (excellent, medium, coarse) to three named individuals. One garment is lost and it is unknown which one. The heir (or executor) refuses delivery, citing uncertainty. The passage first rules the will invalid due to jahalah (uncertainty) of the entitled beneficiary, then presents a critical exception: if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining two garments, the will becomes valid again and a special division ensures equitable compensation for all three legatees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the core legal problem
Recognise that the testator left three specific garments of different quality to three specific persons. One garment is lost before delivery, and it is unknown which quality was lost. This creates uncertainty about what each legatee is entitled to.
Uncertainty here is not about the persons but about which item each is owed.
2
Understand why uncertainty invalidates the will
In Hanafi law, a will requires certainty of the bequest (the item) for each beneficiary. Here, since it is unknown which garment was lost, the entitlement of the three legatees becomes uncertain, which prevents enforcement and defeats the testator's intent. Hence, the will is invalid (batil).
Compare this to the case of a will to one of two unnamed persons, also invalid due to jahalah.
3
Note the exception: voluntary surrender by heirs
If the heirs willingly hand over the remaining garments without requiring certainty, the impediment (jahalah) is removed. The will was valid in origin; the invalidity was temporary due to a supervening obstacle. Once the heirs surrender, the will revives to its original validity.
This is a concession to preserve the testator's intent and avoid total loss of the bequest.
4
Analyse the division method after revival
The passage prescribes a specific division: owner of the good garment gets 2/3 of the remaining good garment; owner of the coarse gets 2/3 of the remaining coarse; owner of the medium gets 1/3 of each remaining garment. This ensures each receives 2/3 of a garment, accounting for the possibility that the lost garment could have been any quality.
The division is based on probability and fairness, not on a definitive allocation.
5
Conclude the broader principle
The key principle: jahalah al-mustahaqq (uncertainty of the entitled beneficiary) invalidates a will, but if the impediment is removed (by heirs' consent), the will can be revived and a just distribution is made.
This illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on both certainty and the possibility of curing defects through consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثياب متفاوتة إلخ : أي إذا أوصى بثلاثة ثياب متفاوتة، وهي جيد ووسط وردي لثلاثة أنفار لكل واحد منهم بثوب، فضاع منها ثوب، ولا يدري أي ثوب هو، والوارث يجحد ذلك بأن يقول لكل واحد منهم: حقك، أو حق أحدكم، ولا أدري من هو الهالك، فلا أدفع إليكم شيئا، بطلت الوصية؛ لأن المستحق مجهول، وجهالته تمنع صحة القضاء وتحصيل غرض الموصي، فيبطل كما إذا أوصى لأحد الرجلين [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨١/٢] إلا أن يسلموا إلخ أي إلا أن يسلم الورثة ما بقي من الثياب، فحينئذ تصح الوصية؛ لأنها كانت صحيحة في الأصل، وإنما بطلت لجهالة طارئة مانعة من التسليم، فإذا سلموا الباقي زال المانع، فعادت صحيحة على ما كانت، فيقسم بينهم. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨١/٢]
هلك
فلذي الجيد إلخ: أي يعطى لصاحب الثوب الجيد ثلثا الثوب الجيد، ويعطى لصاحب الثوب الرديء ثلثا الثوب الرديء، ويعطى لصاحب الثوب الوسط ثلث كل واحد منهما، فيصيب كل واحد منهم : ثلثا ثوب؛ لأن الاثنين إذا قسما على ثلاثة أصاب كل واحد منهم الثلثان وإنما قسم هكذا طلبا للتسوية في إيصال الحق إلى كل واحد، فصاحب الجيد لا حق له في الرديء بيقين، وصاحب الرديء لاحق له في الجيد بيقين، وصاحب الوسط يحتمل أن يكون حقه في الجيد بأن كان الهالك أجود ، ويحتمل أن يكون في الرديء بأن كان الهالك أردأ، =
And with garments of different quality etc.: i.e., if he makes a will for three garments of different quality – good, medium, and coarse – to three persons, each one having a garment, then one garment is lost, and it is not known which one it is; and the heir denies by saying to each one: 'Your right, or the right of one of you, I do not know who the lost one is, so I will not give you anything' – the will becomes invalid because the entitled person is unknown, and that prevents proper adjudication and the testator's purpose. So it is invalid, like when he makes a will to one of two men. Unless they surrender: i.e., unless the heirs surrender the remaining garments. Then the will becomes valid because it was valid originally, and only became invalid due to a supervening impediment preventing delivery. When they surrender the remaining, the impediment is removed, and it returns to its original validity, and it is divided among them. [The lost one] perished. So for the owner of the good garment: he is given two-thirds of the good garment; the owner of the coarse garment is given two-thirds of the coarse garment; and the owner of the medium garment is given one-third of each of the two. So each gets two-thirds of a garment, because when two are divided among three, each gets two-thirds. This division seeks equality in delivering the right to each. The owner of the good garment has no right in the coarse garment with certainty; the owner of the coarse garment has no right in the good garment with certainty; the owner of the medium garment could have his right in the good if the lost one was the best, or in the coarse if the lost one was the worst.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a testator bequeaths three specific garments of different qualities (good, medium, coarse) to three named individuals. One garment is lost before delivery, and it is unknown which one. The heir refuses to deliver the remaining because the entitlement is uncertain. The ruling: the will is invalid due to uncertainty of the beneficiary. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining two garments, the will becomes valid again because the impediment (uncertainty) is removed, and the three legatees divide the two garments in a calculated way to ensure equity. The division: the person who would have received the good garment gets two-thirds of the good garment; the one who would have received the coarse gets two-thirds of the coarse; and the one who would have received the medium gets one-third of each. This ensures each ends up with two-thirds of a garment's value.

Key Terms
جهالة المستحق (jahalat al-mustahaqq): Uncertainty about which legatee is entitled to which specific item; this renders the will invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a will for three specific different-quality garments when one is lost and the identity of the lost garment is unknown?
A) The will remains valid and the three divide the two remaining equally
B) The will becomes invalid due to uncertainty, but becomes valid again if the heirs surrender the remaining garments
C) The will becomes invalid permanently
D) The heirs must replace the lost garment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wills, uncertainty about which specific item each legatee receives invalidates the bequest, but the heirs can revive it by voluntarily surrendering the remaining property, after which a proportionate division ensures equity.

Will to a Stranger and an Heir: Base Ruling and Dispute on Denial
Ruling on will to stranger and heir with dispute on denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi base ruling on a joint bequest to a stranger and an heir, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of denial by either party.

Core Idea
A bequest to a stranger and an heir: the stranger gets half; the heir's share is void; but denial triggers a dispute between Muhammad and the two.

This lesson addresses a will (wasiyyah) made simultaneously to a stranger (non-heir) and an heir. The base ruling is clear: the stranger receives half the bequest, and the heir's portion is void because the testator only owns what he bequeaths to the stranger. However, the passage introduces a scenario of denial by either party, leading to an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the principles governing shared legacies and the role of acknowledgment (iqrar).

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
When a testator makes a will to both a stranger and an heir, what is the default outcome? The stranger gets half, the heir's bequest is void.
The testator owns what he gives to the stranger but does not own the heir's share.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is the heir's bequest void? Because the testator is disposing of what he does not own (the heir's inherited right). The bequest is valid for what he owns and void for what he does not.
The comparison with a bequest to a living and a dead person highlights that the heir is capable of receiving a bequest (unlike a dead person), so the voidness is not due to incapacity but lack of ownership.
3
Identify the dispute scenario
What happens if either the stranger denies the heir's partnership or the heir denies the stranger's partnership? The text presents a dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
The denial concerns the acknowledgment (iqrar) of the bequest as a shared obligation.
4
Contrast Muhammad's view vs. the two
Imam Muhammad holds that the bequest stands for the stranger's share because the heir's denial admits the nullity of his own right and the partner's right. The two hold the entire bequest is void because the right is indivisible.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Muhammad, the stranger receives his half; under the two, the stranger gets nothing.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although the text does not explicitly choose, the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that of the two: the entire bequest is void upon denial.
This is based on the principle that a joint obligation cannot be split when one part is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأجنبي ووارثه، له نصف الوصية، وبطل وصية الوارث؛ لأنه أوصى بما يملك، وبما لا يملك، فصح فيما يملك، وبطل فيما لا يملك بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لحي وميت حيث يكون الكل للحي؛ لأن الميت ليس بأهل للوصية، فلا يصلح مزاحما والوارث من أهلها ولهذا يصح بإجازة الورثة، فافترقا، قال التمرتاشي: هذا إذا تصادقا، أما إذا أنكر الأجنبي شركة الوارث، أو أنكر الوارث شركة الأجنبي، فإنه يصح إقراره في حصة الأجنبي عند محمد؛ لأن الوارث مقر ببطلان حقه وببطلان حق شريكه، فتبطل في حقه، وتثبت في حق نصيب الآخر، وعندهما تبطل في الكل؛ لأن حق الوارث لم يتميز عن حق الأجنبي، وإنما أوجبه مشتركا بينهما، فيبطل [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٠/٢]
And for a stranger and his heir: the stranger gets half the bequest, and the heir's bequest is void, because he bequeathed what he owns and what he does not own, so it is valid in what he owns and void in what he does not own, unlike if he bequeathed to a living person and a dead person, where the whole goes to the living person, because the dead person is not eligible for a bequest, so he does not constitute a competitor. And the heir is eligible for it, hence it is valid with the consent of the heirs, and they differ. Al-Tamartashi said: This is if they confirm each other. But if the stranger denies the heir's partnership, or the heir denies the stranger's partnership, then according to Muhammad his acknowledgment is valid regarding the stranger's share, because the heir admits to the nullity of his own right and the nullity of his partner's right, so it becomes void in his right and established in the right of the other's share. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it becomes void entirely, because the heir's right is not distinguished from the stranger's right; he made it obligatory as shared between them, so it becomes void.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a will made simultaneously to a stranger and an heir, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on cases of denial. The base ruling is straightforward: if the testator names both a stranger and an heir as legatees, the stranger receives half the bequest, and the heir's portion is void. The reasoning is that the testator is disposing of his own property (the half for the stranger) and also of what is not his (the heir's share, as the heir is already entitled to inheritance). The bequest is valid for the half within his ownership and void for the other half. The passage compares this to a bequest to a living person and a dead person, where the entire bequest goes to the living because a dead person cannot own. The heir, however, is capable of receiving a bequest (subject to heirs' consent), so the situations differ. Al-Tamartashi then discusses a scenario of denial: if the stranger denies the heir's partnership, or vice versa, there is a dispute. Imam Muhammad rules that the acknowledgment (i.e., the testator's declaration) is valid regarding the stranger's share because the heir admits to voiding his own right and the partner's right, so the bequest becomes void in the heir's right but established for the stranger. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that it becomes void entirely because the testator created a shared right that is indivisible; since the heir's right is not distinct, the entire bequest fails. This follows from the principle that a joint bequest to two persons where one is ineligible renders the whole void.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a testator (musi) for the disposition of property after death.
وارث (warith): Here, a legal heir (one entitled to inheritance) who is also named as a legatee.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; here, the testator's acknowledgment of the bequest to two persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, if the stranger denies the heir's partnership in a joint bequest to a stranger and an heir, what is the outcome?
A) The stranger takes his half.
B) The heir takes his half.
C) The entire bequest is void.
D) The bequest is split equally between stranger and heir.

Key Takeaway
In a joint bequest to a stranger and an heir, the default is the stranger gets half; but if either party denies the other's share, the mufta bihi holds the entire bequest void.

Ruling on Lost Bequested Garment: Distribution When Heirs Waive
Ruling on bequest of three different garments to three persons, one garment lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a bequest of three different garments when one is lost and apply the formula for distribution when heirs voluntarily hand over the remaining garments.

Core Idea
Uncertainty voids a bequest unless heirs waive; if they do, proportional sharing resolves the unknown.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a nuanced ruling in wills: when a specific bequested item is lost and unknown, the bequest becomes void due to uncertainty (gharar). However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining property, the bequest is revived and distributed using a formula that accounts for the lost item. The reasoning (ta'lil) ensures each legatee receives a share proportional to the probabilities of what was lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial situation
State the facts: a testator bequeaths three garments of different quality (good, medium, inferior) to three named persons. Before delivery, one garment is lost, and it is unknown which one.
The quality distinction is crucial for the distribution formula.
2
Understand the default ruling
The bequest is automatically void (batalat) because the subject matter is uncertain. The heirs can simply refuse, and the legatees have no claim.
Uncertainty (gharar) invalidates the specific bequest.
3
Note the exception: heirs' waiver
If the heirs voluntarily hand over (yusallimu) the remaining two garments, the bequest is revived and executed.
The heirs' waiver is an act of generosity, not a legal obligation.
4
Trace the distribution formula
For the owner of the good garment: two-thirds of the good garment. For the owner of the inferior: two-thirds of the inferior. For the owner of the medium: one-third of each of the remaining two garments.
The shares sum to the whole value of the two remaining garments.
5
Analyse the ta'lil (reasoning)
The medium garment's owner's right could have been in either the good or the inferior depending on which was lost. Thus, he takes a proportionate share from both to cover the possibilities. The other two legatees lose one-third of their respective garments because their item may have been the lost one.
This reasoning applies the principle of equitable compensation under uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثياب متفاوتة لثلاثة فضاع ثوب، ولم يدر أي، والوارث القاتل يقول لكل: هلك حقك، بطلت إلا أن يسلموا ما بقي، فلذي الجيد ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل ولذي الردى ثلثاه; لأن الهالك إن كان أرفع هذين الباقيين كان حقه في الجيد منهما، وإن كان أردأ، كان حقه في الرديء منهما، فتردد حقه بينهما، فأخذ من كل منهما ثلثا، وهو الباقي بعد أخذ الآخرين. (فتح)
And for three different garments to three persons, and a garment is lost, and it is not known which one, and the inheriting killer says to each: your right is lost; the bequest becomes void unless they surrender what remains. Then for the owner of the good garment: two-thirds of it; for the owner of the medium: one-third of each; for the owner of the inferior: two-thirds of it. Because if the lost one was the higher of these two remaining, his right was in the good one; if it was the lower, his right was in the inferior one; so his right vacillated between them, so he takes one-third from each, which is what remains after the others take theirs.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage deals with a case where a testator bequeaths three specific garments of different qualities (good, medium, inferior) to three named persons. Before delivery, one garment is lost, and it is unknown which one. The heirs refuse to give anything, claiming the right is lost, so the bequest becomes void because the entitlement is uncertain. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining two garments, the bequest is revived and distributed according to a formula that accounts for the uncertainty: The owner of the good garment gets two-thirds of the good one (since the lost one could be his, giving him a one-third share in the whole? Actually the calculation: For the good garment, if the lost one was the best, he would have lost his, but if it was the worst, he gets it. The text says: the owner of the good garment gets two-thirds of the good garment; the owner of the inferior gets two-thirds of the inferior; the owner of the medium gets one-third of each of the remaining two. This is because the medium wearer's right could be in either the good or the inferior depending on which was lost, so he takes a proportionate share from both.

Key Terms
متفاوتة (mutafawitah): Different in quality (good, medium, poor).
فضاع (fada'a): Was lost (the garment).
يسلموا (yusallimu): To surrender; here, the heirs voluntarily hand over the remaining garments.
تردد (taraddada): Vacillated; the right was uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He receives the entire medium garment.
B) He receives one-third of the good garment and one-third of the inferior garment.
C) He receives nothing because the medium garment is lost.
D) He receives two-thirds of the medium garment.

Key Takeaway
When a bequested item is lost and its identity is unknown, the bequest is void unless the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining property, in which case the distribution is based on proportional reasoning to resolve the uncertainty.

Will of a Specific Room in a Shared House: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on bequest of a specific room in a jointly owned house, with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the bequest of a specific room from a jointly owned house, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind each view.

Core Idea
A bequest of a specific room from shared property is valid but depends on partition: the legatee gets the whole room (two imams) or half (Muhammad).

When a co-owner bequeaths a specific room from a jointly owned house, the outcome hinges on how partition assigns the room. The Hanafi imams differ on whether the testator's ownership is completed by partition to cover the whole room or only half. This lesson examines the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other, focusing on the underlying reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the case
A house is jointly owned by two. One co-owner bequeaths a specific room (bayt 'ayn) to a third party. The house is then divided. We need to determine what the legatee receives depending on which share the room falls into.
This is not a bequest of an undivided share but of a definite physical part.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two) hold that if the room falls in the testator's share, the legatee gets the whole room; if in the other's share, the legatee gets an equivalent area. Imam Muhammad holds that in either case, the legatee receives only half the room or its equivalent area.
Muhammad's view treats the bequest as partially void in the other's share.
3
Trace the talil (reasoning) of each side
The two argue that the testator intends full benefit, and partition completes ownership of the room for him, so the bequest attaches to the entire room. Muhammad argues that the testator initially owned only half the room, and the bequest of the whole is void in the other half without consent; partition does not retroactively grant ownership of the other half.
The two emphasize the purpose of partition as separation, not exchange; Muhammad emphasizes the time of bequest.
4
Apply to both scenarios
Scenario A: room falls in testator's share. The two: legatee gets whole room. Muhammad: legatee gets half. Scenario B: room falls in other's share. The two: legatee gets equivalent of whole room. Muhammad: legatee gets equivalent of half.
The 'equivalent' is typically from the testator's estate, not from the other co-owner.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is clear: under the two, the legatee always receives a full room (or its value); under Muhammad, only half. This affects the amount the testator's estate must pay.
The view of the two is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وببيت عين من دار مشتركة، وقسم فوقع في حظه، فهو للموصى له، وإلا مثل ذرعه والإقرار مثلها; أي إذا كانت الدار مشتركة بين اثنين، فأوصى أحدهما ببيت بعينه لرجل، فإن الدار تقسم، فإن وقع البيت في نصيب الموصي، فهو للموصى له وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر، فللموصى له مثل ذرع البيت، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما، وقال محمد: له نصف البيت إن وقع في نصيب الموصي، وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر، كان له مثل ذرع نصف البيت; لأنه أوصى بملكه وبملك غيره فينفذ في ملكه، ويتوقف الباقي على إجازة صاحبه، ثم إذا أصابه بالقسمة عين البيت كان للموصى له نصف البيت; لأنه عين ما أوصى به، وإن وقع في نصيب صاحبه كان له مثل نصف البيت ولهما أنه إذا أوصى بما يستقر ملكه فيه بالقسمة; لأنه يقصد الإيصاء بما يمكن الانتفاع به على الكمال ظاهرا، وذلك يكون بالقسمة; لأن الانتفاع بالمشاع قاصر، وقد استقر ملكه في جميع البيت إذا وقع في نصيبه فتنفذ الوصية فيه، ومعنى المبادلة في القسمة تابع، وإنما المقصود الإفراز تكميلا للمنفعة، ولهذا يجبر على القسمة فيه. (تكملة، عيني) والإقرار مثلها; أي الإقرار ببيت معين من دار مشتركة مثل الوصية به، حتى يؤمر بتسليم كله إذا وقع البيت في نصيب المقر عندهما، وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر يؤمر بتسليم مثله، وعند محمد: يؤمر بتسليم النصف أو قدر نصف، وقيل: محمد معهما في الإقرار [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٢/٢]
And for a specific room in a shared house, and it is divided and it falls in his share, then it is for the legatee; otherwise, the like of its area. And acknowledgment is like that. Meaning: if the house is shared between two, and one of them bequeaths a specific room to a man, then the house is divided. If the room falls in the testator's share, it is for the legatee; if it falls in the other's share, then the legatee is entitled to the equivalent area of the room. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He is entitled to half the room if it falls in the testator's share, and if it falls in the other's share, he is entitled to the equivalent area of half the room. Because he bequeathed what he owns and what he does not own, so it takes effect in his ownership, and the rest depends on the other's consent. Then if the specific room falls to him through division, the legatee gets half the room because it is the specific thing bequeathed; if it falls in the other's share, he gets the equivalent of half the room. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), because he bequeathed what becomes fully his through division, since he intends to bequeath what can be fully utilized, and that happens through division because shared utilization is deficient. And his ownership is fully established over the entire room if it falls in his share, so the bequest executes fully. The exchange aspect in division is subsidiary; the purpose is separation to complete the benefit, hence he is compelled to division in this matter. And acknowledgment is like that: meaning acknowledgment of a specific room in a shared house is like the bequest, so he is ordered to hand over the whole if the room falls in the share of the acknowledger according to the two; if it falls in the other's share, he is ordered to hand over its equivalent. According to Muhammad: he is ordered to hand over half, or the value of half. It is said that Muhammad agrees with the two in acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage discusses a bequest of a specific room from a house that is jointly owned by two persons. The testator is one of the co-owners. The ruling depends on which co-owner's share the room falls into when the house is partitioned. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: If the room falls in the testator's share, the legatee gets the entire room; if it falls in the other co-owner's share, the legatee gets an area equivalent to the room's area (from testator's other property or compensation). Imam Muhammad differs: If the room falls in the testator's share, the legatee gets only half the room; if in the other's share, he gets the equivalent of half the room. The reasoning: Muhammad views the bequest as comprising both the testator's share (which is half of the room in undivided ownership) and the other co-owner's share (which he cannot bequeath). So it takes effect in his half, and the other half is pending on the other's consent. When partition assigns the room to the testator, the legatee gets the specific room but only half ownership, because the testator owned only half. When it assigns to the other, the legatee gets the value of half. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the testator's intention is to bequeath something fully usable, and that is achieved through partition. Since partition aims to separate shares, the testator effectively becomes owner of the whole room if it falls to him, so the bequest executes on the whole. The principle is that the testator owned a right to the whole room through potential partition. The passage also notes that acknowledgment (iqrar) of a specific room in a shared house follows the same rules as a bequest, with a similar difference among the imams, though some say Muhammad agrees with the two in the case of acknowledgment.

Key Terms
بيت عين (bayt 'ayn): A specific room (identified by location or description).
مشاع (musha'): Undivided share in joint ownership.
إقرا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire room.
B) Half the room.
C) Nothing, because the bequest is void.
D) The equivalent area of the room from the other co-owner.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest of a specific room from a jointly owned house is valid but the legatee's entitlement depends on which share the room falls into after partition; the mufta bihi view (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) gives the legatee the whole room or its equivalent.

Bequest of Another's Property: Owner's Revocable Consent
Ruling on bequest of specific 1000 dirhams from someone else's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of a specific item from another's property and explain why the owner may refuse delivery even after consent.

Core Idea
A bequest of another's property binds the owner only as a revocable gift until delivery.

The testator may bequeath a specific sum from someone else's property, but the owner's consent does not make the bequest binding. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: the consent creates a new donation from the owner, and a gift (hiba) is not binding until delivered. The passage contrasts this with bequests from the testator's own estate, where heirs' consent removes obstacles. Understanding this distinction clarifies the limits of consent in wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
State the scenario: bequest of 1000 dirhams explicitly from another person's property. Note the ruling: it is valid if the owner consents and delivers, but the owner may still refuse after consent.
The bequest itself is not from the testator's estate, so it is treated as a conditional promise.
2
Understand the legal basis
The text explains: it is a donation (tabarru') of another's property, dependent on his consent. When he consents, it becomes his own donation, like a gift (hiba) that is not binding until delivery.
The key analogy: owner's consent is akin to a gift offer, not a binding contract.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The owner's position is analogized to a donor of a gift before delivery: both may retract. The 'illa (effective cause) is that the consent creates a voluntary transfer that is incomplete until physical delivery.
This is a qiyas khafi (implicit analogy) to the established rule for gifts.
4
Distinguish from heirs' consent
Contrast with bequests exceeding one-third, to an heir, or to a killer: here the heirs' consent makes the bequest binding. Why? Because the bequest itself was valid from the testator's property; the heirs' consent merely removes their right to object.
In this passage, the subject matter is not the testator's property, so the owner's consent creates a new right, not a removal of an obstacle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبألف عين من مال آخر، فأجاز رب المال بعد موت الموصي، ودفعه صح، وله المنع بعد الإجازة; لأنه تبرع بمال الغير فيتوقف على إجازته، فإذا أجاز كان تبرعا منه أيضا فله أن يمتنع من التسليم; لأنه لم يتم بعده فأشبه الهبة قبل التسليم، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بالزيادة على الثلث أو للوارث أو للقاتل، وأجازت الورثة; لأن الوصية صحيحة; لمصادفتها ملك نفسه، والامتناع لحق الورثة، فإذا أجازوها سقط حقهم، فينفذ من جهة الموصي. (تكملة، فتح)
And for a specific thousand dirhams from another's property, and the owner of the property consents after the testator's death and delivers it, it is valid, but he has the right to refuse after consent, because it is a donation of another's property, so it depends on his consent. When he consents, it becomes a donation from him as well, so he may refuse delivery because it is not completed after that, resembling a gift before delivery. Unlike if he bequeaths more than one-third, or to an heir, or to a killer, and the heirs consent; because the bequest is valid as it meets his own property, and refusal is due to the heirs' right; when they consent, their right falls, and it executes from the testator's side.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a bequest where the testator specifies a sum of money (1000 dirhams) from the property of another person (not the testator's own estate). The bequest is initially dependent on the consent of the property owner. If the owner consents after the testator's death and delivers the money, the bequest becomes valid. However, the owner retains the right to withhold delivery even after giving consent, because his action is considered a new donation (hiba) from him, and a gift is not binding until delivery is made. This resembles the rule for gifts: a donor may retract before delivery. The passage contrasts this with a bequest of more than one-third, or to an heir, or to a killer, where the consent of the heirs validates the bequest fully, because the bequest itself was valid from the testator (being his own property), and the heirs' consent removes the obstacle of their right; thus, the bequest is executed from the testator's side, and the heirs cannot later refuse. The difference is that in the first case, the subject matter is not the testator's property, so the consent creates a new donation from the owner, which is revocable; in the second case, it is the testator's property, and the heirs' consent merely lifts their claim, so the bequest is binding.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Consent given by the owner of the property after the testator's death.
تبرع (tabarru'): Donation; here, the owner's consent is considered a voluntary donation of his property.
هبة (hibah): Gift; the analogy drawn: owner's consent is like a gift that is not binding until delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the owner of the property refuse to deliver the specified 1000 dirhams even after consenting to the bequest?
A) Because the bequest is invalid from the beginning.
B) Because the consent is considered a new donation that is not binding until delivery.
C) Because the testator was not allowed to bequeath another's property.
D) Because the heirs have a superior right.

Key Takeaway
A bequest of another's property is valid only after the owner's consent and delivery, but the owner retains the right to refuse delivery because his consent is analogous to a revocable gift.

Acknowledgment of a Will After Division: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Ruling on acknowledgment of will after division with istihsan vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi istihsan and Zufar's qiyas regarding an acknowledgment of a will after division, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When one son acknowledges a will, he gives one-third of his share by istihsan, not half by qiyas.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi inheritance law: after two sons have divided their father's estate, one son acknowledges that their father had made a will to a third person for one-third of the wealth. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and the two companions) holds that the acknowledging son must give one-third of his own share, based on istihsan (juridical preference). Imam Zufar, however, argues via qiyas (analogy) that he should give half. We will explore both proofs and understand why the istihsan view is the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling in the matn.
The case: two sons divide the estate; one later acknowledges a will for one-third. The matn states the acknowledging son gives one-third of what is in his hand (his share). This is the Hanafi position.
This is a specific application of the principle that iqrar binds only the one who makes it.
2
Contrast Zufar's qiyas position.
Zufar argues the acknowledgment implies equality, so the legatee should be treated like a third brother. Since the other son's share is 'destroyed' (he denies), the acknowledging son must give half of his share to cover the legatee's portion from both shares.
Zufar's qiyas is based on the analogy of acknowledging a third brother.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning.
The acknowledging son admits a one-third share in the whole estate, but his admission only binds himself, not his brother. So he gives one-third of his own hand. Forcing half would risk inconsistency: the other son might later acknowledge and take half, giving him more than one-third.
Istihsan overrides the strict qiyas due to practical considerations and equity.
4
Distinguish from acknowledgment of debt.
If one son acknowledges a debt, he gives everything in his hand because debt takes precedence over inheritance. The will legatee is a partner, not a creditor, so the rule differs.
This distinction is crucial for avoiding confusion.
5
Determine the mufta bihi.
The relied-upon position is the istihsan view: one-third. The text itself presents it as the valid ruling and explains its basis.
Zufar's view is a legitimate ikhtilaf but not operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح إقرار أحد الابنين بعد القسمة بوصية أبيه في ثلث نصيبه. معناه: إذا قسم الابنان تركة أبيهما، وهي ألف درهم مثلا، ثم أقر أحدهما لرجل أن أباه أوصى له بثلث ماله فإن المقر يعطيه ثلث ما في يده وهذا استحسان والقياس أن يعطيه نصف ما في يده، وهو قول زفر؛ لأن إقراره بالثلث له تضمن إقراره بمساواته إياه والتسوية في إعطاء النصف ليبقى له النصف، فصار كما إذا أقر أحدهما بأخ ثالث لهما، وهذا لأن ما أخذه المنكر كالهالك، فيهلك عليهما. وجه الاستحسان: أنه أقر له بثلث شائع في جميع التركة، وهي في أيديهما، فيكون مقرا له بثلث ما في يده، وبثلث ما في يد أخيه، فيقبل إقراره في حق نفسه، ولا يقبل في حق أخيه؛ لعدم الولاية عليه، فيعطيه ثلث ما في يده؛ ولأنه لو أخذ منه نصف ما في يده أدى إلى محظور، وهو أن الابن الآخر ربما يقر به، فيأخذ نصف ما في يده، فيأخذ نصف التركة، فيزداد نصيبه على الثلث، وهو خلف. بخلاف ما أقر أحدهما بدين لغيره حيث يأخذ كل ما في يده إذا كان الدين مستغرقا له؛ لأن الدين مقدم على الميراث؛ فيكون مقرا بتقدمه عليه، أما الموصى له بالثلث شريك الوارث، فلا يسلم له شيء إلا إذا سلم للوارث مثلاه.
And valid is the acknowledgment of one of the two sons after division of his father's will regarding one-third of his share. Its meaning: If the two sons divide their father's estate, which is one thousand dirhams for example, then one of them acknowledges to a man that his father bequeathed to him one-third of his wealth, then the acknowledging one gives him one-third of what is in his hand. This is istihsan (juridical preference). And the analogy (qiyas) is that he gives him half of what is in his hand, and it is the saying of Zufar. Because his acknowledgment of one-third for him implied an acknowledgment of equality with him, and equality requires giving half so that half remains for him. So it becomes like the case when one of them acknowledges a third brother for them. And this is because what the denier takes is like destroyed, so it is destroyed on both of them. The face of istihsan: He acknowledged for him a one-third share in the entire estate, and it is in their hands. So he is acknowledging for him one-third of what is in his hand and one-third of what is in his brother's hand. His acknowledgment is accepted regarding himself and not accepted regarding his brother due to lack of authority over him. So he gives him one-third of what is in his hand. And because if he took half of what is in his hand, it would lead to a prohibition: that the other son might also acknowledge it, so he would take half of what is in his hand, thus he would take half of the estate, and his share would increase beyond one-third, which is contrary. Unlike if one of them acknowledged a debt owed to someone else, where he takes everything in his hand if the debt is exhaustive, because debt takes precedence over inheritance; so he is acknowledging its precedence over him. As for the legatee of one-third, they are partners with the heir, so nothing is secured for him unless the heir is secured twice as much.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of an acknowledgment of a will after division. The matn states that if one of two sons acknowledges after the division of the estate that his father bequeathed one-third of his wealth to a certain person, the acknowledging son gives only one-third of what is in his own hand. This is the relied-upon position (istihsan). Zufar's qiyas (analogy) would require giving half of what is in his hand, because the acknowledgment implies equality: if he acknowledges a one-third right for the legatee, he effectively acknowledges that the legatee is like a third brother, so they should share the estate equally, leaving the acknowledging son with one-third and the legatee with one-third, and the other son with one-third. But since the other son denies, his portion is treated as lost, so the acknowledging son should pay half of his share to cover the legatee's portion from both. The istihsan reasoning: The acknowledgment is for a one-third share in the entire estate, which includes both the acknowledging son's portion and the other son's portion. The acknowledging son's admission is valid only for himself, not for his brother. So he gives one-third of what is in his hand, which is fair. If he were forced to give half, the other son might later also acknowledge, take half, and end up with more than one-third, causing inconsistency. This differs from a debt, where the acknowledging son must pay the entire debt from his share because debt precedes inheritance. Here, the legatee is a partner with the heir, so the rule is different.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): A legal acknowledgment by one party of a right belonging to another; in this context, a son's admission that his father made a will to a third party.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) due to considerations of equity, custom, or necessity. Here it is used to give one-third instead of half.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning from a known case (the 'asl) to a new case (the far') based on a common effective cause ('illa). Here, Zufar analogizes the acknowledgment of a will to the acknowledgment of a third brother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when one of two sons acknowledges a will after division, how much does he give?
A) One-third of his own share.
B) Half of his own share.
C) One-third of the entire estate.
D) Half of the entire estate.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, acknowledgment of a will after division binds only the acknowledger, so he gives one-third of his own share, not half, despite Zufar's qiyas.

beginner
