Gratuitous Acts in Terminal Illness Are Wills
Establishes general rule for gratuities in deathly illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that any gratuitous disposition in terminal illness is treated as a will, and identify the condition that it is effective only from one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Core Idea
Gratuitous acts in terminal illness are wills — restricted to one-third unless heirs permit.

A person in his deathly illness may engage in acts like manumission, gift, or muhabah (a sale at undervalue). The Hanafi school treats these as wills by analogy, meaning they are only effective from one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. This lesson establishes the general principle and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts covered
The passage lists manumission (itq), muhabah (favorable sale), and gift (hiba) as examples. Each is a gratuitous disposition.
Muhabah includes selling below market value or buying above.
2
Understand the ruling: they are like wills
These acts are legally treated as a will (wasiyyah). The predicate 'وصية' applies to all of them.
That means they take effect only after death, not during illness.
3
Note the one-third restriction
Like a will, they are enforceable only from one-third of the estate. The heirs' right attaches to the property, so the sick person cannot give away more than a third without heir permission.
The restriction is because the sick person's property is considered encumbered by heirs' rights.
4
Recognize the effect of heirs' permission
If the heirs permit after death, the act becomes effective from the whole estate. No sa'y (earning) is required from a manumitted slave if heirs agree.
This is because the prohibition was solely for the heirs' benefit, which they can waive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العتق في المرض أي مرض الموت تحريره في مرض موته ومحاباته وهبته وصية ولم يسع إن أجيز، فإن حابى فحرر، العبد عتقه فهي أحق، وبعكسه استويا ، وإن أوصى بأن يعتق عنه بهذا المائة عبد، أي المحاباة بان حرر فحابى وقالا عتقه أولى فيهما باب العتق إلخ لما كان الإعتاق في المرض من أنواع الوصية، وكان له أحكام مخصوصة أفرده بباب على حدة، وأخره عن صريح الوصية؛ لأن الصريح هو الأصل تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣١٦/٩] الحباء، وهو ومحاباته إلخ: أي محاباة الرجل في مرضه، وهي من العطاء، وصورتها: أن يبيع المريض ما يساوي مائة بخمسين، أو يشتري ما يساوي خمسين بمائة، فالزائد على قيمة المثل في الشراء، والناقص في البيع محاباة، حكمها حكم الوصية. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٤/٢] وصية: خبر للمبتدأ، وهو قوله: "تحريره" وما عطف عليه، يعني حكم هذه التصرفات كحكم الوصية، حتى يعتبر من الثلث، وإنما اعتبرت من الثلث؛ لتعلق حق الورثة بماله فصار محجورا عليه في حق الزائد على الثلث، وكذا كل تصرف ابتدأ المريض إيجابه على نفسه كالضمان والكفالة، فهو في حكم الوصية؛ لأنه تبرع كالهبة، وكل ما أوجبه بعد الموت، فهو من الثلث، وإن أوجبه في حال صحته؛ إذ المعتبر حالة الإضافة لا حالة العقد، نفذه من التصرفات كالعتق والهبة فالمعتبر فيه حالة العقد، فإن كان صحيحا فهو من جميع المال، وإن كان وكل مرض برئ منه فهو ملحق بحال الصحة؛ لأن حق الورثة والغرماء لا يتعلق بماله إلا في مريضا فهو من الثلث مرض موته، وبالبرء تبين أنه ليس مرض الموت. (عيني، فتح) من ولم يسع إن أجيز: أي إذا أجازت الورثة العتق في المرض فلا سعاية على المعتق؛ لأن العتق في المرض وصية على ما بيناه، وهو يجوز بإجازة الورثة، فلا يلزمه شيء؛ لأن المنع لحقهم، فيسقط بالإجازة على ما بينا، هذا إذا لم يخرج الثلث تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۲۳/۹] فهي :أحق أي أحق من العتق صورته إذا باع رجل في مرض موته عبدا من رجل بألف درهم وقيمته ألفان، ثم أعتق عبدا له آخر يساوي ألفا ولا مال له غيرهما، فالمحاباة أولى من العتق فيسلم العبد للمشتري بألف ويسعى العبد في قيمته لورثته؛ لأنها تثبت في ضمن عقد المعاوضة، فكان تبرعا بمعناه لا بصيغته حتى يأخذ الشفيع بالشفعة، ويملكه الصبي والعبد المأذون لهما أي يملك البيع بالمحاباة، والإعتاق تبرع صيغة ومعنى، فإذا وجد المحاباة أولا دفع الأضعف، وإذا وجد العتق أولا وثبت، وهو لا يحتمل كان ضرورته المزاحمة. (ملا) ،مسكين (فتح استويا أي إن أعتق ثم حابي والصورة الباقية على حالها، فهما سواء، فيسعى العبد في نصفه بخمس مائة ويعتق النصف الآخر مجانا، وتكون المحاباة بقدر خمس مائة، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : العتق أولى في المسألتين، وقال زفر الأول أولى. (ملا مسكين)
Chapter of Manumission in Illness, i.e., deathly illness. His manumission, his muhabah (favorable transaction), and his gift in his deathly illness are a will, and it is not effective without permission. If he gave muhabah then freed, the slave of the muhabah has precedence, and in the opposite case they are equal. And if he bequeaths that a slave be purchased for him with this hundred, i.e., the muhabah, then he freed and gave muhabah, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: manumission has precedence in both cases. The chapter etc. Since manumission in illness is a type of will and has specific rulings, he dedicated a separate chapter for it and placed it after explicit will because the explicit is the original. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:316] Muhabah etc.: i.e., a man's favorable transaction in his illness, which is a type of gift. Its form: the sick person sells what is worth one hundred for fifty, or buys what is worth fifty for one hundred, so the excess over the fair value in purchase and the deficit in sale is muhabah; its ruling is like that of a will. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:484] 'Will' is the predicate of the subject, which is his statement 'his manumission' and what is conjoined to it, meaning the ruling of these dispositions is like the ruling of a will, so that it is considered from one-third. It is considered from one-third because the right of the heirs attaches to his property, so he becomes restricted with respect to what exceeds one-third. Likewise every disposition that the sick person initiates as an obligation on himself, like guaranty and surety, is in the ruling of a will because it is a gratuity like a gift. Whatever he obligates after death is from one-third, even if he obligated it during health, because what matters is the time of obligation, not the time of contract. For dispositions like manumission and gift, what matters is the time of contract; if it was in health, it is from all the property; if it was in a sickness from which he recovered, it is attached to the state of health, because the right of heirs and creditors does not attach to his property except in deathly illness; recovery shows it was not deathly illness. (Ayni, Fath) 'And it is not effective if not permitted': i.e., if the heirs permit the manumission in illness, there is no sa'y (earning) on the manumitted slave because manumission in illness is a will, and it is valid with the heirs' permission, so nothing is required of him because the prohibition is for their right, so it falls with permission. This is if one-third is not exceeded. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:223] 'It has precedence': i.e., over manumission. Its form: if a man in his deathly illness sells a slave for one thousand dirhams while he is worth two thousand, then he manumits another slave worth one thousand and he has no other property, then the muhabah takes precedence over manumission, so the slave is delivered to the buyer for one thousand, and the (manumitted) slave works to earn his value for the heirs because the muhabah is established within a compensatory contract, so it is a gratuity in meaning but not in wording, so that the preemptor takes by preemption, and the minor and the authorized slave can own it, i.e., they can own the sale with muhabah. Manumission is a gratuity in wording and meaning. If muhabah occurs first, it repels the weaker; if manumission occurs first and is established, and it cannot bear (the precedence of muhabah), the necessity is competition. (Mulla) Miskeen (Fath) 'Equal': i.e., if he manumitted first then gave muhabah, and the remaining picture is as it was, they are equal. So the slave works for half his value (five hundred) and the other half is freed gratis, and the muhabah is to the extent of five hundred. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: manumission has precedence in both cases. Zufar said: the first has precedence. (Mulla Miskeen)
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rules on manumission in terminal illness. It establishes that in deathly illness, any gratuitous disposition—whether manumission, gift, or muhabah (a sale at undervalue or overvalue)—is treated as a will, meaning it is only effective from one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. The key dispute among Hanafi scholars is about priority when a person both engages in muhabah and manumits in the same illness. Abu Hanifa differentiates based on the order and nature: muhabah, being embedded in a sale contract, is a stronger form of gratuity because it is a gratuity in meaning only, whereas manumission is a pure gratuity in both wording and meaning. Therefore, if muhabah occurs first, it takes full effect and the later manumission is restricted. If manumission occurs first, they compete and the slave is half-free and half-works for the value. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider manumission stronger in both scenarios because it is a pure act of worship. Zufar gives precedence to whichever occurred first. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view. The passage also clarifies that the heirs' permission renders the will effective from the whole estate, and that dispositions after death or in non-terminal sickness are treated differently.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): A sale at undervalue or purchase at overvalue in terminal illness, treated as a gratuitous disposition.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave in terminal illness, treated as a will by the Hanafi school.
وصية (waṣiyyah): A will or bequest, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is a valid gift from the entire estate.
B) It is treated as a will, limited to one-third.
C) It is void regardless of heirs' consent.
D) It is valid only if the donor recovers.

Key Takeaway
All gratuitous acts in terminal illness are akin to wills and thus effective only up to one-third without heir consent.

Priority Between Muhabah and Manumission in Terminal Illness
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on priority in terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the priority between muhabah and manumission in terminal illness, and apply Abu Hanifa's view with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
When muhabah and manumission conflict, Abu Hanifa gives precedence based on timing and nature; the Sahibayn prioritize manumission absolutely.

When a person in terminal illness both engages in muhabah and manumits a slave, a priority problem arises if the estate is insufficient. Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn, and Zufar each have distinct views. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical outcome in estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Set the scenario
Assume a person sells a slave (worth 2000) for 1000 (muhabah) and manumits another slave worth 1000, with no other assets. The estate is 2000 (the remaining value after sale?) Actually the example: sells one slave for 1000 when worth 2000, then manumits another worth 1000, no other property.
The total estate includes the sold slave's proceeds and the manumitted slave's value.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
If muhabah comes first, it takes full effect; the manumitted slave must work for his value. If manumission comes first, they share equally: half free, half works.
Muhabah is a gratuity in meaning only, manumission is pure gratuity.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say manumission always takes precedence, regardless of order. The muhabah is then reduced.
They view manumission as an act of worship deserving full effect.
4
Identify Zufar's position
Zufar says the earlier act, regardless of type, takes precedence.
This is the simplest position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, if muhabah is first, the buyer gets the slave, and the manumitted slave works for his full value. Under Sahibayn, the manumitted slave is free, and the muhabah is reduced proportionally.
The difference affects the rights of heirs and the slave.

Source Text

Chapter of Manumission in Illness, i.e., deathly illness. His manumission, his muhabah (favorable transaction), and his gift in his deathly illness are a will, and it is not effective without permission. If he gave muhabah then freed, the slave of the muhabah has precedence, and in the opposite case they are equal. And if he bequeaths that a slave be purchased for him with this hundred, i.e., the muhabah, then he freed and gave muhabah, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: manumission has precedence in both cases. The chapter etc. Since manumission in illness is a type of will and has specific rulings, he dedicated a separate chapter for it and placed it after explicit will because the explicit is the original. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:316] Muhabah etc.: i.e., a man's favorable transaction in his illness, which is a type of gift. Its form: the sick person sells what is worth one hundred for fifty, or buys what is worth fifty for one hundred, so the excess over the fair value in purchase and the deficit in sale is muhabah; its ruling is like that of a will. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:484] 'Will' is the predicate of the subject, which is his statement 'his manumission' and what is conjoined to it, meaning the ruling of these dispositions is like the ruling of a will, so that it is considered from one-third. It is considered from one-third because the right of the heirs attaches to his property, so he becomes restricted with respect to what exceeds one-third. Likewise every disposition that the sick person initiates as an obligation on himself, like guaranty and surety, is in the ruling of a will because it is a gratuity like a gift. Whatever he obligates after death is from one-third, even if he obligated it during health, because what matters is the time of obligation, not the time of contract. For dispositions like manumission and gift, what matters is the time of contract; if it was in health, it is from all the property; if it was in a sickness from which he recovered, it is attached to the state of health, because the right of heirs and creditors does not attach to his property except in deathly illness; recovery shows it was not deathly illness. (Ayni, Fath) 'And it is not effective if not permitted': i.e., if the heirs permit the manumission in illness, there is no sa'y (earning) on the manumitted slave because manumission in illness is a will, and it is valid with the heirs' permission, so nothing is required of him because the prohibition is for their right, so it falls with permission. This is if one-third is not exceeded. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:223] 'It has precedence': i.e., over manumission. Its form: if a man in his deathly illness sells a slave for one thousand dirhams while he is worth two thousand, then he manumits another slave worth one thousand and he has no other property, then the muhabah takes precedence over manumission, so the slave is delivered to the buyer for one thousand, and the (manumitted) slave works to earn his value for the heirs because the muhabah is established within a compensatory contract, so it is a gratuity in meaning but not in wording, so that the preemptor takes by preemption, and the minor and the authorized slave can own it, i.e., they can own the sale with muhabah. Manumission is a gratuity in wording and meaning. If muhabah occurs first, it repels the weaker; if manumission occurs first and is established, and it cannot bear (the precedence of muhabah), the necessity is competition. (Mulla) Miskeen (Fath) 'Equal': i.e., if he manumitted first then gave muhabah, and the remaining picture is as it was, they are equal. So the slave works for half his value (five hundred) and the other half is freed gratis, and the muhabah is to the extent of five hundred. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: manumission has precedence in both cases. Zufar said: the first has precedence. (Mulla Miskeen)
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rules on manumission in terminal illness. It establishes that in deathly illness, any gratuitous disposition—whether manumission, gift, or muhabah (a sale at undervalue or overvalue)—is treated as a will, meaning it is only effective from one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. The key dispute among Hanafi scholars is about priority when a person both engages in muhabah and manumits in the same illness. Abu Hanifa differentiates based on the order and nature: muhabah, being embedded in a sale contract, is a stronger form of gratuity because it is a gratuity in meaning only, whereas manumission is a pure gratuity in both wording and meaning. Therefore, if muhabah occurs first, it takes full effect and the later manumission is restricted. If manumission occurs first, they compete and the slave is half-free and half-works for the value. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider manumission stronger in both scenarios because it is a pure act of worship. Zufar gives precedence to whichever occurred first. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view. The passage also clarifies that the heirs' permission renders the will effective from the whole estate, and that dispositions after death or in non-terminal sickness are treated differently.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): A sale at undervalue or purchase at overvalue in terminal illness, treated as a gratuitous disposition.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave in terminal illness, treated as a will by the Hanafi school.
وصية (waṣiyyah): A will or bequest, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a terminally ill person manumits a slave first and then gives muhabah, what is the ruling?
A) Manumission takes precedence.
B) Muhabah takes precedence.
C) They are equal.
D) The first act takes precedence.

Key Takeaway
When muhabah and manumission conflict in terminal illness, Abu Hanifa's view (mufta bihi) differentiates by order: if muhabah first, it wins; if manumission first, they share equally.

Bequest for Manumission When Funds Are Lost: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial execution of bequest for manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on partial execution of a bequest for manumission and state the underlying basis of ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
If the bequest fund is partially lost, Abu Hanifa voids the bequest; the Sahibayn save it by analogy to Hajj.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a bequest to purchase and free a slave can be partially executed when the designated fund is diminished. Abu Hanifa insists on strict compliance with the testator's instruction, while the Sahibayn prioritize the piety of manumission. The difference hinges on the nature of manumission—is it a right of Allah or a right of the slave? Let us unpack their arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
A testator bequeaths a specific sum (e.g., 100 dirhams) to buy and free a slave. Part of the sum is lost. The question: does the bequest fail or is it executed partially?
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa rules that the bequest fails entirely. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that it is executed as far as possible.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They analogize to a bequest for Hajj: if funds are insufficient, Hajj is performed with what remains. Manumission is also an act of piety (qurbah), so partial execution should be valid.
Analogy (qiyas) to Hajj bequest.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
He distinguishes: Hajj is pure worship where the beneficiary (Allah) does not change. Here, the bequest is to buy a specific slave; if less money is available, a cheaper slave would be bought, changing the intended beneficiary. He analogizes to a monetary bequest where partial payment is allowed only if the legatee is the same.
The legatee (the slave) changes, so the bequest fails.
5
Identify the underlying principle
The dispute is rooted in a deeper ikhtilaf: is manumission a right of Allah (haqq Allah) or a right of the slave (haqq al-ʿabd)? The Sahibayn say it is Allah's right (so the beneficiary does not change), while Abu Hanifa says it is the slave's right (so the intended beneficiary changes if a different slave is freed).
Al-Zaylai confirms this principle.

Source Text

(فتح الله المعين) بخلاف الحج إلخ: أي لو أوصى أن يحج عنه بهذه المائة، فهلك منها درهم يحج بما بقي من حيث يبلغ، وإن لم يهلك شيء حج عنه بها، وإن بقي شيء من الحجة يرد على الورثة، وهذا بالاتفاق، وقد مر وجه الفرق لأبي حنيفة بين الحج والعتق (من) ملا مسكين بزيادة
Then if one dirham of it perishes, it (the bequest) is not executed, unlike Hajj with it. And with the manumission of his slave, he died and committed a crime, and it was paid, it becomes void. i.e., And if the testator bequeaths the slave (garbled) the crime, the bequest the bequest, and if he ransoms, not. And with his one-third to Zayd, and he left a slave, and Zayd claimed his manumission in health, and the heir claimed it in his illness, the word is the heir's, and there is nothing for Zayd unless something remains from his one-third, or he provides proof with his oath. i.e., his one-third of his property = property and heir, to be executed from all the property, to be executed from one-third, i.e., the value of the slave is the right of Allah, it is not executed, i.e., the bequest, so he is not manumitted with what remains according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is manumitted with what remains because it is a bequest of a type of piety, so it must be executed as much as possible, analogically to the bequest for Hajj. And according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is a bequest for manumission of a slave purchased with a hundred from his property, and executing it for someone purchased for less is execution for someone other than the legatee, unlike the bequest for Hajj because it is pure piety and the beneficiary has not changed, so it is like if he bequeathed a hundred to a man, then some of it perishes, the remainder is given to him. And it is said this issue is built on another principle in which there is difference, namely that manumission is the right of Allah, so testimony is accepted without claim, so the beneficiary did not change; according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is the right of the slave, so testimony is not accepted without claim, so the beneficiary changed. al-Zaylai said: this construction is correct because the principle is established and known and cannot be denied. (Fathallah al-Mu'in) Unlike Hajj etc.: i.e., if he bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him with this hundred, then one dirham perishes, he performs Hajj with what remains as far as it reaches, and if nothing perishes, Hajj is performed for him with it, and if something remains after Hajj, it is returned to the heirs. This is by agreement, and the point of difference for Abu Hanifa between Hajj and manumission has been mentioned. (from Mulla Miskeen with addition)
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest to purchase and manumit a slave from a specific sum of money. If part of the sum is lost, Abu Hanifa rules that the bequest fails entirely because it specifies a particular slave (purchased with that amount) and cannot be executed for a lesser amount or a different slave. The Sahibayn argue that since manumission is an act of piety, the bequest should be executed as far as possible, analogous to a bequest to perform Hajj, where if funds are insufficient, one performs Hajj with the remainder. The commentary explains that the underlying difference is about the nature of manumission: whether it is the right of Allah (in which case the beneficiary does not change, and partial execution is possible) or the right of the slave (in which case the beneficiary changes if a cheaper slave is purchased, invalidating the bequest). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
وصية بالعتق (waṣiyyah bi al-ʿitq): A bequest to purchase and manumit a slave.
قربة (qurbah): An act of devotion or piety, like Hajj or manumission.
حق الله (haqq Allāh): Right of Allah; legal obligations where the benefit is purely spiritual and the beneficiary is Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa says it is valid; Sahibayn say it is invalid.
B) Abu Hanifa says it fails; Sahibayn say it is partially executed.
C) Both say it fails entirely.
D) Both say it is partially executed.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to buy and free a specific slave, partial loss of the fund voids the bequest according to Abu Hanifa, because the intended beneficiary changes; the Sahibayn disagree by analogy to Hajj.

Effect of Slave's Crime on Bequest of Manumission
Ruling on a bequest of manumission when the slave commits a crime and is given as compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a bequest of manumission when the slave commits a crime and distinguish between the two outcomes based on whether the slave is surrendered or ransomed by the heirs.

Core Idea
The bequest is valid if heirs ransom the slave; void if the slave is surrendered to the victim.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter on wasiyyah: the interaction between a bequest of manumission and a crime committed by the slave. The passage clarifies that the right of the crime victim's guardian takes precedence, but the heirs can preserve the bequest by paying ransom from their own wealth. We will analyze the two possible outcomes and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest of manumission. Its validity depends on whether the slave is still part of the estate at the testator's death.
The ruling is not about obligation but about validity.
2
Examine the effect of surrendering the slave
If the slave is given to the victim's guardian as compensation for the crime, the bequest becomes void because the slave leaves the testator's ownership.
The victim's right takes precedence over the testator's bequest.
3
Examine the effect of ransom by heirs
If the heirs ransom the slave from their own wealth, the bequest remains valid because the slave remains in the estate and is purified from the crime.
The ransom must be from the heirs' own money, not from the estate.
4
State the underlying principle
The right of the crime victim's guardian takes precedence, but if heirs voluntarily pay the ransom, the slave is as if innocent, and the bequest stands.
This balances the rights of the victim, the testator, and the heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلت لأن الدفع قد صح؛ لأن حق ولي الجناية مقدم على حق الموصي، فيخرج به عن ملكه فبطلت رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢] وإن فدى: العبد بأن فداه الورثة، وكان الفداء في أموالهم (عيني) لا : أي لا تبطل الوصية؛ لأنهم هم الذين التزموه، وجازت الوصية؛ لأن العبد طهر عن الجناية، فصار كأنه لم يجن. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢]
It becomes void because the payment has taken effect; because the right of the guardian of the crime victim takes precedence over the right of the testator, so he (the slave) leaves his ownership, so it becomes void. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:485] And if he ransoms: i.e., the heirs ransom the slave, and the ransom is from their own wealth (Ayni), no: i.e., the bequest does not become void because they (the heirs) have undertaken it, and the bequest is valid because the slave is purified from the crime, so he becomes as if he did not commit it. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:485]
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage provides two scenarios regarding a bequest of manumission when the slave has committed a crime that results in a claim against him. First, if the slave is given to the victim's guardian as compensation (i.e., the slave himself is used to satisfy the claim), the bequest of manumission becomes void because the slave leaves the testator's estate and the subject of the bequest no longer exists. Second, if the heirs ransom the slave by paying from their own money, the bequest remains valid because the slave continues to be part of the estate, and the crime claim is satisfied by the heirs' payment. The principle: the right of the crime victim's guardian takes precedence over the testator's bequest if the slave is surrendered; but if the heirs choose to pay ransom, they preserve the slave for the bequest.

Key Terms
ولي الجناية (walī al-jināyah): The guardian or representative of the victim who has the right to claim compensation for the crime.
فداء (fidā'): Ransom paid by the heirs to satisfy the crime claim and retain the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The slave is freed immediately.
D) The heirs must pay the ransom from the estate.

Key Takeaway
The bequest of manumission is void if the slave is surrendered as compensation, but valid if the heirs ransom the slave from their own wealth.

Dispute on Timing of Manumission: Heir vs. Legatee
Ruling on dispute of timing between heir and legatee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the legatee and heir disagree on whether a manumission occurred in health or illness, and explain the evidentiary principles used.

Core Idea
When legatee and heir dispute timing of manumission, the heir wins by default—events are attributed to the nearest time.

This passage addresses a dispute that arises after a testator's death. Both parties agree the slave was freed, but they disagree on when. The outcome determines whether the bequest to Zayd remains valid. We explore the Hanafi ruling and the two key principles that govern it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
The legatee claims manumission in health; the heir claims it occurred in illness. The timing is crucial because it changes the legal nature of the manumission.
2
Understand the legal consequence of each timing
If in health: manumission is not a will, so the slave is not part of the estate, and the legatee is entitled to one-third of the remaining property. If in illness: manumission is a will and consumes the one-third, leaving nothing for the legatee.
3
Determine burden of proof
The legatee claims entitlement to one-third excluding the slave; the heir denies this. The heir is the denier (munkir), so his word is accepted with oath, according to the principle al-qawlu qawlu al-munkir.
Standard evidentiary rule: the burden is on the claimant.
4
Apply the principle of attributing events to the nearest time
Manumission is a recent event; by default, it is attributed to the nearest possible time, which is the period of illness (closer to death). This strengthens the heir's position.
Principle: al-ḥawādith tuḍāf ilā aqrab al-awqāt.
5
Recognize the exception with proof
If the legatee can provide evidence (bayyinah) that the manumission occurred in health, his claim is established and he receives his share. Proof overrides the default presumption.
The text mentions 'or he provides proof' from Ramz al-Haqa'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول للوارث إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد وله عبد، وأقر الموصى له والوارث أن الميت أعتق هذا العبد، فقال الموصى له: أعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث : أعتقه في المرض، فالقول قول الوارث، ولا شيء للموصى له؛ لأن الموصى له يدعي استحقاق ثلث ماله سوى العبد؛ لأن العتق في الصحة ليس بوصية، فينفذ من جميع المال، والوارث ينكر استحقاقه ثلث ماله غير العبد؛ لأن العتق في المرض وصية، وهو مقدم على غيره من الوصايا، فذهب الثلث بالعتق، فبطل حق الموصى له بالثلث، فكان الوارث منكرا لاستحقاقه والقول قول المنكر مع اليمين، ولأن العتق حادث، والحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات؛ للتيقن بها، فكان الظاهر شاهدا للورثة، فيكون القول قولهم مع اليمين تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٣٢/٩] (بتغيير) يعني ولا شيء إلخ : أي إذا كان القول قول الوارث فلا شيء لزيد، وهو الموصى له إلا أن يفضل من ثلثه شيء من قيمة العبد؛ لأنه لا مزاحم له فيه، فيسلم له ذلك [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢] (بتغيير) أو يبرهن إلخ: أي أو يقيم زيد بينة أن العتق وقع في الصحة، فيكون له حينئذ ثلث جميع المال سوى العبد؛ لأن الثابت بالبينة كالثابت على دعواه، يعني معاينة، والموصى له خصم بالإجماع؛ لأنه يثبت حقه، وكذا العبد؛ لأن العتق حقه. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢]
The word is the heir's. If a man bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and he has a slave, and the legatee and the heir agree that the deceased manumitted this slave, but the legatee says: 'He manumitted him in health' and the heir says: 'He manumitted him in his illness,' then the word is the heir's, and there is nothing for the legatee. Because the legatee claims entitlement to one-third of his property excluding the slave, since manumission in health is not a will, so it is executed from all the property (so the slave is not part of the estate). The heir denies his entitlement to one-third of his property excluding the slave because manumission in illness is a will, and it takes precedence over other bequests, so the one-third is consumed by the manumission, thus the legatee's right to the one-third is void. So the heir is the denier, and the word is the denier's with oath. Also because manumission is a recent event, and recent events are attributed to the nearest time (to death) for certainty, so the apparent evidence supports the heirs, so their word is accepted with oath. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:332] (modified) Meaning 'and nothing etc.': i.e., if the word is the heir's, there is nothing for Zayd, the legatee, unless something remains from his one-third from the slave's value, because there is no competitor, so that is given to him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:485] (modified) 'Or he provides proof etc.': i.e., if Zayd provides evidence that the manumission occurred in health, then he gets one-third of all the property excluding the slave, because what is proven by evidence is like what is established by direct observation, and the legatee is a litigant by consensus because he establishes his right; similarly the slave because manumission is his right. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:485]
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute between a legatee (Zayd) and the heir regarding the timing of the decedent's manumission of a slave. Both agree that the slave was manumitted, but they disagree on whether it occurred in health or in terminal illness. If it was in health, the manumission is not a will and takes effect from the entire estate, so the slave is not part of the estate, and Zayd is entitled to one-third of the estate excluding the slave. If it was in illness, manumission is a will and consumes the one-third, leaving nothing for Zayd. The ruling: the word of the heir is accepted with his oath because the heir denies the claim of the legatee, and also because the default is to attribute recent events to the nearest time (i.e., the illness period). This is based on the principle that a recent event is assumed to have occurred at the closest possible time to the present. However, if Zayd can produce evidence (bayan) that the manumission was in health, his claim is established, and he receives his one-third of the estate excluding the slave.

Key Terms
القول قول المنكر (al-qawlu qawlu al-munkir): The word of the one who denies the claim is accepted with oath.
الحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات (al-ḥawādith tuḍāf ilā aqrab al-awqāt): Events are attributed to the nearest possible time, used here to presume manumission occurred in illness (closer to death).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between a legatee and an heir about whether manumission occurred in health or illness, whose word is accepted initially?
A) The legatee's.
B) The heir's, with oath.
C) The slave's.
D) Both are equal.

Key Takeaway
When timing of manumission is disputed, the heir's word prevails by default due to legal presumptions, unless the legatee provides proof.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

10 min
Bequest of Manumission: Death of Slave or Loss of Value
Intra-Hanafi dispute on execution of manumission bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn on execution of manumission bequests when the slave dies or the bequest diminishes, and evaluate the underlying principle regarding the nature of itq.

Core Idea
Manumission bequest fails entirely if the slave dies or value is lost; the Sahibayn allow partial execution—the nature of itq as a right determines the outcome.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement on bequests of manumission. Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, clash over whether a bequest of a slave or a specific sum for manumission must be executed exactly as designated, or can be partially fulfilled if the slave dies or part of the bequest is lost. The dispute turns on a fundamental question: is manumission a right of Allah or a right of the slave? Understanding this disagreement illuminates broader Hanafi principles of bequest interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Note the three cases: (1) part of the specified sum perishes, (2) the bequeathed slave dies, (3) the slave commits a tort after the testator's death.
The third scenario has two subcases: compensation paid by the estate vs. ransom paid by the heirs.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest is nullified in all cases where the exact designated subject (specific sum or specific slave) cannot be delivered. His reasoning: the bequest is for a specific recipient, and executing it with a different amount or a different slave would be a bequest to someone else.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the bequest should be executed as much as possible, by analogy to a bequest for Hajj. Since manumission is an act of worship (qurbah), it should be fulfilled proportionally.
Their analogy: if one bequeaths money for Hajj and part is lost, the Hajj is performed with the remainder.
4
Trace the deeper principle
The commentary reveals the root of the dispute: is manumission a right of Allah (in which case the beneficiary is not tied to a specific slave) or a right of the slave (so the specific slave is the beneficiary)? Abu Hanifa views it as a right of the slave, so changing the slave changes the beneficiary.
Al-Zayla'i confirms this foundational disagreement as the basis for the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهلك منها درهم لم تنفذ، بخلاف الحج به، وبعتق عبده فمات فجنى ودفع بطلت، وإن فدى لا. عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يعتق عنه بما بقي؛ لأنه وصية بنوع قربة، فيجب تنفيذها ما أمكن قياسا على الوصية بالحج، وله أنه وصية بالعتق لعبد يشتري بمائة من ماله، وتنفيذها فيمن يشتري بأقل منه تنفيذ في غير الموصى له بخلاف الوصية بالحج؛ لأنها قربة محضة والمستحق لم يتبدل فصار كما لو أوصى بمائة لرجل، فهلك بعضها يدفع إليه الباقي، وقيل: هذه المسألة مبنية على أصل آخر مختلف فيه، وهو أن العتق حق الله تعالى حتى تقبل الشهادة فيه من غير دعوى، فلم يتبدل المستحق، وعنده: حق العبد حتى لا تقبل الشهادة فيه من غير دعوى، فاختلف المستحق، قال الزيلعي: وهذا البناء صحيح؛ لأن الأصل ثابت معروف ولا سبيل لإنكاره. (فتح الله المعين) بخلاف الحج إلخ: أي لو أوصى أن يحج عنه بهذه المائة، فهلك منها درهم يحج بما بقي من حيث يبلغ، وإن لم يهلك شيء حج عنه بها، وإن بقي شيء من الحجة يرد على الورثة، وهذا بالاتفاق، وقد مر وجه الفرق لأبي حنيفة بين الحج والعتق (من) ملا مسكين بزيادة بطلت لأن الدفع قد صح؛ لأن حق ولي الجناية مقدم على حق الموصي، فيخرج به عن ملكه فبطلت رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢] وإن فدى: العبد بأن فداه الورثة، وكان الفداء في أموالهم (عيني) لا : أي لا تبطل الوصية؛ لأنهم هم الذين التزموه، وجازت الوصية؛ لأن العبد طهر عن الجناية، فصار كأنه لم يجن. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٥/٢]
If a dirham of it perishes, it is not executed, unlike the Hajj with it. And if he bequeaths his slave, then he dies, then commits a tort, and compensation is paid, the bequest is invalid. But if he ransoms, it is not invalid. According to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: it is executed from what remains, because it is a bequest for a type of worship, so its execution should be as much as possible, by analogy to the bequest for Hajj. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that it is a bequest for manumission of a slave to be bought with one hundred of his wealth, and executing it by buying someone cheaper is execution for someone other than the intended person, unlike the bequest for Hajj, because it is a pure act of worship and the beneficiary does not change, so it is like if he bequeathed one hundred to a man and some of it perishes, the remainder is paid to him. And it was said: This issue is built upon another principle in which there is difference, namely that manumission is the right of Allah, so testimony is accepted without a claim, and the beneficiary does not change; according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is the right of the slave, so testimony is not accepted without a claim, and the beneficiary changes. Al-Zayla'i said: This building is correct, because the principle is established and well-known, and there is no way to deny it. (Fath al-Mu'in) Unlike Hajj, etc.: i.e., if he bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him with this hundred, and a dirham of it perishes, he performs Hajj with what remains as far as it suffices; and if nothing perishes, Hajj is performed for him with it; and if something remains from Hajj, it is returned to the heirs, and this is by agreement. And the difference between Hajj and manumission for Abu Hanifa has been mentioned. If he bequeaths a slave worth more than the bequest and he commits a tort and compensation is paid, the bequest is invalid because the payment has been validly made; because the right of the guardian of the tort takes precedence over the right of the testator, so (the slave) leaves his ownership, so it is invalid. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/485) And if he ransoms: i.e., the heirs ransom the slave, and the ransom is from their wealth (not from the bequest), i.e., the bequest is not invalidated because they are the ones who undertook it, and the bequest becomes valid because the slave becomes cleared of the tort, as if he had not committed it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/485)
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest of manumission. The matn states that if a dirham of the bequest perishes, the bequest is not executed, unlike the case of Hajj. The commentary expands on this, presenting the disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest fails entirely if the slave dies or the specified value is diminished, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) argue that it should be executed to the extent possible, by analogy to Hajj. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that manumission has a specific recipient, so executing it with a different value or slave changes the subject. The commentary further explains that this dispute is rooted in a deeper principle about the nature of manumission: is it a right of Allah or a right of the slave? Abu Hanifa considers it a right of the slave, affecting testimonial capacity. The commentary also covers cases where the slave commits a tort and is ransomed by the heirs, concluding that the bequest remains valid in that case.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave, considered a type of qurbah (act of worship) in the context of bequests.
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest or will, a legal disposition that takes effect after death and is limited to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person bequeaths that a slave be bought and freed with 100 dirhams, and the slave dies before being bought, what happens to the bequest?
A) The bequest is executed from the remaining wealth after the slave's death.
B) The bequest is nullified entirely because the intended recipient is not the same.
C) The bequest is executed partially, and the heirs receive the unused portion.
D) The bequest is executed only if the heirs approve.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over manumission bequests hinges on whether the slave is a specific subject or whether the bequest is purely for worship, affecting how much flexibility exists in execution.

Dispute on Timing of Manumission: Heir vs Legatee
Ruling on dispute between legatee and heir over timing of manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for resolving conflicting claims about the timing of manumission in a will and apply it to determine who is believed.

Core Idea
The heir's word is taken as the default; the legatee must prove earlier manumission.

When a testator manumits a slave and a legatee claims the manumission occurred in health (allowing full effect from the estate) while the heir claims it happened in illness (limiting it to one-third), a dispute arises. The Hanafi school provides a clear procedural rule to resolve this: the heir's statement is accepted unless the legatee brings proof. This lesson explores the reasoning and the conditions under which the legatee might still recover something.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
The testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and has a slave. Both Zayd and the heir confirm the slave was manumitted, but disagree on whether it was in health (Zayd) or illness (heir).
The timing affects the financial impact: health = full value from estate; illness = limited to one-third.
2
Determine who is the defendant
The heir is the defendant because he denies the legatee's claim of health-time manumission.
The default legal principle is that the defendant's statement is taken with an oath.
3
Apply the principle of default attribution
Events are attributed to the nearest possible time, which in this case is the period of illness. Thus the heir's claim is consistent with the default.
This is a usul principle: al-asl idafat al-hadith ila aqrab al-awqat.
4
Consider the legatee's recourse
The legatee can still benefit if there is surplus from the one-third after the manumission, or if he provides proof (bayyinah) along with his oath.
Proof must be Islamic legal evidence, e.g., two male witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول للوارث إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد وله عبد، وأقر الموصى له والوارث أن الميت أعتق هذا العبد، فقال الموصى له: أعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث: أعتقه في المرض، فالقول قول الوارث، ولا شيء للموصى له إلا أن يفضل من ثلثه شيء من قيمة العبد، أو يبرهن مع يمينه. ولو ادعى رجل دينا والعبد عتقا، وصدقهما الوارث، سعى في قيمته، وتدفع إلى الغريم، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة لله، وقالا: يعتق ولا يسعى في شيء. وبحقوق الله تعالى قدمت الفرائض كالحج والزكاة والكفارة، وإن تساوت في القوة بدئ بما بدأ به، وبحجة الإسلام أحجوا عنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا.
So the saying is that of the heir if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd, and he has a slave, and the legatee and heir both affirm that the deceased manumitted this slave, but the legatee says: he manumitted him in health, and the heir says: he manumitted him in illness, then the saying is that of the heir, and there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from his third (i.e., from the value of the slave), or he provides proof with his oath. And if a man claims a debt and the slave claims manumission, and the heir affirms both, the slave works to pay his value, and it is given to the creditor, and this according to Abu Hanifa. But the two said: he is free and does not work for anything. And with regard to the rights of Allah, obligatory duties are given precedence, such as Hajj, Zakat, and expiation. If they are equal in strength, start with what the testator started with. And for the Hajj of Islam, let them perform Hajj for him by a man from his town riding.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage treats two separate issues within the book of wills. First, a dispute between a legatee (Zayd) and the heir about whether a manumission occurred in health (when it would be fully effective from the estate) or in illness (when it would be limited to one-third). The ruling is that the heir's statement is taken with an oath, because the default is that events are attributed to the nearest time (illness), and the heir denies the legatee's claim. The legatee only gets something if there is surplus from the slave's value after the manumission. Second, if a slave claims manumission and a creditor claims a debt, and the heir affirms both, Abu Hanifa rules that the slave must work to pay his value to satisfy the debt; the two (Sahibayn) say the slave is free and need not work. This is because Abu Hanifa considers the debt stronger, while the two consider both rights equal. The passage also addresses the priority of bequests for religious obligations: obligatory acts (like Hajj, Zakat, expiation) take precedence over voluntary ones. If multiple obligatory bequests are made, the testator's order should be followed. Lastly, a bequest for Hajj must be performed by a person from the testator's town, riding, as that was the testator's obligation.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'a): The slave works to earn his value to pay the creditor, a type of kitabah imposed by the court.
فروض (furuud): Obligatory religious duties (like Hajj, Zakat, expiation) that are binding on the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the Hanafi rule, whose statement is taken in a dispute between a legatee and an heir about the timing of manumission?
A) The legatee's statement is taken because he is the beneficiary.
B) The heir's statement is taken because the default is to attribute the event to the nearest time (illness).
C) The slave's statement is taken because manumission affects him directly.
D) Both statements are considered equal and the matter goes to a judge.

Key Takeaway
In a dispute over the timing of manumission, the heir's word is accepted by default; the legatee must provide proof or benefit from surplus to recover anything.

Conflict Between Slave's Freedom and Creditor's Debt
Internal Hanafi dispute on the effect of concurrent acknowledgment of debt and manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's ruling and that of the Sahibayn regarding a slave's duty to work when a debt and manumission are both affirmed by the heir.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa makes the slave work to pay his value to the creditor; the Sahibayn free him without payment.

When a deceased person owes a debt and also has a slave whom he manumitted, the heir may affirm both the debt and the manumission. This creates a conflict: the creditor wants payment, and the slave claims freedom. The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf on how to resolve this. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parties and their claims
The creditor claims a debt against the estate. The slave claims he was manumitted by the deceased. The heir affirms both claims.
The heir's affirmation is critical because he would otherwise deny the debt or manumission.
2
Understand the conflict
Both claims cannot be fully satisfied simultaneously: the slave wants immediate freedom without payment, but the creditor wants the slave's value to be available to satisfy the debt.
The slave's value is part of the estate.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the debt is stronger because an acknowledgment of debt is valid from the entire estate even in illness, whereas manumission in illness is like a bequest limited to one-third. The stronger right prevails, but since manumission has occurred and cannot be undone, the slave must work (sa'a) to earn his value, which goes to the creditor.
This is a compromise: the slave becomes free but must pay his value through work.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that both claims are affirmed by the heir in one statement, so they are on equal footing. Therefore, the slave is free without working, and the creditor must seek payment from other assets.
They analogize to a slave manumitted in health, who does not work to pay debts.
5
Determine the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa, the slave works and the creditor gets paid from his earnings. Under the Sahibayn, the slave goes free and the creditor must look to other estate assets.
If the estate has no other assets, the creditor may go unpaid under the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول للوارث إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد وله عبد، وأقر الموصى له والوارث أن الميت أعتق هذا العبد، فقال الموصى له: أعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث: أعتقه في المرض، فالقول قول الوارث، ولا شيء للموصى له إلا أن يفضل من ثلثه شيء من قيمة العبد، أو يبرهن مع يمينه. ولو ادعى رجل دينا والعبد عتقا، وصدقهما الوارث، سعى في قيمته، وتدفع إلى الغريم، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة لله، وقالا: يعتق ولا يسعى في شيء. وبحقوق الله تعالى قدمت الفرائض كالحج والزكاة والكفارة، وإن تساوت في القوة بدئ بما بدأ به، وبحجة الإسلام أحجوا عنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا.
So the saying is that of the heir if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd, and he has a slave, and the legatee and heir both affirm that the deceased manumitted this slave, but the legatee says: he manumitted him in health, and the heir says: he manumitted him in illness, then the saying is that of the heir, and there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from his third (i.e., from the value of the slave), or he provides proof with his oath. But the two said: he is free and does not work for anything. And with regard to the rights of Allah, obligatory duties are given precedence, such as Hajj, Zakat, and expiation. Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal status of a slave when the heir affirms both a debt and the slave's manumission?
A) The slave is sold to pay the debt.

C) The slave is freed immediately without any payment.

Priority of Religious Obligatory Bequests
Rules for prioritizing bequests for religious duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for prioritizing bequests for obligatory religious duties (like Hajj, Zakat, expiation) over voluntary bequests, and apply the testator's order when multiple obligatory bequests are equal.

Core Idea
Obligatory bequests take precedence over voluntary ones; if equal, follow the testator's order.

When a testator makes multiple bequests for religious purposes, some are obligatory (e.g., unpaid Hajj, Zakat, expiation) and some are voluntary. The Hanafi school holds that the obligatory ones must be fulfilled first from the estate, because they are debts owed to Allah. If multiple obligatory bequests are of equal strength, the order prescribed by the testator is followed. This lesson also specifies that a bequest for Hajj should be performed by a person from the testator's town, riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of bequests
Some bequests are for obligatory acts (fara'id) like Hajj, Zakat, and expiation (kaffarah). Others are voluntary (tatawwu').
Obligatory acts are debts owed to Allah.
2
Apply the priority rule
Obligatory bequests are given precedence over voluntary ones because fulfilling obligations is more urgent.
This is based on the principle that rights of Allah (huquq Allah) are not waived lightly.
3
Handle equal strength obligations
If multiple obligatory bequests are of equal strength (e.g., both are fard), the testator's order is followed: start with what he started with.
If the testator mentioned Hajj first, then Hajj is performed first.
4
Implement the Hajj bequest correctly
The Hajj should be performed by a man from the testator's town, riding, as that was the testator's obligation.
This ensures the proxy Hajj matches the testator's duty (if he was capable of riding).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول للوارث إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد وله عبد، وأقر الموصى له والوارث أن الميت أعتق هذا العبد، فقال الموصى له: أعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث: أعتقه في المرض، فالقول قول الوارث، ولا شيء للموصى له إلا أن يفضل من ثلثه شيء من قيمة العبد، أو يبرهن مع يمينه. ولو ادعى رجل دينا والعبد عتقا، وصدقهما الوارث، سعى في قيمته، وتدفع إلى الغريم، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة لله، وقالا: يعتق ولا يسعى في شيء. وبحقوق الله تعالى قدمت الفرائض كالحج والزكاة والكفارة، وإن تساوت في القوة بدئ بما بدأ به، وبحجة الإسلام أحجوا عنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا.

Key Takeaway

8 min
Who is a Neighbor? – Hanafi Definition for Bequests
Defining 'neighbors' for a bequest with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'neighbor' (jār) for bequest purposes and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
For a bequest to 'neighbors,' only adjacent property owners (mulāṣiq) are entitled according to Abu Hanifa – not all local residents.

When a testator leaves a bequest 'to my neighbors,' who qualifies? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition, where Abu Hanifa restricts it to adjacent property owners, while the Sahibayn include all residents of the locality. Understanding this difference is crucial for executing such bequests correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
A testator bequeaths to 'my neighbors.' Who are the intended beneficiaries? The term 'neighbor' requires definition.
The bequest is a gift; proper identification of recipients ensures validity.
2
State Abu Hanifa's definition and evidence
Abu Hanifa defines 'neighbor' as 'mulāṣiq' – those whose property directly adjoins the testator's. His evidence: custom (urf) and the analogy to pre-emption (shuf'a) which is only for adjacent owners.
Pre-emption is a strong parallel: only adjacent owners have the right to pre-empt sale of adjoining property.
3
State the Sahibayn's definition and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad define 'neighbor' as all residents of the same locality who share a mosque. They cite a hadith: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque.'
This hadith implies that mosque-goers are considered neighbors.
4
Note the dismissal of the forty-houses view
The text mentions a view that neighbor includes forty houses on each side, but dismisses it as weak in transmission (da'if).
This view is attributed to other schools (likely Shafi'i/Maliki) but not relied upon in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the definition to different classes of people
The text clarifies that the term applies equally to resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi. A resident slave is included per Abu Hanifa (contrary to Sahibayn). A married woman is excluded because she is dependent on her husband; a widow or mukatab is included.
These nuanced rules show the depth of fiqh in determining eligibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم جيرانه ملاصقوه، وأصهاره كل ذي رحم محرم من امرأته وأختانه زوج أي أصهار الشخص باب الوصية إلخ: إنما أخر هذا الباب عما تقدمه؛ لأنه ذكر في هذا الباب الوصية لقوم مخصوصين، وفيما تقدم ذكر أحكامها على وجه العموم، والخصوص أبدا يتلو العموم وجودا، فكذا ذكرا، ولهذا أوجب أئمة الميزان تقديم الجنس على الفصل. (فتح) جيرانه إلخ أي جيران الشخص ملاصقوه عند أبي حنيفة، حتى إذا أوصى لجيرانه، فهي للملاصقين؛ لأنهم الجيران تسمية وعرفا، ولهذا يجب حق الشفعة لهم، وقالا لهم ولغيرهم ممن سكن محلته، ويجمعهم مسجدها؛ لقوله عليه: "لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد، وعند الثلاثة أربعون دارا من كل جانب؛ لقوله عليه : حق الجار أربعون دارا هكذا ،وهكذا قلنا : هذا ضعيف عند أهل النقل، ويستوي في الجار الساكن والمالك، والذكر والأنثى، والمسلم والذمي؛ لأن الاسم يتناول الكل، ويدخل فيه العبد الساكن عنده، خلافا لهما، بخلاف المكاتب والأرملة تدخل؛ لأن سكناها يضاف إليها، ولا تدخل التي لها بعل؛ لأنها تبع لزوجها، فلم تكن جارا حقيقة [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢]
Chapter of Bequest for Relatives and Others. His neighbors are his adjacent ones, and his in-laws are every blood relative through marriage from his wife and his brothers-in-law, the husband of any in-law of the person. 'Chapter of Bequest etc.': This chapter is placed after previous ones because it mentions bequest for specific groups, while previous chapters dealt with general rulings, and the specific always follows the general in existence, so in presentation. Thus the masters of logic require the genus to precede the species. (Fath) 'His neighbors etc.' means a person's neighbors are his adjacent ones according to Abu Hanifa, so if he bequeaths to his neighbors, it goes to the adjacent ones, because they are neighbors in name and custom, and therefore the right of pre-emption is for them. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: for them and for others who live in his locality and are gathered by its mosque, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque.' According to the three (imams), forty houses on each side, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The right of the neighbor extends to forty houses.' We say: this is weak according to the narrators. And equal regarding the neighbor are the resident and the owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi, because the name includes all. And included is the resident slave living with him, contrary to the two (companions). Unlike the mukatib and the widow are included because her residence is attributed to her; the married woman is not included because she is dependent on her husband, so she is not really a neighbor. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:478]
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a definition with an intra-Hanafi dispute about the meaning of 'neighbors' in a bequest. The chapter is introduced: 'Chapter of Bequest for Relatives and Others.' The author explains that this chapter follows the general chapters because it deals with specific recipients. Then the ruling: 'His neighbors are his adjacent ones' is the definition according to Abu Hanifa. If someone bequeaths to his 'neighbors,' only those whose property directly adjoins the testator's property are entitled. The evidence is custom and the pre-emption rule. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) expand the definition to include all residents of the same locality who pray in the same mosque, citing a hadith about the neighbor of the mosque. They also mention the view of the 'three' (Imams Abu Hanifa? Actually 'the three' might refer to other schools) that neighbor includes forty houses on each side, but the author dismisses that as weak in transmission. The passage then clarifies that the term 'neighbor' includes both resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi. A resident slave is included according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the Sahibayn. A mukatab (slave on contract) and a widow are included because their residence is attributed to them, but a married woman is not included because she is under her husband's authority and not considered a neighbor independently.

Key Terms
جار (jār): Neighbor; in the context of a bequest, defined narrowly by Abu Hanifa as adjacent owner, broadly by Sahibayn as any local resident.
ملاصق (mulāṣiq): Adjacent property owner whose land or house directly touches the testator's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person bequeaths to 'his neighbors,' who receives the bequest?
A) All residents of the locality.
B) Only those whose property directly adjoins the testator's property.
C) Everyone within forty houses.
D) Only Muslims among the neighbors.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, 'neighbor' (jār) is defined as the adjacent property owner (mulāṣiq) unless the testator explicitly intends a broader meaning.

Definition of In-Laws and Brothers-in-Law for Bequest Purposes
Defining in-laws and brothers-in-law for bequest purposes with discussion of scope and condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'sihr' (in-laws) and 'khatan' (brothers-in-law) in the context of bequest (wasiyyah) according to the Hanafi school and identify the marital condition required for eligibility.

Core Idea
For a bequest to include in-laws, the wife must be married or in revocable idda at death.

This passage clarifies who qualifies as an in-law (sihr) and brother-in-law (khatan) when a testator makes a bequest to these relatives. The definition varies between earlier and later custom, but a key condition is the marital status at death: the wife must be in a valid marriage or revocable divorce waiting period. We will explore the definitions, the condition, and the difference in custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms and their definitions
First, note that 'sihr' refers to in-laws (blood relatives of the wife), and 'khatan' refers to brothers-in-law (husbands of female mahram relatives). The text provides broad and narrow definitions.
2
Note the condition for eligibility
The bequest to in-laws only applies if the wife was married to the testator at death or in a revocable divorce waiting period (idda of raj'i). If the wife is in a final divorce (ba'in or triple), the in-laws do not qualify.
This condition is crucial for validity.
3
Compare earlier broad definition with later restricted definition
According to earlier custom (and the preferred view of Muhammad and Abu Ubayd), all mahram relatives of the wife are in-laws. In later custom, 'sihr' is often restricted to the wife's parents, and 'khatan' to the husband of the daughter.
Both views are recognized; local custom may determine the operative rule.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
Take a testator who bequeaths to 'my in-laws'. If his wife is in a revocable idda at his death, her parents (and other mahram) are eligible. If she is in a ba'in idda, they are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل ذي رحم: قال الحلواني: هذا في عرفهم وأما في عرفنا فيختص بأبويها، كذا في "العناية" وغيرها، وأقره القهستاني لكن جزم في البرهان" وغيره بالأول، وأقره في "الشرنبلالية" كذا في "الدر". (فتح) امرأته كآبائها وأعمامها وأخوالها وأخواتها وغيرهم بشرط موته وهي منكوحته أو معتدته من رجعي. (طائي)] لأنه عليه لما تزوج جويرية أعتق كل من ملك من ذي رحم محرم منها إكراما لها، وكانوا يسمون أصهار النبي كذا في "الفتح"، وهذا تفسير اختيار محمد وأبي عبيد، وفي الصحاح : الأصهار أهل بيت المرأة، ولم يقيد بالمحرم، ونقل عن الفراء وابن عباس في تفسير الصهر غير ما ذكر ذكره الإمام العيني، من شاء فلينظر فيه. قال في "ملا" مسكين": وكذا يدخل فيه كل ذي رحم محرم من زوجة أبيه وزوجة ابنه وزوجة كل ذي رحم محرم منه، وإنما يدخل تحت الوصية من كان صهر الموصي يوم موته بأن كانت المرأة منكوحة له عند الموت، أو معتدة عنه بطلاق رجعي، حتى لو مات الموصي والمرأة في نكاحه أو في عدته طلاق من رجعي، فالصهر يستحق الوصية، وإن كانت في عدة من طلاق بائن أو ثلاث، فلا يستحقها. وأختانه إلخ : أي أختان الشخص زوج كل ذات رحم محرم منه كأزواج البنات والعمات والخالات؛ لأن الكل ختنا، وكذا كل ذي رحم محرم من أزواجهن؛ لأنهم يسمون أختانا، وقيل: هذا في عرفهم، وفي عرفنا لا يتناول الأزواج المحارم، ويستوي فيه الحر والعبد [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٧/٢] وفي "الطائي": قيل: هذا في عرفهم، وفي عرفنا الصهر أبو المرأة ،وأمها والختن زوج المحرم فقط، وفي "القهستاني": وينبغي في ديارنا أن يختص الصهر بأبي الزوجة، والختن بزوج البنت؛ لأنه المشهور كذا في "الدر".
'Every blood relative (dhi rahim]': Al-Halwani said: 'This is according to their custom, but according to our custom it is restricted to her parents.' So in al-'Inaya and others, and al-Qahustani confirmed it, but in al-Burhan and others he definitively stated the first, and it was confirmed in al-Sharnablaliyya, so in al-Durr. (Fath) 'His wife' like her fathers, uncles (paternal and maternal), sisters, etc., provided he dies while she is his wife or in a revocable divorce (raj'i). (Ta'i) Because when he (peace be upon him) married Juwayriyya, he freed every mahram relative from her side in her honor, and they were called the in-laws (as-har) of the Prophet. So in al-Fath, and this is the interpretation chosen by Muhammad and Abu Ubayd. In al-Sihah: 'The in-laws (as-har) are the family of the wife,' and he did not restrict it to mahram. It is narrated from al-Farra' and Ibn 'Abbas regarding the interpretation of al-sihr other than what was mentioned, mentioned by al-'Ayni; whoever wishes may look into it. In 'Mulla Miskeen': 'Likewise included is every mahram relative from the wife of his father, the wife of his son, and the wife of every mahram relative of his.' Only the in-law of the testator at the time of his death is included in the bequest, meaning the woman should be married to him at death or in a revocable divorce. So if the testator dies while the woman is in his marriage or in her waiting period from a revocable divorce, then the in-law (sihr) is entitled to the bequest. If she is in the waiting period of a final divorce (ba'in) or triple divorce, he does not receive it. 'And his brothers-in-law (akhtan) etc.' means the brothers-in-law of a person are the husband of every female mahram relative, like husbands of daughters, aunts (paternal and maternal), etc. Because all are akhtan. Likewise every mahram relative from their wives because they are called akhtan. It is said: this is according to their custom; in our custom it does not include the husbands of mahram relatives. And it is equal whether free or slave. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:487] In al-Ta'i: It is said: this is according to their custom; in our custom, al-sihr is the father of the woman and her mother, and al-khatan is only the husband of the mahram relative. In al-Qahustani: 'In our lands, it is appropriate that al-sihr be restricted to the wife's father, and al-khatan to the husband of the daughter, because that is well-known.' So in al-Durr.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage continues the definition of in-laws (أصهار) and brothers-in-law (أختان) for bequest purposes. It begins with a note on the definition of 'every blood relative' (كل ذي رحم) from earlier: according to Al-Halwani, in their custom it meant all relatives, but in our custom it is restricted to parents. Then it defines 'his wife' as including all her blood relatives (fathers, uncles, aunts, etc.) provided that at the time of death the wife was in a valid marriage or in a revocable divorce waiting period (idda of raj'i). This is supported by the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) freed the mahram relatives of Juwayriyya, and they were called his 'as-har'. The text cites various authorities (Muhammad, Abu Ubayd, al-Sihah) and mentions differences in interpretation. The key condition for eligibility: the testator must be married to the woman at death or in a revocable divorce; if the woman is in the waiting period of a final divorce (ba'in or triple), the in-laws do not qualify. Then it defines 'akhtan' (brothers-in-law) as husbands of female mahram relatives such as daughters, aunts, etc. There is a difference between earlier custom and current custom: in earlier custom, all such husbands were considered akhtan; in later custom, the term is often restricted. The text notes that in some regions, 'sihr' is limited to the wife's parents, and 'khatan' to the husband of the daughter. The ruling is independent of slave or free status.

Key Terms
صهر (sihr): In-law; relative by marriage through the wife. Defined broadly as every mahram relative of the wife, but in later custom restricted to the wife's parents.
ختن (khatan): Brother-in-law; husband of a female mahram relative (daughter, aunt, etc.) or vice versa. In later custom, often limited to husband of daughter.
محرم (mahram): Blood relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden (father, brother, son, uncle, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a person considered an in-law (sihr) for the purpose of a bequest according to the Hanafi school?
A) If the woman was legally married to the testator at death or in a revocable divorce waiting period.
B) If the woman was in a final divorce waiting period.
C) If the woman was divorced before death.
D) Only if the woman was alive at the time of bequest.

Key Takeaway
The eligibility of in-laws in a bequest hinges on the wife's marital status at the testator's death, and the scope of the term may be shaped by local custom.
