Bequest to Heirs: The Male Double Female Share Rule
Explains ruling of bequest to relatives with male-female distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for distributing a bequest made to the heirs of a person and identify the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A bequest to heirs is distributed like inheritance: male takes double female.

This passage from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq commentary addresses a common scenario: someone bequeaths one-third of their estate to the heirs of a specific person. How should that bequest be divided among the heirs? The text explains that the distribution follows the inheritance rule of male receiving double the female share, and it conditions the bequest on the death of that person before the testator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'And for the heirs of so-and-so, for the male the share of two females.' This is the core ruling: a bequest to the heirs of a named person is distributed with males getting double the female share.
This applies only when the bequest is to 'heirs' (ورثة), not to 'children' (أولاد) directly.
2
Locate the proof
The commentary cites the Quranic verse (2:233): 'And upon the heir is the like of that.' This verse establishes that the term 'heir' triggers inheritance rules, so the bequest follows the same distribution.
The proof is dalil naqli from the Quran, showing that the ruling is derived from the text.
3
Understand the derivation
The term 'warith' (heir) is derived from 'wirathah' (inheritance). The attachment of the ruling to this derivative indicates that the cause ('illah) is the relationship of inheritance. Therefore, the distribution mirrors inheritance shares.
This is a key principle in Hanafi usul: the name derived from a meaning invokes that meaning.
4
Note the condition
The text states that the bequest is valid only if the person whose heirs are bequeathed (e.g., Zaid) dies before the testator. Otherwise, the bequest is void because the heirs cannot be identified.
This condition is specific to bequests to the heirs of a living person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
ولورثة فلان للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين.
باسم الولد، واسم الولد يطلق على الإناث حالة الانفراد كما يطلق على الذكور، ثم في مسألتنا إن لم يكن لفلان إلا ولد واحد كان الثلث كله له بخلاف ما لو أوصى لأولاد فلان، وله ولد واحد، فإنه يستحق النصف، ووجه الفرق: أن الأولاد جمع، وأقل الجمع في باب الوصية والميراث اثنان فكان للواحد النصف، كما لو أوصى لأقربائه، وله عم واحد كان له النصف، وأما الولد فليس باسم جمع، فإنما هو اسم جنس، ومطلق اسم الجنس يطلق على أدنى ما يطلق عليه الاسم، كما لو حلف لا يشرب الماء، ولا يتزوج النساء، حيث يحنث بشرب قطرة، ونكاح واحدة، وإذا أوصى لأولاد فلان وليس لفلان أولاد صلبية يدخل في الوصية أولاد البنين، وهل يدخل أولاد البنات؟ فيه روايتان.
للذكر مثل حظ إلخ: يعني لورثة فلان يدفع للذكر قدر حظ الأنثيين؛ لأنه اسم مشتق من الوراثة، وترتب الاسم على المشتق يدل على العلية، ألا ترى أن الله تعالى لما نص على الوراثة بقوله: ﴿وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٣)، ترتب الحكم عليها حتى وجبت النفقة بقدرها، ثم شرط هذه الوصية أن يموت فلان الموصى لورثته قبل موت الموصي، حتى يعرف ورثته منهم حتى لو مات الموصي قبل موت الموصى لورثته، بطلت الوصية، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لولده ولو كان مع ورثته موصى له آخر قسم بينهم وبينه على الرؤوس، ثم ما أصاب الورثة جمع، وقسم بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٥/٩]
Book of Wills: Bequest to relatives and others. And for the heirs of so-and-so, for the male the share of two females. By the name of child (walad), and the name walad applies to females when alone as it applies to males. Then in our issue, if so-and-so has only one child (walad), the whole third is for him, contrary to if he bequeaths to the children (awlad) of so-and-so and he has one child, then he deserves half. The difference is that awlad is a plural, and the minimum of plural in the chapter of bequest and inheritance is two, so the one gets half, as if he bequeaths to his relatives and he has one paternal uncle, he gets half. As for walad, it is not a plural name; it is a generic name, and the absolute generic name applies to the minimum to which the name applies, as if he swears not to drink water or not to marry women, he breaks the oath by drinking a drop and marrying one. If he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so and so-and-so has no direct children, the children of sons enter the bequest. And do the children of daughters enter? There are two narrations. Commentary on 'for the male the share of two females': meaning for the heirs of so-and-so, the male is given the share of two females because it is a name derived from inheritance (wirathah), and the attachment of the name to the derivative indicates causation (illah). Do you not see that Allah, when He legislated inheritance by His saying 'And upon the heir is the like of that' (Quran 2:233), the ruling was attached to it so that maintenance was obligatory according to it. Then the condition of this bequest is that so-and-so (the person bequeathed to his heirs) dies before the testator so that his heirs are known; if the testator dies before the death of the person bequeathed to his heirs, the bequest becomes void. Contrary to if he bequeaths to his child, even if with his heirs there is another legatee, they divide among them per capita, then what falls to the heirs is collected and divided among them with the male having the share of two females.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on wills (al-wasaya) concerning bequests to relatives and others, particularly the distribution of a bequest to the 'heirs' of a named person. The text first states the general rule: if one bequeaths to the heirs of so-and-so, the distribution is for the male the share of two females. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the word 'warith' (heir) is derived from 'wirathah' (inheritance), and the attachment of the ruling to this derivative indicates that the cause ('illah) is the relationship of inheritance. The commentator cites the Quranic verse (Quran 2:233) as evidence that the ruling of maintenance was attached to the heir, and similarly here the distribution follows the inheritance share. The text then distinguishes between the word 'walad' (child, singular) and 'awlad' (children, plural). If the bequest is to 'awlad' (children) and the person has only one child, that child gets only half of the bequeathed third because 'awlad' is a plural requiring at least two, so one child takes half as if he were one of two. But if the bequest is to 'walad' (offspring), and there is only one child, the entire third goes to that child because 'walad' is a generic name applying to one or more. This is illustrated with an example of an oath: swearing not to drink water is broken by a single drop. The passage also addresses a secondary issue: if the bequest is to the children of so-and-so and he has no direct children, the children of sons enter; whether children of daughters enter is subject to two narrations (riwayatan) within the Hanafi school. Finally, the commentary adds a condition: the bequest to the heirs of someone is valid only if that person dies before the testator so that his heirs are identifiable. If the testator dies first, the bequest is void. However, if the testator also has another legatee, they divide per capita among the children, and then the heirs' portion is distributed according to the male:female ratio.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A legal disposition of property or usufruct to take effect after the testator's death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
الورثة (al-warathah): Heirs; those who inherit from a deceased person. In this context, it refers to the heirs of the person named in the bequest.
الولد (al-walad): Offspring, singular but generic; applies to one or more and includes males and females.
للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين (li al-dhakari mithlu hazz al-unthayayn): A distribution rule where a male receives twice the share of a female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for a bequest to 'the heirs of Zaid' to be valid?
A) Zaid must be alive at the testator's death.
B) Zaid must die before the testator.
C) Zaid must consent to the bequest.
D) The bequest must be to Zaid himself.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to the heirs of a person is distributed according to inheritance shares (male doubles female) and requires that the person dies before the testator.

Walad vs Awlad: Singular vs Plural in Bequests
Explains ruling of bequest to relatives with male-female distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a bequest to 'walad' and 'awlad' and state the Hanafi position on including grandchildren.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'awlad' gives a single child only half; to 'walad' gives the whole third.

The same passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq also clarifies a crucial terminological distinction in bequests: the difference between the singular generic term 'walad' (child) and the plural 'awlad' (children). This distinction has practical consequences for how much a single child receives when named as a beneficiary. Furthermore, the text addresses whether grandchildren through daughters are included in a bequest to 'children'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text contrasts two cases: (1) bequest to 'walad' (singular generic) when there is only one child, and (2) bequest to 'awlad' (plural) when there is only one child.
The same number of children (one) produces different results depending on the wording.
2
Apply the semantic rule
In Hanafi fiqh, 'walad' is a generic term (ism jins) that applies to the minimum of the category (one). 'Awlad' is a plural that requires at least two. Therefore, a bequest to 'awlad' when there is only one child gives that child only half (because half is the share of one child if there were two).
This is based on the principle that the minimum of plural in bequest and inheritance is two.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text notes that when the bequest is to 'children' (أولاد) and the person has no direct children, the children of sons are included. Whether children of daughters are included is subject to two narrations (riwayatan) within the Hanafi school.
This dispute has practical implications for how far the bequest extends.

Source Text

الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
ولورثة فلان للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين.
باسم الولد، واسم الولد يطلق على الإناث حالة الانفراد كما يطلق على الذكور، ثم في مسألتنا إن لم يكن لفلان إلا ولد واحد كان الثلث كله له بخلاف ما لو أوصى لأولاد فلان، وله ولد واحد، فإنه يستحق النصف، ووجه الفرق: أن الأولاد جمع، وأقل الجمع في باب الوصية والميراث اثنان فكان للواحد النصف، كما لو أوصى لأقربائه، وله عم واحد كان له النصف، وأما الولد فليس باسم جمع، فإنما هو اسم جنس، ومطلق اسم الجنس يطلق على أدنى ما يطلق عليه الاسم، كما لو حلف لا يشرب الماء، ولا يتزوج النساء، حيث يحنث بشرب قطرة، ونكاح واحدة، وإذا أوصى لأولاد فلان وليس لفلان أولاد صلبية يدخل في الوصية أولاد البنين، وهل يدخل أولاد البنات؟ فيه روايتان.
للذكر مثل حظ إلخ: يعني لورثة فلان يدفع للذكر قدر حظ الأنثيين؛ لأنه اسم مشتق من الوراثة، وترتب الاسم على المشتق يدل على العلية، ألا ترى أن الله تعالى لما نص على الوراثة بقوله: ﴿وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٣)، ترتب الحكم عليها حتى وجبت النفقة بقدرها، ثم شرط هذه الوصية أن يموت فلان الموصى لورثته قبل موت الموصي، حتى يعرف ورثته منهم حتى لو مات الموصي قبل موت الموصى لورثته، بطلت الوصية، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لولده ولو كان مع ورثته موصى له آخر قسم بينهم وبينه على الرؤوس، ثم ما أصاب الورثة جمع، وقسم بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٥/٩]
Book of Wills: Bequest to relatives and others. And for the heirs of so-and-so, for the male the share of two females. By the name of child (walad), and the name walad applies to females when alone as it applies to males. Then in our issue, if so-and-so has only one child (walad), the whole third is for him, contrary to if he bequeaths to the children (awlad) of so-and-so and he has one child, then he deserves half. The difference is that awlad is a plural, and the minimum of plural in the chapter of bequest and inheritance is two, so the one gets half, as if he bequeaths to his relatives and he has one paternal uncle, he gets half. As for walad, it is not a plural name; it is a generic name, and the absolute generic name applies to the minimum to which the name applies, as if he swears not to drink water or not to marry women, he breaks the oath by drinking a drop and marrying one. If he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so and so-and-so has no direct children, the children of sons enter the bequest. And do the children of daughters enter? There are two narrations. Commentary on 'for the male the share of two females': meaning for the heirs of so-and-so, the male is given the share of two females because it is a name derived from inheritance (wirathah), and the attachment of the name to the derivative indicates causation (illah). Do you not see that Allah, when He legislated inheritance by His saying 'And upon the heir is the like of that' (Quran 2:233), the ruling was attached to it so that maintenance was obligatory according to it. Then the condition of this bequest is that so-and-so (the person bequeathed to his heirs) dies before the testator so that his heirs are known; if the testator dies before the death of the person bequeathed to his heirs, the bequest becomes void. Contrary to if he bequeaths to his child, even if with his heirs there is another legatee, they divide among them per capita, then what falls to the heirs is collected and divided among them with the male having the share of two females.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on wills (al-wasaya) concerning bequests to relatives and others, particularly the distribution of a bequest to the 'heirs' of a named person. The text first states the general rule: if one bequeaths to the heirs of so-and-so, the distribution is for the male the share of two females. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the word 'warith' (heir) is derived from 'wirathah' (inheritance), and the attachment of the ruling to this derivative indicates that the cause ('illah) is the relationship of inheritance. The commentator cites the Quranic verse (Quran 2:233) as evidence that the ruling of maintenance was attached to the heir, and similarly here the distribution follows the inheritance share. The text then distinguishes between the word 'walad' (child, singular) and 'awlad' (children, plural). If the bequest is to 'awlad' (children) and the person has only one child, that child gets only half of the bequeathed third because 'awlad' is a plural requiring at least two, so one child takes half as if he were one of two. But if the bequest is to 'walad' (offspring), and there is only one child, the entire third goes to that child because 'walad' is a generic name applying to one or more. This is illustrated with an example of an oath: swearing not to drink water is broken by a single drop. The passage also addresses a secondary issue: if the bequest is to the children of so-and-so and he has no direct children, the children of sons enter; whether children of daughters enter is subject to two narrations (riwayatan) within the Hanafi school. Finally, the commentary adds a condition: the bequest to the heirs of someone is valid only if that person dies before the testator so that his heirs are identifiable. If the testator dies first, the bequest is void. However, if the testator also has another legatee, they divide per capita among the children, and then the heirs' portion is distributed according to the male:female ratio.

Key Terms
الولد (al-walad): Offspring, singular but generic; applies to one or more.
الأولاد (al-awlad): Children, plural; requires at least two in the context of wills and inheritance.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A legal disposition of property to take effect after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third to 'the children of Zaid' and Zaid has only one son, what fraction of the one-third does the son receive?
A) The entire one-third.
B) Half of the one-third.
C) One-third of the one-third.
D) Nothing; the bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the term 'awlad' (children) in a bequest requires at least two beneficiaries; a single child receives only half the bequeathed amount.

Validity of Bequest of Usufruct
Establishes validity of bequest of usufruct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates the bequest of usufruct and state the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Bequest of usufruct is valid by analogy to lifetime transfers; it is a transfer of ownership of the benefit, not the asset.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling that a testator may bequeath the service of a slave or the dwelling of a house. The text establishes that usufructs (manafi') can be owned separately from the physical asset, and this ownership can be transferred after death just as it can during life, due to the principle of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being bequeathed? The service of a slave or the dwelling of a house. The ruling is that such a bequest is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The text provides an analogy (qiyas): since usufruct can be transferred during life for compensation or gratuitously, the same applies after death due to need.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative reasoning is that the rule for lifetime transfers extends to post-death transfers because the underlying cause (need and permissibility of owning usufruct) is the same.
4
Note the conditions
The bequest must be of a known usufruct (e.g., service, dwelling) and the duration must be specified or left indefinite (implying forever).

باب الوصية إلخ: لما فرغ عن بيان الوصية المتعلقة بالأعيان، شرع في بيان الوصية المتعلقة بالمنافع، وأخر هذا الباب؛ لأن المنافع بعد الأعيان وجودا، فأخرها عنها وضعا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٥/٩] وتصح الوصية إلخ: لأن المنافع يصح تمليكها في حال الحياة ببدل أو بغير بدل، فكذا بعد الممات للحاجة، كما في حكم الأعيان، ويكون محبوسا على ملك الميت في حق المنفعة، حتى يستوفيه الموصى له على ملكه كما يستوفي الموقوف عليه المنافع على حكم ملك الواقف تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٦/٩] وأبدا إلخ: وإن أوصى بخدمة مطلقة غير موقتة يتناول الأبد، وإن أوصى سنين يتناول ثلاث سنين، وكذا الوصية بغلة العبد والدار. (ملا مسكين) ثلثه بأن كانت قيمة العبد مثل ثلث ماله أو أقل ملا مسكين سلم إليه إلخ لأن حق الموصى له في الثلث لا يزاحمه الورثة فيه، وكذلك سكنى الدار، وليس له أن يؤاجر العبد ولا الدار؛ لأنه ملك المنفعة بغير عوض، فلا يملك تمليكها بعوض رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٩/٢] وإلا خدم إلخ: أي وإن لم يخرج من الثلث بأن لا مال له غيره ملا مسكين خدم الورثة يومين، وخدم الموصى له يوما؛ لأن حقه في الثلث، وحقهم في الثلثين، هذا إذا كانت الوصية غير موقتة، وإن كانت موقتة بوقت كالسنة مثلا، فإن كانت السنة غير معينة يخدم الورثة يومين والموصى له يوما إلى أن تمضي ثلاث سنين، فإذا مضت يسلم إلى الورثة؛ لأن الموصى له استوفى حقه، وإن كانت معينة، فإن مضت السنة قبل موت الموصي، بطلت الوصية، وإن مات قبل مضيها يخدم الموصى له يوما والورثة يومين إلى أن تمضي تلك السنة، فإذا مضت سلم إلى الورثة، وكذا الحكم لو مات الموصي بعد مضي بعضها، بخلاف الوصية بسكنى الدار إذا كانت لا تخرج الثلث من حيث تقسم عين الدار أثلاثا للانتفاع بها؛ لإمكان قسمة عين الدار أجزاء، وهو أعدل للتسوية بينهما زمانا وذاتا، وفي المهايأة تقديم أحدهما زمانا ولو اقتسموا الدار مهايأة من حيث الزمان يجوز أيضا؛ لأن الحق لهم إلا أن الأول أولى؛ لكونه أعدل رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٩/٢]

وبموته إلخ: أي بموت الموصى له يعود العبد أو الدار إلى ورثة الموصي؛ لأنه أوجب الحق للموصى المنافع على حكم ملكه، فلو انتقل إلى وارث الموصى له استحقها أبدا من ملك الموصي بغير رضاه، وذلك غير جائز. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٠/٩]
Chapter on bequest of service, dwelling, and fruit. And the bequest of the service of his slave and the dwelling of his house is valid for a specified period or forever. If the slave comes out of his third (i.e., its value is within one third of the estate), it is handed over to him to serve him; otherwise, the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day. And upon his death, it returns to the heirs of the testator. Commentary: Chapter etc.: after finishing the explanation of bequests related to physical assets, he started explaining bequests related to usufructs, and delayed this chapter because usufructs come after assets in existence, so he delayed them in arrangement. And 'the bequest is valid' because it is permissible to transfer ownership of usufructs during life for a consideration or without, so also after death due to need, just like the ruling for physical assets. And it becomes retained (mahbus) on the ownership of the deceased regarding the usufruct until the legatee receives it on his ownership just as the beneficiary of a waqf receives the usufruct under the ownership of the waqif. And 'forever' etc.: if he bequeaths an absolute service not timed, it includes forever; if he bequeaths for years, it includes three years, and similarly the bequest of the produce of the slave and the house. (Mulla Miskin) 'if it comes out of his third': meaning if the value of the slave is equal to one third of his wealth or less, it is handed over to him because the right of the legatee in the third is not competed by the heirs. And also the dwelling of the house, and he does not have the right to lease the slave or the house because he owns the usufruct without compensation, so he does not have the right to transfer it for compensation. 'Otherwise serve' etc.: i.e., if it does not come out of the third, as he has no wealth besides it, then the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day because his right is in one third and their right is in two thirds. This is if the bequest is not timed. If it is timed with a time like a year, for example, if the year is not specified, the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day until three years pass; when they pass, it is handed over to the heirs because the legatee has received his right. If it is specified, and the year passes before the testator's death, the bequest becomes void; if he dies before its passing, the legatee serves one day and the heirs two days until that year passes; when it passes, it is handed over to the heirs. And similarly the ruling if the testator dies after some of it has passed. This is contrary to the bequest of the dwelling of a house if it does not come out of the third in terms of the physical house being divided into thirds for utilization because it is possible to divide the physical house into parts, and it is more equitable for equalizing them in time and substance. In the case of rotation (muhayah), one of them is given precedence in time; and if they divide the house by rotation in terms of time, it is also permissible because the right is theirs, except that the first (division in kind) is better because it is more equitable. 'And upon his death' i.e., upon the death of the legatee, the slave or house returns to the heirs of the testator because he obligated the right of the usufruct to the legatee under the ownership of the testator; if it were to transfer to the legatee's heir, he would be entitled to it forever from the testator's property without his consent, and that is not permissible.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on bequests of usufructs (manafi'), such as the service of a slave and the dwelling of a house. The main text states that such a bequest is valid for a specified duration or forever. The rationale, as explained in the commentary, is that usufructs can be transferred ownership in life, whether for payment (like rent) or for free, so the same applies after death by analogy (qiyas). The usufruct is considered to remain on the deceased's ownership until the legatee receives it. If the value of the slave (or the usufruct right) falls within one third of the estate, it is given to the legatee. If not, because the testator has no other property, the legatee gets only one day of service while the heirs get two days, proportionally to the thirds. This division applies to untimed bequests; for timed bequests, the calculation adjusts to ensure the legatee gets his full right over the period. The passage also discusses the case of the bequest of dwelling: if the house does not exceed the third, it is divided physically into three parts for simultaneous use, which is the most equitable. Alternatively, they may rotate (muhayah) by time. Upon the death of the legatee, the usufruct reverts to the testator's heirs, because the legatee's right ends, and the property cannot pass to the legatee's heirs without the testator's consent.

Key Terms
الخدمة (al-khidmah): Service, specifically the labor of a slave bequeathed to a legatee.
السكنى (al-sukna): Dwelling, the right to live in a house for a specified period or forever.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One third of the estate, the maximum proportion that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A specific hadith about bequest of services.
B) Analogy (qiyas) to lifetime transfers of usufruct.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) It is invalid; only physical assets can be bequeathed.

Key Takeaway
Bequest of usufruct (service, dwelling, fruit) is valid in Hanafi law by analogy to lifetime transfers, provided the usufruct is known and the duration is specified or indefinite.

Dividing Usufruct When the Bequest Exceeds One-Third
Explains division when bequest exceeds one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional division of usufruct when a bequest of service or dwelling exceeds one-third of the estate, distinguishing between timed and untimed bequests.

Core Idea
When a usufruct bequest exceeds the third, the legatee gets one-third of the time, and the heirs two-thirds; for timed bequests, the method adjusts to ensure full enjoyment over the period.

This lesson addresses a common practical issue: what happens when the value of a bequeathed usufruct exceeds the one-third limit of the estate? The Hanafi school employs a proportional division by time, balancing the legatee's right to one-third with the heirs' right to two-thirds. The text explains the rules for both untimed and timed bequests, including specific scenarios like specified vs. unspecified years.

Guided Path
1
Determine if the bequest exceeds the third
First, assess whether the value of the usufruct (e.g., service of a slave, dwelling) is within one-third of the estate. If yes, the legatee gets full use. If not, proceed to division.
2
Apply the proportional rule for untimed bequests
If the usufruct is bequeathed indefinitely (untimed), the legatee uses the property one day, the heirs two days, cycling continuously.
3
Adjust for timed bequests
If the bequest is for a specific period (e.g., one year), the legatee gets one-third of that period: for a one-year bequest, the legatee gets one day, heirs two days, until the year ends. If the year is unspecified, the division continues for three years.
4
Handle special timing scenarios
If the testator dies after part of the specified period has passed, the division only applies to the remaining part. If the entire specified period passes before death (without the testator dying), the bequest becomes void.

(ملا مسكين) ثلثه بأن كانت قيمة العبد مثل ثلث ماله أو أقل ملا مسكين سلم إليه إلخ لأن حق الموصى له في الثلث لا يزاحمه الورثة فيه، وكذلك سكنى الدار، وليس له أن يؤاجر العبد ولا الدار؛ لأنه ملك المنفعة بغير عوض، فلا يملك تمليكها بعوض رمز الحقائق: ٤٨٩/٢] وإلا خدم إلخ: أي وإن لم يخرج من الثلث بأن لا مال له غيره ملا مسكين خدم الورثة يومين، وخدم الموصى له يوما؛ لأن حقه في الثلث، وحقهم في الثلثين، هذا إذا كانت الوصية غير موقتة، وإن كانت موقتة بوقت كالسنة مثلا، فإن كانت السنة غير معينة يخدم الورثة يومين والموصى له يوما إلى أن تمضي ثلاث سنين، فإذا مضت يسلم إلى الورثة؛ لأن الموصى له استوفى حقه، وإن كانت معينة، فإن مضت السنة قبل موت الموصي، بطلت الوصية، وإن مات قبل مضيها يخدم الموصى له يوما والورثة يومين إلى أن تمضي تلك السنة، فإذا مضت سلم إلى الورثة، وكذا الحكم لو مات الموصي بعد مضي بعضها، بخلاف الوصية بسكنى الدار إذا كانت لا تخرج الثلث من حيث تقسم عين الدار أثلاثا للانتفاع بها؛ لإمكان قسمة عين الدار أجزاء، وهو أعدل للتسوية بينهما زمانا وذاتا، وفي المهايأة تقديم أحدهما زمانا ولو اقتسموا الدار مهايأة من حيث الزمان يجوز أيضا؛ لأن الحق لهم إلا أن الأول أولى؛ لكونه أعدل رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٩/٢]
له؛ ليستوفي
وبموته إلخ: أي بموت الموصى له يعود العبد أو الدار إلى ورثة الموصي؛ لأنه أوجب الحق للموصى المنافع على حكم ملكه، فلو انتقل إلى وارث الموصى له استحقها أبدا من ملك الموصي بغير رضاه، وذلك غير جائز. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٠/٩]
Chapter on bequest of service, dwelling, and fruit. And the bequest of the service of his slave and the dwelling of his house is valid for a specified period or forever. If the slave comes out of his third (i.e., its value is within one third of the estate), it is handed over to him to serve him; otherwise, the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day. And upon his death, it returns to the heirs of the testator. Commentary: Chapter etc.: after finishing the explanation of bequests related to physical assets, he started explaining bequests related to usufructs, and delayed this chapter because usufructs come after assets in existence, so he delayed them in arrangement. And 'the bequest is valid' because it is permissible to transfer ownership of usufructs during life for a consideration or without, so also after death due to need, just like the ruling for physical assets. And it becomes retained (mahbus) on the ownership of the deceased regarding the usufruct until the legatee receives it on his ownership just as the beneficiary of a waqf receives the usufruct under the ownership of the waqif. And 'forever' etc.: if he bequeaths an absolute service not timed, it includes forever; if he bequeaths for years, it includes three years, and similarly the bequest of the produce of the slave and the house. (Mulla Miskin) 'if it comes out of his third': meaning if the value of the slave is equal to one third of his wealth or less, it is handed over to him because the right of the legatee in the third is not competed by the heirs. And also the dwelling of the house, and he does not have the right to lease the slave or the house because he owns the usufruct without compensation, so he does not have the right to transfer it for compensation. 'Otherwise serve' etc.: i.e., if it does not come out of the third, as he has no wealth besides it, then the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day because his right is in one third and their right is in two thirds. This is if the bequest is not timed. If it is timed with a time like a year, for example, if the year is not specified, the heirs serve two days and the legatee one day until three years pass; when they pass, it is handed over to the heirs because the legatee has received his right. If it is specified, and the year passes before the testator's death, the bequest becomes void; if he dies before its passing, the legatee serves one day and the heirs two days until that year passes; when it passes, it is handed over to the heirs. And similarly the ruling if the testator dies after some of it has passed. This is contrary to the bequest of the dwelling of a house if it does not come out of the third in terms of the physical house being divided into thirds for utilization because it is possible to divide the physical house into parts, and it is more equitable for equalizing them in time and substance. In the case of rotation (muhayah), one of them is given precedence in time; and if they divide the house by rotation in terms of time, it is also permissible because the right is theirs, except that the first (division in kind) is better because it is more equitable. 'And upon his death' i.e., upon the death of the legatee, the slave or house returns to the heirs of the testator because he obligated the right of the usufruct to the legatee under the ownership of the testator; if it were to transfer to the legatee's heir, he would be entitled to it forever from the testator's property without his consent, and that is not permissible.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on bequests of usufructs (manafi'), such as the service of a slave and the dwelling of a house. The main text states that such a bequest is valid for a specified duration or forever. The rationale, as explained in the commentary, is that usufructs can be transferred ownership in life, whether for payment (like rent) or for free, so the same applies after death by analogy (qiyas). The usufruct is considered to remain on the deceased's ownership until the legatee receives it. If the value of the slave (or the usufruct right) falls within one third of the estate, it is given to the legatee. If not, because the testator has no other property, the legatee gets only one day of service while the heirs get two days, proportionally to the thirds. This division applies to untimed bequests; for timed bequests, the calculation adjusts to ensure the legatee gets his full right over the period. The passage also discusses the case of the bequest of dwelling: if the house does not exceed the third, it is divided physically into three parts for simultaneous use, which is the most equitable. Alternatively, they may rotate (muhayah) by time. Upon the death of the legatee, the usufruct reverts to the testator's heirs, because the legatee's right ends, and the property cannot pass to the legatee's heirs without the testator's consent.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One third of the estate, the maximum proportion that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.
الخدمة (al-khidmah): Service, specifically the labor of a slave bequeathed to a legatee.
السكنى (al-sukna): Dwelling, the right to live in a house for a specified period or forever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths the service of his slave for life (untimed). The slave is the only asset, valued at $100,000, while the estate is $100,000 ($33,333 third). What is the correct division?
A) The legatee gets the service for one day, the heirs for two days, cycling forever.
B) The legatee gets the service for one-third of each day only.
C) The bequest is invalid because the entire estate is consumed.
D) The slave is sold and proceeds divided.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest of usufruct exceeds one-third without other assets, the legatee's enjoyment is reduced proportionally: one-third of the time for untimed bequests, and the same ratio applied to the specified period for timed bequests.

Muhayah and Reversion of Usufruct upon Legatee's Death
Discusses division of dwelling and reversion of usufruct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between physical division and muhayah (rotation) for dwelling bequests, and state the ruling that usufruct reverts to the testator's heirs upon the legatee's death.

Core Idea
For dwelling, physical division of the house into parts is more equitable than time-based rotation; upon the legatee's death, the usufruct automatically reverts to the testator's heirs.

This lesson covers two additional details about bequest of dwelling: first, the preferred method of dividing the usufruct when the house does not exceed the third—physical division into thirds is recommended over muhayah (rotation by time) because it allows simultaneous use. Second, the important principle that the legatee's right to usufruct is personal; it ends upon his death and reverts to the testator's heirs, preventing the usufruct from passing to the legatee's own heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two division methods for dwelling
When the bequest of dwelling is within the third, the text mentions two options: physical division of the house into thirds (each party uses their part simultaneously) or muhayah (rotation by time where one party uses the whole house for a period, then the other).
2
Understand why physical division is preferred
The text says physical division is 'more equitable' because it allows each party to use their portion at the same time, rather than taking turns.
3
Recognize the permissibility of muhayah
If the parties agree, they may opt for muhayah by time, as the right to the usufruct is theirs to divide.
4
Apply the reversion rule upon legatee's death
Upon the death of the legatee, the usufruct returns to the testator's heirs because the legatee's right was personal and temporary; it cannot pass to his own heirs without the testator's consent.

Bequests of Usufruct: Three Hanafi Categories
Distinguishes three categories of usufruct bequests using custom and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a bequest of usufruct into one of three Hanafi categories and apply the correct scope of the bequeathed benefit.

Core Idea
A bequest of 'fruit' includes only existing fruit unless 'forever' is added; 'yield' includes both existing and future by default; wool and milk only include existing.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a critical distinction in bequests of usufruct. The Hanafi school uses customary meanings and analogical reasoning to determine whether future benefits are included. Understanding this three-category system prevents common errors in executing wills and ensures the testator's intent is respected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of usufruct bequeathed
Read the bequest wording: is it fruit (thamara), yield (ghalla), wool (suf), milk (laban), service (khidma), or dwelling (sukna)?
Customary definitions matter; 'yield' implies recurring revenue, 'fruit' typically refers to the current crop.
2
Check for the word 'abada' (forever)
If the testator said 'abada', note it. For fruit, this expands the scope to future harvests. For wool/milk, 'abada' has no effect.
The absence of 'abada' restricts the bequest to existing benefits only in certain cases.
3
Classify the bequest into one of three categories
Refer to al-Zayla'i's classification: (1) includes existing and non-existent always (service, dwelling, yield, fruit when not existing at death), (2) includes only existing always (milk, wool, offspring in womb), (3) includes existing and non-existent only if 'abada' is mentioned (fruit when existing at death).
Category (1) applies when the usufruct is inherently recurring; category (2) when it is a one-time item at death.
4
Apply the corresponding ruling
Based on the category, state what the legatee receives: only existing, both existing and future, or existing plus future if 'abada'.
For fruit existing at death without 'abada', only existing fruit is given.
5
Explain the reasoning
The ruling is based on custom ('urf) for the meaning of terms, and qiyas (analogy) – bequest of future usufruct is valid by analogy to contracts like muzara'ah and mu'amalah which allow future benefits.
Wool and milk are different because they are considered property existing at death and not prone to automatic renewal in the same sense.

Source Text

ولو مات في حياة الموصي بطلت وبثمرة بستانته، فمات، وفيه ثمرة، له هذه الثمرة، فإن زاد "أبدا"، له هذه وما يستقبل كغلة بستانه، وبصوف غنمه ولبنها، له الموجود عند موته قال: "أبدا" أو لا.
ولو مات إلخ : أي لو مات الموصى له قبل موت الموصي بطلت الوصية؛ لأنها تمليك مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت، وفي الحال ملك الموصي ثابت فيه، ولا يتصور تملك الموح له بعد موته فبطلت تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٠/٩] هذه الثمرة: أي إذا أوصى بثمرة بستانه، ثم مات وفيه ثمرة، كان للموصى هذه الثمرة وحدها؛ لأن الثمرة اسم لموجود عرفا، فلا يتناول المعدوم إلا بدلالة زائدة مثل التنصيص على الأبد ؛ إذ لا يتأبد إلا بتناول المعدوم، وإليه أشار بقوله: "فإن زاد أي إن زاد الموصي في وصيته بثمرة بستانه قوله: "أبدا" بأن قال: "له ثمرة بستاني أبدا" كان للموصى له هذه الثمرة فيما يستقبل من ثمرته ما عاش رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٠/٢] (بزيادة) كغلة بستانه : أي كما إذا أوصى بغلة بستانه فله أي للموصى له الغلة القائمة فيه وغلته فيما يستقبل؛ لأن الغلة تنتظم الموجود، وما يكون بعرض الوجود مرة بعد أخرى عرفا، بخلاف الثمرة إذا أطلقت لا تتناول إلا الموجود، فالحاصل أنه إذا أوصى بالغلة استحقه دائما، وبالثمرة لا يستحق إلا القائم إلا إذا زاد "أبدا"، والفرق ما ذكرنا، وإنما قيد بقوله: وفيه مرة ؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن فيه ثمرة، والمسألة بحالها، فهي كمسألة الغلة في تناولها الثمرة المعدومة ما عاش الموصى له رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٠/٢] وبصوف غنمه إلخ : أي إذا أوصى بهذه الأشياء كان له الموجود عند موته، ولا يستحق ما سيحدث بعد موته سواء قال: "أبدا" أو لم يقل؛ لأنه إيجاب عند الموت، فيعتبر وجود هذه الأشياء عنده، لكن جازت الوصية في الغلة المعدومة والثمرة المعدومة على ما بينا؛ لأنها تستحق بغير الوصية من العقود كالمزارعة والمعاملة، فلأن تستحق بالوصية أولى؛ لأنها أوسع بابا من غيرها والحاصل أن مسائل هذا الباب على ثلاثة أوجه: كما في "الزيلعي"، منها ما يقع على الموجود والمعدوم ذكر الأبد أو لم يذكر ، كالوصية بالخدمة والسكنى والغلة والثمرة، ولم تكن موجودة عند موته ومنها ما يقع على الموجود دون المعدوم ذكر الأبد أو لم يذكر، كالوصية باللبن في الضرع، والصوف على الظهر، والولد في البطن، ومنها: ما يقع على الموجود والمعدوم إن ذكر الأبد، وإلا فعلى الموجود فقط، كالوصية بثمرة وفيه ثمرة تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦١/٩] (فتح)
And if he dies during the life of the testator, the bequest is void. And [the bequest] of the fruit of his garden: if he dies and there is fruit in it, he has this fruit. If he adds 'forever', he has this and what will come, like the yield of his garden. And [the bequest] of the wool of his sheep and its milk: he has what is existing at his death, whether he said 'forever' or not. Commentary: 'And if he dies' etc.: i.e., if the legatee dies before the testator, the bequest is void because it is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, and at present the testator's ownership is established in it, and it is not conceivable for the legatee to own it after his death, so it becomes void. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/360. 'This fruit': i.e., if he bequeaths the fruit of his garden, then he dies and there is fruit in it, the legatee has this fruit alone, because 'fruit' is used by custom for existing things, so it does not include non-existent things except with an additional indication, such as explicit mention of 'forever'; because it is not perpetual except by including non-existent things. The author indicated this by his saying: 'If he adds' i.e., if the testator adds in his bequest of the fruit of his garden the word 'forever', saying 'he has the fruit of my garden forever', then the legatee has this fruit and what will come of its fruit as long as he lives. Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 2/490. 'Like the yield of his garden': i.e., just as if he bequeaths the yield of his garden, then he has the existing yield in it and its future yield, because 'yield' comprises the existing and what is prone to come into existence repeatedly by custom, unlike 'fruit' when unrestricted, which only includes the existing. The conclusion is that if he bequeaths the yield, he deserves it perpetually, and if he bequeaths fruit, he only deserves the existing unless he adds 'forever', and the difference is as we mentioned. And he only qualified by saying 'and there is fruit in it' because if there is no fruit, the issue is like the issue of yield in that it includes non-existent fruit as long as the legatee lives. Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 2/490. 'And the wool of his sheep' etc.: i.e., if he bequeaths these things, he has what is existing at his death, and he does not deserve what will come into existence after his death, whether he said 'forever' or not, because it is a bequest at death, so the existence of these things at his death is considered. However, the bequest of non-existent yield and non-existent fruit is valid as we explained, because they are deserved through other contracts like muzara'ah and mu'amalah, so they are more deserving to be deserved through bequest because it is broader in scope than others. The summary is that the issues of this chapter are of three types, as in al-Zayla'i: 1) What includes existing and non-existent whether 'abada' is mentioned or not, like bequest of service, dwelling, yield, and fruit when they are not existing at his death. 2) What includes only existing whether 'abada' is mentioned or not, like bequest of milk in the udder, wool on the back, and offspring in the womb. 3) What includes existing and non-existent if 'abada' is mentioned, otherwise only existing, like bequest of fruit when there is fruit existing. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/361. (Fath)
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage deals with bequests of specific usufructs: fruit of a garden, yield, wool, milk, and offspring. The author first notes that if the legatee dies before the testator, the bequest is void. Then he explains the scope of each bequest. 'Fruit' (thamara) by custom refers only to existing fruit; to include future fruit, the testator must add the word 'abada' (forever). 'Yield' (ghalla) includes both existing and future, because it refers to revenue that recurs. Wool, milk, and offspring are like fruit: only existing at death, even if 'abada' is added, because they are considered existing property at death. The passage concludes with a summary of three categories of bequests of usufruct from Imam al-Zayla'i: (1) those that include existing and future by default (service, dwelling, yield, fruit when not existing at death), (2) those that include only existing always (milk, wool, offspring), and (3) those that include existing and future only if 'abada' is added (fruit when existing at death). This classification helps in determining the extent of the legatee's rights.

Key Terms
ثمرة (thamara): Fruit of a garden; when bequeathed, only existing fruit is included unless 'abada' is added.
غلة (ghalla): Yield or revenue of a garden; includes both existing and future produce by default.
صوف (suf): Wool on the back of sheep; bequest includes only wool existing at death, not future growth.
لبن (laban): Milk in the udder; same ruling as wool – only existing milk at death is bequeathed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person bequeaths 'the fruit of my garden' without saying 'forever', and at his death there is existing fruit, what does the legatee receive?
A) Only the existing fruit.
B) Both existing and future fruit.
C) Nothing, because the garden is not bequeathed.
D) The garden itself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies bequests of usufruct into three categories based on custom and wording; careful drafting of the will is essential to cover intended benefits.

Bequest of a Musta'min: When the One-Third Limit Does Not Apply
Ruling that a musta'min's bequest to a Muslim or dhimmi is valid, even beyond one-third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests by a musta'min, explain why the one-third limit is waived, and identify the minority view requiring heir consent.

Core Idea
A musta'min's bequest beyond one-third is valid because his heirs are legally dead from our perspective.

Islamic law generally limits bequests to one-third of the estate to protect the rights of legal heirs. But what if the testator's heirs are not recognized by Islamic law? The Hanafi school rules on the bequest of a musta'min—a non-Muslim from enemy territory granted temporary protection—illustrates this exception. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and a minority opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and legal act
The subject is a musta'min (ḥarbī with amān). The act is a bequest (waṣiyyah) of all or part of his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi. Determine the default ruling on bequests for comparison.
A musta'min is legally capable of ownership and transfer (tamlik) during his life, e.g., gifts.
2
Understand the normal limit on bequests
In Islamic law, a bequest is generally limited to one-third of the estate; anything beyond requires the consent of the legal heirs. This limit protects heirship rights.
This is based on the ḥadīth: 'Your bequest is one-third, and one-third is plenty.'
3
Analyze why the limit does not apply here
The text gives the reason: 'because his heirs have no recognized right; they are dead in our regard (amwāt fī ḥaqqinā).' The musta'min's heirs are from dār al-ḥarb and have no legal standing in Islamic courts. Since no heir rights exist, the protective limit is superfluous.
This principle applies only when the testator is a non-Muslim from enemy territory; Muslim or dhimmi testators still have protected heirs.
4
Examine the minority opinion
The commentary mentions a second view (‎قيل): 'if she (or they) does not permit, it is not permissible beyond one-third except with their consent.' This suggests that if the musta'min's heirs are present and known, some scholars require their permission for the excess.
The phrase 'إن كانت' may refer to the wife or the heirs collectively; the text leaves it ambiguous.
5
Apply the rule and identify the muftā bihī
The primary, relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is that the bequest is valid without restriction. The minority view is acknowledged but not preferred. Students should be able to apply this rule to similar scenarios.
This ruling from Kanz al-Daqā'iq is from later fatāwā (fatāwā muta'akhkhirīn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوصية حربي مستأمن بكل ماله لمسلم أو ذمي. كوصية حربي إلخ أي صحت هذه الوصية كما تصح وصية حربي مستأمن بكل ماله لمسلم أو ذمي؛ لأنه أهل للتمليك منجزا كالهبة ،ونحوها وكذا مضافا ، ولو أوصى بأكثر من الثلث أو بماله كله جاز؛ لأن امتناع الوصية بما زاد على الثلث لحق الورثة، وليس لورثته حق مراعى؛ لأنهم أموات في حقنا، وقيل: إن كانت لا يجوز بأكثر من الثلث إلا بإجازتهم والله أعلم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٩١/٢]
Like the bequest of a harbī musta'min of all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi. 'Like the bequest of a harbī etc.' meaning: this bequest is valid just as the bequest of a harbī musta'min of all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi is valid; because he is capable of immediate transfer (tamlik) like a gift and similar, and also deferred. And if he bequeaths more than one-third or all his property, it is permissible; because the prohibition of bequest exceeding one-third is for the right of heirs, and his heirs have no recognized right; because they are dead in our regard. And it is said: if she (his wife?) does not permit, it is not permissible beyond one-third except with their consent. And Allah knows best. [From Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:491]
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the bequest of a musta'min (a non-Muslim from enemy territory who has entered Islamic lands with temporary security). The matn states that such a person's bequest of all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi is valid. The commentary explains that the musta'min is legally capable of transferring ownership immediately, like a gift, and similarly for a deferred transfer (bequest). Therefore, even if he bequeaths more than one-third or all his property, it is permissible. The reason is that the one-third limitation in Islamic law is to protect the rights of legal heirs. However, the heirs of a musta'min are not recognized by Islamic law because they are from enemy territory and considered legally dead (amwāt) from our perspective, so no heir-rights exist. However, the text notes a minority view (qīla) that if the bequest exceeds one-third, it requires the consent of those heirs (possibly if they are present or recognized by some accounts). And Allah knows best.

Key Terms
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim from enemy territory (dār al-ḥarb) with no covenant with Muslims.
مستأمن (musta'min): A harbī who has been granted temporary safe passage (amān) into Muslim territory.
أموات في حقنا (amwāt fī ḥaqqinā): Legally dead from our perspective, meaning their rights are not considered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school permit a musta'min to bequeath more than one-third of his property without the consent of his heirs?
A) Because the musta'min is under Muslim protection and his rights are absolute
B) Because the musta'min's heirs have no legal status in Islamic law and are considered dead
C) Because the one-third limit only applies to Muslims
D) Because the bequest is valid only for debts, not gifts

Key Takeaway
The one-third limit on bequests is tied to the existence of protected heirs; where heirs have no legal standing, the limit is removed.

Will of a Dhimmi: No One-Third Limit
Ruling with proof (talil) on dhimmi will exceeding one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi's will exceeding one-third and explain the reasoning (talil) based on the heirs' lack of protected rights.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's will exceeding one-third is valid because his heirs have no protected right under Islamic law.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the will of a dhimmi. The core question: Does the one-third limit apply to non-Muslims? The Hanafi answer is no, based on the rationale that the limit exists to protect Muslim heirs, which does not apply here. Let's examine the proof and the differing opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal act being ruled upon? The will (wasiyyah) of a dhimmi. What is the ruling? The will is valid (ja'iz/sahih) even if it exceeds one-third of the estate or covers all property.
The ruling applies equally to bequests to Muslims or dhimmis.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is an analogy (qiyas) to a harbi musta'min (a non-Muslim with temporary safe passage). Just as a harbi musta'min's will with all his property is valid, so is a dhimmi's.
The common element (illa) is that the heirs have no protected rights in Islamic inheritance law.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: The prohibition of bequeathing more than one-third is for the right of the heirs. For a dhimmi, the heirs are 'dead' in our regard (i.e., not entitled to fixed shares under Islamic law). Therefore, the prohibition does not apply.
This is a talil (rationale) based on the purpose of the rule.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a differing view (qil) that the dhimmi's will is not valid beyond one-third without the heirs' permission. This may be an intra-Hanafi variant or from another school.
The text does not fully rebut this view but implies the first opinion is stronger.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the first: the will is valid without consent. The author presents it as the main ruling and adds 'Wallahu a'lam' (Allah knows best).
The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
أحكام وصية الذمي كوصية حربي مستأمن بكل ماله لمسلم أو ذمي. كوصية حربي إلخ أي صحت هذه الوصية كما تصح وصية حربي مستأمن بكل ماله لمسلم أو ذمي؛ لأنه أهل للتمليك منجزا كالهبة، ونحوها وكذا مضافا، ولو أوصى بأكثر من الثلث أو بماله كله جاز؛ لأن امتناع الوصية بما زاد على الثلث لحق الورثة، وليس لورثته حق مراعى؛ لأنهم أموات في حقنا، وقيل: إن كانت لا يجوز بأكثر من الثلث إلا بإجازتهم والله أعلم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٩١/٢]
ورثته معه
Book of Wills. Rulings of the will of a dhimmi like the will of a harbi musta'min with all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi. 'Like the will of a harbi' etc., meaning: this will is valid just as the will of a harbi musta'min with all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi is valid, because he is capable of transferring ownership immediately like a gift and similar, and likewise when added [to death]. And if he bequeathed more than one-third or all his property, it is permissible because the prohibition of bequeathing beyond one-third is for the right of the heirs, and his heirs have no right to be considered because they are dead in our regard. And it was said: it is not permissible beyond one-third except with their permission. And Allah knows best. Reference from Haqa'iq: 491/2. His heirs with him.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It states that the will of a dhimmi (a non-Muslim under Muslim rule) is exactly like the will of a harbi musta'min (a non-Muslim who enters Muslim lands with temporary security). The ruling covers both immediate transfer (like a gift) and testamentary transfer. The key point is that if the dhimmi bequeaths more than one-third of his property, the bequest is still valid, unlike for a Muslim where it is limited to one-third. The reason given is that the prohibition of bequeathing beyond one-third is to protect the rights of the heirs, but in the case of a dhimmi, his heirs have no protected rights in Islamic law because they are considered 'dead' in our regard (i.e., they are not entitled to the fixed shares under Islamic inheritance law, which applies only to Muslims). Therefore, the bequest is valid even if it exceeds one-third or covers the entire estate. However, there is a differing opinion (attributed to some scholars) that it is not valid beyond one-third without the permission of the heirs. The phrase 'ورثته معه' likely indicates that the heirs are with him (i.e., they exist but are not legally protected). The passage concludes with 'والله أعلم' (Allah knows best).

Key Terms
وصية الذمي (wasiyyat al-dhimmi): The will made by a non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state (dhimmi).
حربي مستأمن (harbi musta'min): A non-Muslim from a hostile territory (harbi) who has been granted temporary safe passage (aman) into Muslim lands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The will is invalid because a dhimmi cannot bequeath more than one-third.
D) The will is valid but only up to one-third, and the rest goes to heirs.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's will exceeding one-third is valid without heirs' permission because Islamic inheritance rights do not protect dhimmi heirs.

Executor's Binding Acceptance and Implied Acceptance by Sale
Rules on when an executor's acceptance or rejection is binding, with comparison to agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an executor's acceptance or rejection is binding and explain why the sale of the estate serves as acceptance by conduct.

Core Idea
An executor's acceptance in the testator's presence is binding; sale of the estate before verbal acceptance is valid as implied acceptance.

This lesson explores the rules governing an executor's (wasi) acceptance and rejection of a testamentary appointment. We examine when the executor's word or deed becomes irrevocable and how the Hanafi school distinguishes the executor from an ordinary agent, particularly regarding the need for knowledge of the appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify scenarios of acceptance and rejection
The matn presents three cases: acceptance/rejection in the testator's presence, rejection without his knowledge, and no response until the testator's death. Determine the ruling for each.
The key distinction is whether the testator relied on the executor's actions.
2
Understand the rationale behind binding acceptance
If the executor accepts in the testator's presence, the testator relies on that and does not appoint another. Permitting later revocation would defraud the testator, hence it is binding.
This reasoning is from the commentary citing Fath and Hidayah.
3
Recognize acceptance by conduct
The matn states that selling the testator's estate is like acceptance. The commentary explains that selling before verbal acceptance is acceptance by indication (qabul dilala), valid even if the executor was unaware of the appointment.
This rule contrasts with agency, where knowledge is required.
4
Distinguish executor from agent
An agent must know of his appointment to act, because agency operates during the principal's authority. Executorship, like inheritance, takes effect from the testator's death, so knowledge is not required.
The analogy is with inheritance: you inherit without needing to know beforehand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصي
أوصى إلى رجل فقبل عنده ورد عنده يرتد، وإلا لا، وبيعه تركته كقبوله، وإن
أي عند الموصي صح
بيع الوصي تركة الموصي بعد موته
الموصي
باب الوصي: لما فرغ من بيان أحكام الموصى له شرع في بيان أحكام الموصى إليه، وهو الوصي، وقدم أحكام الموصى له؛ لكثرتها وكثرة وقوعها، فكانت الحاجة إلى معرفتها أمس تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٧/٩] ورد عنده إلخ لأنه متبرع في ذلك، فإن شاء دام عليه، وإن شاء رجع؛ إذ ليس للموصي ولاية إلزام التصرف على الغير، وليس في الرجوع تغريرا؛ إذ يمكنه أن يوصي إلى غيره، والمراد بقوله: 'قبل عنده ورد علم بالقبول والرد. (فتح بزيادة وإلا لا أي وإن ردها في غير علم الموصي لا يرتد؛ لأنه لما قبل في وجهه اعتمد الموصي على قبوله، فلم يوص إلى غيره، فلو جوزنا رده في حياته أو بعد مماته لصار الميت مغرورا، وذلك باطل، وإن لم يقبل ولم يرد حتى مات الموصي، فهو بالخيار إن شاء قبل، وإن شاء لم يقبل؛ لأن الموصي ليس له ولاية الإلزام، فبقي مخيرا. (فتح، هداية) وبيعه تركته إلخ شرع المؤلف يبين أن القبول تارة يكون باللفظ، وتارة يكون بالفعل، فالقبول بالفعل بأن التركة قبل القبول باللفظ، فهو قبول دلالة، وهو معتبر بالموت وينفذ البيع لصدوره من الوصي، سواء علم بالإيصاء أو لم يعلم بخلاف الوكيل حيث لا يكون وكيلا من غير علم؛ لأن التوكيل إنابة في حال قيام ولاية الموكل ولا يصح من غير علم كإثبات الملك في البيع والشراء، فلابد من العلم، وطريق العلم به أن واحد من أهل التمييز، وقد تقدم بيانه أما الإيصاء فخلافه؛ لأنه مختص بحال انقطاع ولاية الميت، فلا يتوقف على العلم كالوراثة. (تكملة البحر الرائق)
Chapter of the Executor. A man appointed an executor, so he accepted in his presence and rejected in his presence, it is binding; otherwise not. And his sale of his estate is like his acceptance. (Gloss: i.e., in the presence of the testator, it is valid. Sale of the executor of the testator's estate after his death. The testator.) Chapter of the Executor: When he finished explaining the rulings of the legatee, he began explaining the rulings of the one appointed as executor, who is the wasi, and he gave precedence to the rulings of the legatee due to their abundance and frequency of occurrence, so the need to know them was more pressing. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/367) 'He rejected in his presence' etc., because he is volunteering in that, so if he wishes he continues, and if he wishes he withdraws; for the testator has no authority to compel action from others, and there is no deceit in withdrawal since he can appoint another. And what is meant by his saying: 'he accepted in his presence and rejected' is knowledge of acceptance and rejection. (Fath, with addition) 'Otherwise not': meaning if he rejected it without the testator's knowledge, it is not binding; because when he accepted in his face, the testator relied on his acceptance, so he did not appoint another. If we permitted his rejection during his life or after his death, the deceased would be deceived, which is invalid. And if he neither accepted nor rejected until the testator died, he has the choice: if he wishes he accepts, if he wishes he does not accept, because the testator has no authority to compel, so he remains with choice. (Fath, Hidayah) 'And his sale of his estate' etc. The author begins to explain that acceptance is sometimes verbal and sometimes by action. Acceptance by action is that [he sells] the estate before verbal acceptance; it is acceptance by indication, and it is considered after death, and the sale is executed because it emanates from the executor, whether he knew of the appointment or not, unlike the agent (wakil) who is not an agent without knowledge. Because agency is a deputyship during the continuance of the principal's authority and is not valid without knowledge, like establishing ownership in sale and purchase, so knowledge is necessary, and the way to know it is that someone of discernment informs him, and its explanation has preceded. As for executorship, it is different because it is specific to the situation of the cessation of the deceased's authority, so it does not depend on knowledge, like inheritance. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq)
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) from the chapter on the executor (wasi). The matn (base text) states: If a man appoints an executor and the executor accepts or rejects in the presence of the testator, that acceptance or rejection is binding (irredeemable). If he rejects without the testator's knowledge, it is not binding. The sale of the estate by the executor before formal acceptance is considered as acceptance (by conduct). The commentary explains that the executor is a volunteer; he can withdraw any time because the testator cannot compel him. However, if he accepted in the testator's presence, the testator relies on that and may not appoint another, so the executor cannot revoke later, as that would defraud the testator. If the executor neither accepts nor rejects until death, he has the choice after death. The commentary then discusses acceptance by action: selling the estate implies acceptance, valid even if the executor did not know of the appointment beforehand, unlike an agent (wakil) who must know. The reason is that executorship is like inheritance, effective from death, whereas agency requires knowledge during the principal's lifetime.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor appointed by the testator to manage the estate after death.
قبول دلالة (qabul dilala): Acceptance by indication, i.e., conduct that implies acceptance, such as selling the estate.
الوكيل (al-wakil): An agent who acts on behalf of a living principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if an executor rejects the appointment without the testator's knowledge, what is the ruling?
A) The rejection is binding.
B) The rejection is not binding; he can still accept later.
C) The rejection is valid only if witnessed.
D) The testator must confirm the rejection.

Key Takeaway
An executor's acceptance is binding only if the testator relied on it; sale of the estate before formal acceptance counts as implied acceptance, even without knowledge of the appointment.

Late Acceptance by Executor After Initial Refusal
Ruling on executor's late acceptance after refusal, with talil and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an executor's late acceptance after refusal and explain the judge's authority to remove him based on the principle of preventing harm.

Core Idea
An executor's initial refusal does not automatically void his appointment; he may still accept, but the judge may remove him based on valid ijtihad.

When an executor is appointed in a will, he may initially decline. Does that refusal permanently disqualify him? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that mere refusal does not nullify the appointment, yet the judge retains the power to remove the executor if harm is foreseen. We will see how the school balances the testator's interest and the executor's capability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator dies, and the executor says 'I do not accept' then later says 'I accept'. Determine the conditions under which this late acceptance is valid.
Focus on the phrase 'صح إن لم يخرجه قاض' (valid if judge has not removed him).
2
Understand the basis for validity
Why is mere refusal not automatically void? Because voiding would harm the deceased (darar), and the executor's harm is compensated by reward. Repelling harm to the deceased takes priority.
The principle 'الضرر يزال' is implicit.
3
Recognize the judge's role
The judge may remove the executor after refusal, based on Zufar's view that rejection is valid. This is an ijtihad within the school.
Contrast with the majority view that refusal does not nullify.
4
Contrast the two positions
Majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): refusal does not nullify, so executor can accept later. Zufar: refusal is valid and nullifies, so judge may remove.
The commentary treats both as valid ijtihad.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the judge does not remove, the executor can still accept. If the judge removes, later acceptance is invalid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات، فقال: لا أقبل ثم قبل صح إن لم يخرجه قاض من قال: لا أقبل، وإلى عبد
الموصى إليه
الموصي
صح إن لم يخرجه إلخ أي الموصى إليه إن لم يقبل حتى مات الموصي فقال: لا أقبل، ثم قال: أقبل، فله ذلك إن لم يكن القاضي أخرجه من الوصية حين قال لا أقبل؛ لأن مجرد قوله: لا أقبل لا يبطل الإيصاء؛ لأن فيه ضررا بالميت، وضرر الوصي في الإبقاء مجبور بالثواب ودفع الضرر الأول أولى، إلا أن القاضي إذا أخرجه عن ذلك؛ لأنه مجتهد فيه؛ إذ الرد صحيح عند زفر، فكان له إخراجه بعد قوله: لا أقبل، كما أن له الوصية يصح إخراجه بعد قبوله أولا؛ لأنه نصب ناظرا، فإذا رأى غيره أصلح منه كان له عزله، ونصب غيره، وربما يعجز هو ذلك، فيتضرر بالوصية، فيدفع القاضي الضرر، وينصب حافظا لمال الميت متصرفا فيدفع الضرر من الجانبين، ولو قال: أقبل بعد ما أخرجه القاضي، لا يلتفت إليه؛ لأنه قبل بعد ما بطلت الوصية بإخراج القاضي إياه. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧٢/٩] (بزيادة)
And if he died, and he (the executor) said: 'I do not accept,' then he said: 'I accept,' it is valid as long as the judge has not removed him from saying 'I do not accept.' And to (the slave? - gloss: the one appointed executorship, the testator). 'Valid as long as he has not removed him' etc.: meaning the one appointed as executor if he did not accept until the testator died, then he said: 'I do not accept,' then he said: 'I accept,' he has that right as long as the judge has not removed him from the executorship when he said 'I do not accept.' Because mere saying 'I do not accept' does not invalidate the appointment, because there is harm to the deceased. And the harm to the executor in retaining is compensated by reward, and repelling the first harm is more important. Except that if the judge removes him from it, because he exercises ijtihad in that matter; since rejection is valid according to Zufar, so the judge may remove him after he said 'I do not accept,' just as he may remove him after his initial acceptance? Because he appointed him as an overseer; if he sees someone more suitable, he may dismiss him and appoint another. And perhaps he (the executor) is unable to manage, so he suffers from the executorship, so the judge repels the harm and appoints a guardian for the deceased's property to act, thus repelling harm from both sides. And if he says 'I accept' after the judge has removed him, it is not heeded, because he accepted after the executorship was invalidated by the judge's removal. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/372, with addition)
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) addressing a scenario where the executor initially refuses but later accepts. The matn states: If the executor dies (i.e., the testator dies) and the executor says 'I do not accept' and then later says 'I accept', it is valid as long as the judge has not removed him. The commentary explains that mere refusal does not nullify the appointment because that would harm the deceased. The executor's retention is compensated by divine reward, so the harm to the deceased is avoided. However, if the judge removes him after the refusal, this is permissible because there is ijtihad: Zufar holds that rejection is valid, so the judge may remove him. Also, the judge has the authority to dismiss an executor even after acceptance if he finds someone better, just as he can appoint a guardian. If the executor accepts after dismissal, it is not accepted. The passage highlights the principle of preventing harm (darar) and the judge's role as overseer.

Key Terms
إخراج القاضي (ikhraj al-qadi): The judge's removal of the executor from the position of executorship.
ضرر (darar): Harm or injury; the principle of preventing harm is used to justify the executor's retention and the judge's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if an executor says 'I do not accept' after the testator's death, then later changes his mind and says 'I accept', what is the ruling?
A) His acceptance is valid only if the heirs consent.
B) His acceptance is valid as long as the judge has not removed him.
C) His acceptance is never valid after refusal.
D) His acceptance requires a new appointment from the judge.

Key Takeaway
An executor's initial refusal does not automatically void his appointment, but the judge may remove him based on valid ijtihad.
